Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Hierarchy of Ifta in Absence of Early Narration
Procedural rule for mufti when no early riwaya exists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of ifta when no early narration exists, identifying which authority to rely upon at each step.

Core Idea
When early Hanafi texts are silent, the mufti must follow a strict hierarchy: first the early students, then later scholars’ consensus, then majority, and only then cautious ijtihad.

This passage from Al-Hawi al-Qudsi and Al-Khaniyah lays down a procedural rule (rasm) for a mufti encountering a novel issue without explicit narration from the early Hanafi masters. Understanding this hierarchy is essential to avoid reckless fatwa and to maintain the integrity of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
Determine if there is any narration (riwaya) from Abu Hanifa. If none, the mufti does not proceed to ijtihad immediately but follows a defined order.
2
Rank the early students
Take the apparent (zahir) opinion of Abu Yusuf first, then Muhammad, then Zufar, al-Hasan, and so on in descending order of seniority (al-akbar fa al-akbar).
3
Check later scholars' agreement
If no individual early student's apparent answer exists, look for a single agreed opinion among the muta'akhkhirun (later scholars). If consensus, it is binding.
4
Apply majority when later scholars differ
If the later scholars differ, adopt the opinion of the majority, especially those relied upon by well-known seniors like Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, and al-Tahawi.
5
Resort to ijtihad or taqlid
If no textual answer exists at all, the mufti must exert careful ijtihad (if qualified) or, if a muqallid, seek the opinion of the most knowledgeable available scholar, even by correspondence.
Emphasize the severe caution: the mufti must fear Allah and not speak arbitrarily.

Source Text

مطلب
طريق الإفتاء في ما لم توجد فيه الرواية من المتقدمين واختلف المتأخرون أو لم توجد منهم رواية
قال في آخر "الحاوي القدسي" : " ومتى لم يوجد في المسألة عن أبي حنيفة رواية، يؤخذ بظاهر قول أبي يوسف، ثم بظاهر قول محمد، ثم بظاهر قول زفر والحسن ،وغيرهم الأكبر فالأكبر ، هكذا إلى آخر من كان من كبار الأصحاب. وإذا لم يوجد في الحادثة عن واحد منهم جواب ظاهر، وتكلم فيه المشايخ المتأخرون قولا واحدا ، يؤخذ به. فإن اختلفوا يؤخذ بقول الأكثرين مما اعتمد عليه الكبار المعروفون، كأبي حفص وأبي جعفر وأبى الليث والطحاوى وغيرهم، فيعتمد عليه.
وإن لم يوجد منهم جواب البتة نصا، ينظر المفتى فيها نظر تأمل وتدبّر واجتهاد ؛ ليجد فيها ما يقرب إلى الخروج عن العهدة، ولا يتكلم فيها جزافًا ؛ لمنصبه وحرمته، وليخش الله تعالى ويراقبه ؛ فإنه أمر عظيم لا يتجاسر عليه إلا كل جاهل شقى ) . اهـ .
وفى "الخانية" : "وإن كانت المسألة فى غير ظاهر الرواية ، إن كانت توافق أصول أصحابنا يعمل بها . فإن لم يجد لها رواية عن أصحابنا، واتفق فيها المتأخرون على شيء - يعمل به. وإن اختلفوا، يجتهد ويفتي بما هو صواب عنده. وإن كان المفتى مقلدا غير مجتهد يأخذ بقول من هو أفقه الناس عنده، ويضيف الجواب إليه، فإن كان أفقه الناس عنده في مصر آخر، يرجع إليه بالكتاب و يكتب بالجواب، ولا يجازف ؛ خوفًا من الافتراء على الله تعالى بتحريم الحلال وضده . اهـ.
Topic: The way of issuing fatwa in matters where there is no narration from the early scholars, and the later scholars differed or there is no narration from them. He said at the end of Al-Hawi al-Qudsi: "Whenever there is no narration from Abu Hanifa in a matter, the apparent statement of Abu Yusuf is taken, then the apparent statement of Muhammad, then the apparent statement of Zufar and al-Hasan and others, the greater then the greater, up to the last of the senior companions. If there is no apparent answer from any one of them, and the later scholars speak on it with a single opinion, it is taken. If they differ, the opinion of the majority is taken from what the well-known seniors relied upon, such as Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi, and others, and it is relied upon. If there is absolutely no answer from them textually, the mufti looks into it with careful consideration, reflection, and ijtihad to find something that brings him close to discharging his responsibility, and he should not speak arbitrarily due to his position and its sanctity. He should fear Allah and watch Him, for it is a great matter that only every ignorant wretched person dares to undertake." In Al-Khaniyah: "If the matter is not from the apparent narration, if it agrees with the principles of our companions, it is acted upon. If he finds no narration from our companions, and the later scholars agree on something, it is acted upon. If they differ, he exercises ijtihad and gives the ruling he deems correct. If the mufti is a muqallid not a mujtahid, he takes the statement of the person he considers most knowledgeable among people and attributes the answer to him. If the most knowledgeable person in his view is in another city, he refers to him by writing and writes the answer. He should not be reckless, fearing to fabricate against Allah by declaring lawful what is unlawful or vice versa."
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents a procedural rule (rasm) for the mufti when faced with a novel issue (نازلة) for which no explicit narration (رواية) from the early Hanafi masters (أبو حنيفة, أبو يوسف, محمد, etc.) exists. It draws primarily from two later Hanafi juristic texts: Al-Hawi al-Qudsi and Al-Khaniyah. The author first states the title: the method of ifta' when there is no riwaya from the early scholars and the later scholars differ or have no narration. Quoting Al-Hawi al-Qudsi, the priority order is given: start with the apparent (ظاهر) opinion of Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and al-Hasan, then others in descending order of seniority (الأكبر فالأكبر). If no apparent answer exists from any individual, then if the later scholars (مشايخ متأخرون) have a single statement, that is taken. If they differ, the majority opinion (قول الأكثرين) is taken, especially those relied upon by the well-known seniors (كبار معروفون) like Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, and al-Tahawi. If no textual answer exists at all, the mufti must exert careful reflection and ijtihad to find something that allows him to clear his responsibility, avoiding arbitrary speech out of reverence for the office and fear of Allah. Only an ignorant wretched person would dare to give fatwa recklessly. The passage from Al-Khaniyah adds detail: if the issue is from non-apparent narrations (غير ظاهر الرواية), it may be used if it agrees with Hanafi principles. If no narration is found, and the later scholars agree, that agreement is followed. If they differ, the mufti does ijtihad to find what is correct. If the mufti is a muqallid (follower), he must seek the opinion of the most knowledgeable person available, and if that person is in another city, he must correspond in writing. He must not fabricate by declaring halal what is haram or vice versa. The passage emphasizes the gravity of fatwa and the need for caution.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known, transmitted opinions of the early Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, etc.) as collected in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
غير ظاهر الرواية (Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah): Transmissions that are not from the six core books; rare or individual narrations.
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi jurists after the early masters, such as Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Hawi al-Qudsi, what is the mufti's first step when there is no narration from Abu Hanifa?
A) Perform ijtihad independently.
B) Take the apparent opinion of Abu Yusuf.
C) Take the majority opinion of later scholars.
D) Refer to a mufti in another city.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow a clear hierarchical procedure when early texts are silent, prioritizing the earliest and most authoritative opinions before resorting to ijtihad or taqlid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Prohibition of Fatwa by Qawa'id and Nazair Alone
Explains why a mufti cannot rely solely on maxims or analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the reasons why issuing a fatwa based solely on qawa'id or nazair is prohibited in the Hanafi madhhab, and apply the correct procedure for a mufti when faced with a new incident.

Core Idea
Most legal maxims have exceptions; a mufti must know the detailed rulings, not just general principles.

This passage from the 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical methodological point: a mufti cannot rely on general maxims or analogies alone. The Hanafi school, while rich in qawa'id, strictly limits their use to those with deep knowledge of the madhhab's detailed rulings and exceptions. This lesson explores why this restriction exists and what it means for the practice of ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core prohibition
The text states explicitly: 'It is not permissible to issue fatwa by qawa'id nor by nazir.' Recognize that this is a firm rule with limited exceptions.
Exception: 'except in some customary incidents' – but these are rare and require expert judgment.
2
Understand the definition of qa'ida
A qa'ida is a universal ruling applying to many particulars from multiple fiqh chapters. The passage distinguishes it from a dabt (sub-maxim) which applies to only one chapter.
3
Recognize the nature of Hanafi qawa'id
Most fiqhi qawa'id are akthari (majority) not kulli (universal) – they have exceptions (mustathnayat) and restrictions. This is why they cannot be used alone for fatwa.
The text emphasizes: 'most qawa'id are not free from exceptions and restrictions.'
4
Analyze why nazir is insufficient
Two cases may appear similar but have subtle differences only expert jurists perceive. The Hanafi school authored entire books of al-furuq to document these distinctions.
Example from al-Hidayah: trampling wine vs. pig – same action, different zakat ruling due to the nature of the items.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والغالب أن عدم وجدانه النص لقلة اطلاعه، أو عدم معرفته بموضع المسألة المذكورة فيه ؛ إذ قل ما تقع حادثة إلا ولها ذكر في كتب المذهب، إما بعينها أو بذكر قاعدة كلية (٣) تشملها .
(۲) قوله : كما قال من هو أجل منه قدراً " راجع : أول آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى الملحقة بآخر هذا الكتاب ؛ فإن فيه كفاية لذى دراية .
(۱) قوله : " بل من أيد بالوحى صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في الدر المختار: "توقف الإمام في أربع عشرة مسألة ونقل لا أدرى عن الأئمة بل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن جبريل أيضاً. وفي رد المحتار: قوله : (بل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن جبريل أيضا في الكرماني " : "سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أفضل البقاع ، فقال : لا أدرى حتى أسأل جبريل، فسأله فقال : لا أدرى حتى أسأل ربي، فقال عز وجل : خير البقاع المساجد، وخير أهلها أولهم دخولا وآخرهم . خروجاً" . وفى الحقائق : أنه تنبيه لكل مفت أن لا يستنكف من التوقف فيما لا وقوف له عليه ؛ إذ المجازفة افتراء على الله تعالى بتحريم الحلال وضده، كذا في القهستاني". وقال الغزالي في "الإحياء " : وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ما أدرى أعزير نبي أم لا؟ وما أدرى أتبع ملعون أم لا؟ وما أدرى أذو القرنين نبى أم لا؟». (الدر المختار مع رد المحتار: ۸۰۰/۳، ۸۰۱) (۲) قوله : "قاعدة كلية القاعدة في اللغة الأساس، وفي اصطلاح الفقهاء : "حكم کلى ينطبق على جزئيات كثيرة من أبواب متعددة تفهم منه أحكامها" . فقوله : "من أبواب متعددة يخرج الضابط الفقهي، فهو ينبطق على الجزئيات كثيرة من باب واحد كمسائل البيوع مثلا . ثم القاعدة عند الفقهاء غيرها عند النحاة والأصوليين؛ إذ أكثر القواعد الفقهية أكثرى لا كلى ، ولا يخلو أكثرها عن مستثنيات وتقييدات يعتنى الفقهاء بذكرها، ولذلك منعوا عن الإفتاء بها .

الإفتاء بالقواعد والنظير
مطلب
لا يجوز الإفتاء بالقواعد ولا بالنظير
إلا في بعض الحوادث العرفية
ولا يكتفى بوجود نظيرها (۱) مما يقاربها ؛ فإنه لا يأمن أن يكون بين حادثة وما وجده فرق لا يصل إليه فهمه، فكم من مسألة فرقوا بينها وبين نظيرتها (۲)، حتى ألفوا كتب الفروق لذلك، ولو وكل الأمر إلى أفهامنا لم ندرك الفرق بينهما . بل قال العلامة ابن نجيم في "الفوائد الزينية " (۳) : " لا يحل الإفتاء من
(۱) قوله : "نظيرها النظير هو المثل المساوى، جمعه : النظراء، والنظيرة هي المثل والشبه ، جمعه : النظائر والأشباه والنظائر في اصطلاح الفقهاء : المسائل التي يشبه بعضها بعضاً مع اختلافها في الحكم لأمور خفية أدركها الفقهاء بدقة أنظارهم. وذكر العلامة السيوطى الفرق بين المثيل والشبيه والنظير، فقال: "إن المماثلة تقتضى المساواة من كل وجه والمشابهة تقتضى الاشتراك في أكثر الوجوه لا كلها، والمناظرة تكفى فى بعض الوجوه ولو وجها ،واحداً ، يقال : هذا نظير هذا في كذا، وإن خالفه في سائر جهاته " . فعلى هذا المثيل أخص من أخويه، والنظير أعم منهما .
(۲) قوله : فرقوا بينها وبين نظيرتها " كتاب الهداية للإمام المرغيناني مشحون من أمثاله كما لا يخفى على من مارسه ونزودك بشيء منها : قال صاحب الهداية في كتاب الزكاة : " وإن مردمى بخمر أو خنزير عشر الخمر دون الخنزير. ووجه الفرق ... أن القيمة فى ذوات القيم لها حكم العين والخنزير منها . وذوات الأمثال ليس لها هذا الحكم والخمر منها. ولأن حق الأخذ للحماية والمسلم يحمى خمر نفسه للتخليل فكذا يحميها على غيره. ولا يحمى خنزير نفسه بل يجب تسيبه بالإسلام فكذا لا يحمى على غيره . (الهداية : ۱۹۸/۱)
(۳) قوله : "الفوائد الزينية هي كتاب مختصر مشتمل على خمسمائة ضابطة، ألفها صاحب البحر" حين وصوله في شرح الكنز إلى تبييض البيع الفاسد والزينية :
Explanation of the Contract of the Mufti's Drawing. Page 132: The author of al-Bahr is not among the people of ijtihad from the mujtahid Companions and those after them, rather he is among those supported by revelation (may Allah exalt him and grant him peace). And generally, his not finding the text is due to his lack of familiarity, or his lack of knowledge of the location of the mentioned issue in it; for rarely does an incident occur except that it has mention in the books of the madhhab, either explicitly or by mentioning a universal qaida that encompasses it. (2) His statement: 'as said by one greater in rank than him' – refer to the beginning of Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi appended at the end of this book; for in it there is sufficiency for one of understanding. (1) His statement: 'rather he is among those supported by revelation (peace be upon him)' – It is said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'The Imam paused in fourteen issues and transmitted 'I don't know' from the Imams, rather from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and from Jibril as well.' And in Radd al-Muhtar: his statement: 'rather from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and from Jibril also' is in al-Kirmani: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked about the best of places, so he said: I don't know until I ask Jibril. He asked him and he said: I don't know until I ask my Lord. So Allah Almighty said: The best of places are the mosques, and the best of their people are the first to enter and the last to leave.' And in al-Haqa'iq: it is a warning for every mufti not to shy away from pausing on what he has no knowledge of, because rashness is a slander against Allah Almighty by forbidding the lawful and its opposite, as in al-Qahistani. And al-Ghazali said in al-Ihya': The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I do not know whether 'Uzayr is a prophet or not, and I do not know whether Tubba' is cursed or not, and I do not know whether Dhul-Qarnayn is a prophet or not.' (al-Durr al-Mukhtar with Radd al-Muhtar 3:800-801) (2) His statement: 'a universal qaida' – al-qa'ida linguistically means foundation, and in the terminology of the jurists: 'a universal ruling that applies to many particulars from multiple chapters, from which their rulings are understood.' So his statement 'from multiple chapters' excludes the fiqhi dabt (sub-maxim), for it applies to many particulars from one chapter, like the issues of sales for example. Then the qa'ida for the jurists is different from that of the grammarians and usuliyyun; for most fiqhi qawa'id are akthari (majority) not kulli (universal), and most of them are not free from exceptions and restrictions that the jurists take care to mention, and for that reason they prohibited issuing fatwa by them. Page 133: Explanation of the Contract of the Mufti's Drawing. 133. Prohibition of issuing fatwa by qawa'id and nazir. Section: It is not permissible to issue fatwa by qawa'id nor by nazir, except in some customary incidents. And it is not sufficient to have its nazir (analogue) that is close to it; for one cannot be safe from there being a difference between the incident and what he found that his understanding cannot reach. How many a mas'ala they have distinguished between it and its analogue, to the point that they authored books of furuq (differences) for that reason. And if the matter were left to our understandings we would not perceive the difference between them. Rather, Allama Ibn Nujaym said in al-Fawa'id al-Zainiyyah: 'It is not permissible to issue fatwa from (the book).' (1) His statement: 'its nazir' – al-nazir is the equal and equivalent, plural: al-nuzara'; al-nazirah is the similar and resembling, plural: al-naza'ir. Al-ashbah and al-naza'ir in the terminology of the jurists: issues that resemble each other while differing in ruling due to subtle matters that the jurists perceived with the precision of their insights. Allama al-Suyuti mentioned the difference between al-mathil, al-shabih, and al-nazir, saying: 'Al-mumathala requires equality in every aspect, al-mushabaha requires sharing in most aspects not all, and al-munazara suffices in some aspects even if one aspect. It is said: this is nazir of this in such-and-such, even if it differs from it in all other respects.' So on this basis, al-mathil is more specific than its two counterparts, and al-nazir is more general than them. (2) His statement: 'they distinguished between it and its analogue' – The book al-Hidayah by Imam al-Marghinani is full of such examples, as is not hidden from one who has studied it. And we provide you with some of them: The author of al-Hidayah said in the Book of Zakat: 'If someone tramples wine or a pig, the tenth is due for wine but not for the pig. And the face of the difference... is that value in things of value has the ruling of the 'ayn, and the pig is among them. While things of measure do not have this ruling, and wine is among them. And because the right of taking is for protection, and a Muslim protects his wine for making vinegar, so too he protects it against others. But he does not protect his pig; rather it must be set free upon Islam, so too he does not protect it against others.' (al-Hidayah 1:198) (3) His statement: 'al-Fawa'id al-Zainiyyah' – it is a concise book containing five hundred dawat, authored by the author of al-Bahr when he reached in his commentary on al-Kanz to the discussion of whitening the invalid sale. And al-Zainiyyah:
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning the prohibition of issuing fatwas based solely on general legal maxims (qawa'id) or analogous cases (nazair). The text begins by establishing that even the author of al-Bahr (a respected Hanafi scholar) is not on the level of the mujtahid Companions or those after them who were supported by revelation. The point is that a mufti who finds no direct text (nass) from the madhhab should not assume there is none; rather, his inability is due to lack of knowledge or familiarity. Rarely does an incident occur without being mentioned in madhhab books either explicitly or under a universal qaida. Then the text delves into a discussion of qa'ida: definitions and types. It distinguishes a qa'ida (universal ruling applying to many chapters) from a dabt (sub-maxim applying to one chapter). Importantly, most fiqhi qawa'id are akthari (majority) not kulli (universal) and have exceptions; therefore, jurists prohibited issuing fatwa based solely on them. On page 133, the text explicitly states: 'It is not permissible to issue fatwa by qawa'id nor by nazir, except in some customary incidents.' The reason is that relying on an apparent analogy may miss subtle differences that only expert jurists can perceive. The Hanafi school has authored entire books of al-furuq (differences) to highlight such distinctions. An example is given from al-Hidayah: if someone tramples wine or a pig, zakat (tenth) is due on wine but not the pig, because wine is among items of measure (where value is not considered equivalent to the 'ayn) and the Muslim protects his wine for making vinegar, whereas a pig must be set free upon embracing Islam. Thus, despite apparent similarity, the rulings differ. Finally, Ibn Nujaym's al-Fawa'id al-Zainiyyah is mentioned, indicating that even a book of five hundred maxims cannot be used for fatwa by a non-mujtahid. The overarching message is that a mufti must have deep knowledge of the madhhab's specific texts and the subtle distinctions between cases; general principles and analogies are insufficient and dangerous if applied without full comprehension.

Key Terms
قاعدة كلية (qa'ida kulliyya): A universal ruling that applies to many particulars from multiple fiqh chapters, from which their rulings are understood.
نظير (nazir): An equal or similar case; in fiqh, issues that resemble each other but differ in ruling due to subtle distinctions.
ضابط فقهي (dabt fiqhi): A sub-maxim that applies to many particulars from a single fiqh chapter (e.g., sales), as opposed to a qa'ida which spans multiple chapters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to issue a fatwa solely based on a general qa'ida (legal maxim) according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Because qawa'id are not found in the primary sources.
B) Because most qawa'id are akthari (majority) and have exceptions.
C) Because the Prophet prohibited using analogy.
D) Because qawa'id are only for grammar and usul, not fiqh.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must know the specific rulings and exceptions of the madhhab; general maxims and analogies are insufficient and can lead to error.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Prohibition of Issuing Fatwa from Legal Maxims and Analogous Cases
Ruling on the use of legal maxims and analogies in issuing fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a mufti may or may not use qawaid and nazair, and apply the rule of naql sarih when issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must rely on explicit texts, not maxims or analogies, unless for customary incidents.

This passage establishes a fundamental principle of Hanafi fatwa methodology: a mufti below the level of ijtihad cannot derive rulings solely from legal maxims or by analogy to similar cases. The reason is the existence of subtle differences that only mujtahids can perceive. Instead, the mufti must transmit explicit rulings from authoritative sources. An exception is made for customary matters not covered by texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is prohibited? Issuing fatwa from qawaid (legal maxims) and nazair (analogous cases). Exceptions are allowed for customary incidents.
The ruling is from later fatwa works (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
2
Understand the rationale
Why is it prohibited? Because hidden differences may exist between cases that the mufti cannot perceive. Maxims are akthariyya (majority-based), not universal, so they have exceptions.
That is why books of furuq (distinctions) were authored.
3
Note the exception
When is it allowed? For customary incidents (urf) that do not contradict the sacred texts. The mufti may then use maxims or analogies but should state his basis.
The exception is limited to urf, not all novel cases.
4
Apply the rule
What should a mufti do if he lacks an explicit text? He must either refrain from answering (tawaqquf) or ask a more knowledgeable scholar, even in another town.
This applies to non-mujtahid muftis.
5
Recognize the authority hierarchy
The passage relies on Ibn Nujaym (al-Fawaid al-Zayniyyah) and works like al-Khaniyyah and al-Zahiriyyah, representing the later Hanafi fatwa tradition.
These are authoritative sources for muftis today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز الإفتاء بالقواعد ولا بالنظير إلا في بعض الحوادث العرفية ولا يكتفى بوجود نظيرها (۱) مما يقاربها ؛ فإنه لا يأمن أن يكون بين حادثة وما وجده فرق لا يصل إليه فهمه، فكم من مسألة فرقوا بينها وبين نظيرتها (۲)، حتى ألفوا كتب الفروق لذلك، ولو وكل الأمر إلى أفهامنا لم ندرك الفرق بينهما . بل قال العلامة ابن نجيم في "الفوائد الزينية " (۳) : " لا يحل الإفتاء من القواعد والضوابط، وإنما على المفتى حكاية النقل الصريح كما صرحوا به " . اهـ . وقال أيضا : "إن المقرر في الأربعة المذاهب أن قواعد الفقه أكثرية لا كلية ) . انتهى . نقله البيري .
(۱) قوله : "نظيرها النظير هو المثل المساوى، جمعه : النظراء، والنظيرة هي المثل والشبه ، جمعه : النظائر والأشباه والنظائر في اصطلاح الفقهاء : المسائل التي يشبه بعضها بعضاً مع اختلافها في الحكم لأمور خفية أدركها الفقهاء بدقة أنظارهم. وذكر العلامة السيوطى الفرق بين المثيل والشبيه والنظير، فقال: "إن المماثلة تقتضى المساواة من كل وجه والمشابهة تقتضى الاشتراك في أكثر الوجوه لا كلها، والمناظرة تكفى فى بعض الوجوه ولو وجها ،واحداً ، يقال : هذا نظير هذا في كذا، وإن خالفه في سائر جهاته " . فعلى هذا المثيل أخص من أخويه، والنظير أعم منهما .
(۲) قوله : فرقوا بينها وبين نظيرتها " كتاب الهداية للإمام المرغيناني مشحون من أمثاله كما لا يخفى على من مارسه ونزودك بشيء منها : قال صاحب الهداية في كتاب الزكاة : " وإن مردمى بخمر أو خنزير عشر الخمر دون الخنزير. ووجه الفرق ... أن القيمة فى ذوات القيم لها حكم العين والخنزير منها . وذوات الأمثال ليس لها هذا الحكم والخمر منها. ولأن حق الأخذ للحماية والمسلم يحمى خمر نفسه للتخليل فكذا يحميها على غيره. ولا يحمى خنزير نفسه بل يجب تسيبه بالإسلام فكذا لا يحمى على غيره . (الهداية : ۱۹۸/۱)
(۳) قوله : "الفوائد الزينية هي كتاب مختصر مشتمل على خمسمائة ضابطة، ألفها صاحب البحر" حين وصوله في شرح الكنز إلى تبييض البيع الفاسد والزينية : نسبة إلى زين العابدين على ما هو الأصل في النسبة إلى صدر المركب الإضافي، أما البكرى والزبيري في النسبة إلى أبي بكر وابن الزبير فمستثنيان من هذا الأصل، كما تقرر في محله (مظ)
فعلى من لم يجد نقلا صريحًا أن يتوقف في الجواب، أو يسأل من هو أعلم منه ولو في بلدة أخرى، كما يعلم مما نقلناه عن الخـانـيــة " . وفي "الظهيرية " : " وإن لم يكن من أهل الاجتهاد لا يجل له أن يفتى إلا بطريق الحكاية، فيحكى ما يحفظ من أقوال الفقهاء " . اهـ . نعم ! قد توجد حوادث عرفية غير مخالفة للنصوص الشرعية، فيفتى المفتى بها (۲) كما سنذكره آخر المنظومة.
(۱) قوله : "قواعد الفقه أكثرية لا كلية ولذا ترى الفقهاء الذين ألفوا كتب القواعد يذكرون بعد كل قاعدة ما استثنى منها، راجع : الأشباه والنظائر لابن نجيم، الفن الأول، ومقدمة شرح المجلة، المجلد الأول الأول مشتمل على أربع وستين قاعدة ، والثاني على تسع وتسعين قاعدة، ويشتركان فى اثنين وأربعين قاعدة.
(۲) قوله : فيفتى المفتى بها " أي بالقواعد والضوابط ويمكن إرجاع الضمير إلى النظائر . وينبغى للمفتى إذا أفتى بالقواعد أو النظائر أن يصرح بإفتاءه بها؛ لعدم وجدانه النص الصريح والجزئية المتطابقة .
It is not permissible to issue fatwa based on legal maxims (qawaid) nor on analogous cases (nazair), except for some customary incidents. And it is not sufficient to find a similar case (1) that approximates it, because one cannot be sure that there is not a difference between the incident and what he found that his understanding cannot reach. How many cases have they differentiated between them and their analogies (2), until they wrote books on distinctions (al-furuq) for that purpose. If the matter were left to our understandings, we would not grasp the difference between them. Rather, Allamah Ibn Nujaym said in 'al-Fawaid al-Zayniyyah' (3): 'It is not permissible to issue fatwa from maxims and regulations (dawabit). Rather, the mufti must relay explicit transmission, as they have stated.' End quote. He also said: 'It is established in the four schools that fiqh maxims are majority (akthariyyah), not universal (kulliyyah).' End quote. Transmitted by al-Bayri. So whoever does not find an explicit text must refrain from answering or ask someone more knowledgeable than him, even in another town, as is known from what we narrated from al-Khaniyyah. And in al-Zahiriyyah: 'If one is not a jurist capable of ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to issue fatwa except by way of narration; he narrates what he memorizes of the statements of the jurists.' End quote. Yes! There may be customary incidents that do not contradict the legal texts, the mufti may issue fatwa based on them (2) as we will mention at the end of the poem.
(1) His statement: 'its analogy' – an-Nazir is the similar equal, its plural: an-nuzara; an-nazirah is the similar and resemblance, its plural: an-nazair. And ashbah and nazair in the terminology of jurists are cases that resemble each other while differing in ruling due to subtle matters that jurists perceived with the precision of their insights. Allamah al-Suyuti mentioned the difference between mithil, shabih, and nazir, saying: 'Al-mumathalah requires equality in every aspect; al-mushabahah requires sharing in most aspects, not all; al-munazarah suffices in some aspects, even one. It is said: this is nazir of this in such-and-such, even if it differs in all other aspects.' Thus, al-mithil is more specific than its two siblings, and an-nazir is more general than them.
(2) His statement: 'they differentiated between them and their analogies' – The book al-Hidayah by Imam al-Marghinani is full of such examples, as is not hidden from one who studies it. We provide you with some of them: The author of al-Hidayah said in the Book of Zakat: 'If one tramples wine or a pig, he must pay the value ('ushr) of the wine but not of the pig. The face of the difference... is that value in things-of-value has the ruling of the substance, and the pig is among them. But things-of-standard-measure do not have this ruling, and wine is among them. Also because the right to take is for protection, and a Muslim protects his wine for making vinegar, and thus he protects it against others. But he does not protect his pig; rather, he must set it free upon Islam, and thus he does not protect it against others.' (al-Hidayah 1:198)
(3) His statement: 'al-Fawaid al-Zayniyyah' is a brief book containing five hundred regulations (dabt), authored by the author of al-Bahr when he reached the section on 'Tabyid al-Bay' al-Fasid' in his commentary on al-Kanz. Al-Zayniyyah is an attribution to Zayn al-Abidin, as is the rule in attributing to the first part of a compound noun. As for al-Bakri and al-Zubayri, they are exceptions to this rule, as established in its place.
Then: Whoever does not find an explicit text must refrain from answering or ask someone more knowledgeable than him, even in another town, as is known from what we narrated from al-Khaniyyah. And in al-Zahiriyyah: 'If one is not a jurist capable of ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to issue fatwa except by way of narration; he narrates what he memorizes of the statements of the jurists.' End quote. Yes! There may be customary incidents that do not contradict the legal texts, so the mufti may issue fatwa based on them (2) as we will mention at the end of the poem.
(1) His statement: 'Fiqh maxims are majority, not universal.' – Hence you see the jurists who authored books on maxims mention after every maxim what is excepted from it. Refer to al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym, the first chapter, and the introduction to Sharh al-Majallah, the first volume contains sixty-four maxims, the second ninety-nine maxims, and they share forty-two maxims.
(2) His statement: 'so the mufti may issue fatwa based on them' – i.e., based on the maxims and regulations; it is also possible to refer the pronoun back to the analogies. And it is appropriate for the mufti when he issues a fatwa based on maxims or analogies to explicitly state that he is issuing fatwa by them due to not finding an explicit text and a perfectly matching specific case.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling concerning the permissibility of issuing fatwa using legal maxims (qawaid) and analogous cases (nazair). The author begins by stating the general prohibition: a mufti may not derive a ruling solely from a maxim or by analogy to a similar case. The reason given is that subtle differences may exist between cases that the mufti’s understanding cannot perceive, as evidenced by entire books (like al-Furuq) dedicated to distinguishing apparently similar cases. The author then quotes Ibn Nujaym’s al-Fawaid al-Zayniyyah, where he asserts that issuing fatwa from maxims and regulations (dawabit) is not permissible; rather, the mufti must rely on explicit transmitted texts (naql sarih). Ibn Nujaym also states that fiqh maxims are ‘akthariyya’ (majority, not universal), meaning they have exceptions, which is why every maxim is taught with its exceptions. This makes maxims unreliable as sole bases for fatwa. For the mufti who cannot find an explicit text, the options are to refrain from answering (tawaqquf) or to consult a more knowledgeable scholar, even in another town. If the mufti is not a mujtahid, he may only narrate the rulings he remembers from earlier jurists. An exception is made for customary incidents (‘urfiyya) that do not contradict the sacred texts; in such cases, the mufti may issue fatwa using maxims or analogies, but he should clearly state that he is doing so due to the lack of a direct text. The footnotes provide definitions of nazir, examples of subtle distinctions from al-Hidayah, context on al-Fawaid al-Zayniyyah, and further explanation of the nature of qawaid. The ruling is from the later fatwa works (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin) as it cites Ibn Nujaym and others.

Key Terms
القواعد (al-qawaid): Legal maxims that are majority-based (akthariyya), not universal; cannot be used alone for fatwa.
النظير (an-nazir): A similar case that shares some aspects but not all; differs in ruling due to subtle distinctions.
النقل الصريح (an-naql as-sarih): An explicit transmitted ruling from authoritative Hanafi sources, necessary for issuing fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should a mufti do if he cannot find an explicit transmitted text (naql sarih) for a given incident?
A) Issue a fatwa based on a similar case (nazir) if one is found.
B) Refrain from answering or ask a more knowledgeable scholar.
C) Apply a general legal maxim (qaidah) that seems relevant.
D) Use qiyas jali (obvious analogy) without textual evidence.

Key Takeaway
A mufti below the level of ijtihad may only issue fatwa based on explicit transmitted texts; legal maxims and analogous cases are not sufficient, except for customary incidents where no text contradicts.

The Mufti's Rule for Ibadat: Imam Abu Hanifa's Opinion is Primary
A poem establishing a mufti's rule for preferred opinion in worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule from Rasm al-Mufti that in ibadat, the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is preponderant unless a sound riwaya from the Sahibayn is taken, and distinguish this from the rule in mu'amalat.

Core Idea
In all acts of worship, the Imam's opinion rules—unless a sound riwaya from the disciples is followed.

The mufti often faces differences between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. This poem from Rasm al-Mufti provides a clear rule for ibadat: the Imam's view is paramount. However, there is an exception for a sound narration (sahih riwaya) from the Sahibayn. This memorization anchor guides the mufti in choosing the operative position within the Hanafi school for worship matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of the rule
The poem states 'fi kulli abwab al-ibadat' – note that the rule is specific to chapters of worship, not all of fiqh.
This distinction is critical; different rules govern mu'amalat.
2
State the default hierarchy
The Imam's opinion (qawl al-Imam) is preponderant (rajih) absolutely (mutlaqan) in ibadat.
This means the mufti defaults to Abu Hanifa's view.
3
Recognize the exception
The phrase 'ma lam tassih riwayatun biha al-ghair akhadh' – unless a sound transmission from the two disciples is taken.
The exception requires a sahih riwaya; not any narration.
4
Understand the example
The poet gives 'tayammum for one who threw away dates' – a specific case illustrating the rule.
This example reminds the mufti of the practical application.
5
Distinguish from mu'amalat
In transactions, custom ('urf) and other factors may give precedence to the Sahibayn.
The rule here is exclusive to ibadat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٠ - وَهَهُنَا ضَوَابِطُ مُحَرَّرَة (۳) غَدَتْ لَدَى أَهْلِ النَّهَى مُقَرَّرَة (٤) ٤١ - فِي كُلِّ أَبْوَابِ العِبَادَاتِ رُجُحْ قَوْلُ الإِمَامِ مُطْلَقًا مَا لَمْ تَصِحَّ رِوَايَةٌ بِهَا الغَير أَخَذْ ٤٢- عنه مِثْلُ تَيَمَّ لِمَنْ تَمْرًا نَبَدْ
(۳) قوله : ضوابط محررة " أى قواعد منقحة ومهذبة. (مظ)
(٤) قوله : غدت لدى . . . " أي صارت عند العقلاء ثابتة . (مظ)
40 - And here are refined regulations (dawabit) (3) that have become established among people of intellect (4).
41 - In all chapters of worship, the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is deemed preponderant absolutely, unless there is a sound narration (riwayah) by which the other (two, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is taken.
42 - About him, like tayammum for one who threw away dates.
(3) His statement: 'refined regulations' – i.e., rules that are corrected and refined. (Muzhir)
(4) His statement: 'became among...' – i.e., they became established with the rational people. (Muzhir)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage contains two couplets from the poem (manzuma) of Rasm al-Mufti, followed by brief explanatory footnotes. The passage sets forth a rasm rule for the mufti in the area of ibadat (acts of worship) when there is disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The rule states that in all chapters of ibadat, the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is given precedence (rajih) absolutely, unless there is a sound transmission (sahih riwaya) from the Sahibayn that the mufti chooses to follow. The example given is the case of tayammum for one who threw away dates (a reference to a specific mas'ala). The footnotes clarify that 'dawabit muharrara' means corrected and refined rules, and 'ghadat' indicates they have become established among the intelligent. This rule is specific to ibadat; in mu'amalat, the precedence may differ. It is a memorization anchor for the mufti to know which opinion to give in case of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الضوابط المحررة (ad-dawabit al-muharrara): Corrected and refined regulations that serve as rules for the mufti.
قول الإمام (qawl al-Imam): The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, given precedence in ibadat unless a sahih riwaya from the Sahibayn is taken.
رجح (rajih): Preponderant; the opinion that is given weight over others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this poem, what is the mufti's approach in ibadat when Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples differ?
A) The mufti must always follow the opinion of Abu Yusuf.
B) The mufti gives precedence to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion unless a sound riwaya from the disciples is adopted.
C) The mufti must adopt the opinion of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
D) The mufti may choose any opinion based on ease.

Key Takeaway
In ibadat, the mufti must give precedence to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion unless a sound narration from his disciples is adopted.

The Akthariyya Principle: Fiqh Rules Are Majority-Based, Not Absolute
Rasm al-mufti rule: akthariyya of qawa'id and mufti's duty to transmit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule that fiqh rules are akthariyya by identifying when a mufti must stop (tawaqquf) and seek an explicit transmitted ruling rather than deriving from a general maxim.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti cannot derive fatwa from a general maxim alone; he must cite an explicit transmitted ruling from the school.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational rasm al-mufti principle: fiqh rules (qawa'id) are not universal but apply to the majority of cases. This means a mufti cannot automatically apply a maxim to a new case; he must first check for an explicit transmitted ruling. If none exists, he must stop (tawaqquf) or consult a more learned scholar. This passage from a standard manual clarifies the boundaries of fatwa based on rules and the priority of naql sarih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Locate the key statement: 'qawa'id al-fiqh akthariyya la kulliyya' (fiqh rules are majority-based not absolute). This is the core claim of the passage. Understand its meaning: it acknowledges exceptions and prevents universal application.
The term 'akthariyya' is a hallmark of Hanafi usul al-iftā'.
2
Extract the Consequence
The passage then states what a mufti must do: if he does not find an explicit transmission (naql sarih), he must either refrain from answering (tawaqquf) or ask someone more knowledgeable, even if in another town. This is the direct operational implication of the akthariyya principle.
Sources cited: al-Khāniyyah and al-Ẓahīriyyah.
3
Note the Exception
The passage adds that customary incidents (ʿurf) that do not contradict the sacred texts may be used for fatwa, but this is deferred to later in the poem. This shows that the general rule (tawaqquf) has a limited exception.
This exception will be detailed later; for now, focus on the primary obligation.
4
Apply the Rule in Practice
Imagine a mufti encounters a case not explicitly covered by a transmitted text. According to this passage, he must not derive a ruling from a maxim like 'al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā' alone. He must either find a transmitted text or stop/consult.
This prevents subjective ijtihād from non-mujtahids.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإفتاء بالقواعد والنظير
القواعد والضوابط، وإنما على المفتى حكاية النقل الصريح كما صرحوا به " . اهـ . وقال أيضا : "إن المقرر في الأربعة المذاهب أن قواعد الفقه أكثرية لا كلية ) . انتهى . نقله البيري .
(1):
فعلى من لم يجد نقلا صريحًا أن يتوقف في الجواب، أو يسأل من هو أعلم منه ولو في بلدة أخرى، كما يعلم مما نقلناه عن الخـانـيــة " . وفي "الظهيرية " : " وإن لم يكن من أهل الاجتهاد لا يجل له أن يفتى إلا بطريق الحكاية، فيحكى ما يحفظ من أقوال الفقهاء " . اهـ . نعم ! قد توجد حوادث عرفية غير مخالفة للنصوص الشرعية، فيفتى المفتى بها (٢) كما سنذكره آخر
المنظومة.
Issuing fatwa based on maxims and analogies. The maxims and rules. Rather, the mufti is merely to narrate an explicit transmission, as they have stated. He also said: 'It is established in the four schools that fiqh rules are majority-based not absolute.' End quote. Narrated by al-Biri. (1): So whoever does not find an explicit transmission must refrain from answering, or ask someone more knowledgeable than him even if in another town, as is known from what we have narrated from al-Khaniyya. And in al-Zahiriyya: 'If he is not a person of ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa except by way of narration, so he narrates what he has memorized of the statements of the jurists.' End quote. Yes! There may occur customary incidents that do not contradict the legal texts, then the mufti issues fatwa based on them, as we will mention at the end of the poem.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule establishing two fundamental constraints on fatwa: first, that fiqh rules are not universal but majority-based (akthariyya), meaning they admit exceptions. Therefore, a mufti cannot rely on a general maxim alone but must cite an explicit transmitted ruling. Second, if no explicit ruling is found, the mufti must stop (tawaqquf) or consult a more learned scholar. This is taken from the Hanafi works al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya. An exception is recognized for customary matters (urf) that do not contradict texts, where the mufti may use his own reasoning, but this is deferred to later in the poem.

Key Terms
قواعد الفقه (qawa'id al-fiqh): Legal maxims distilled from multiple rulings; not universal but akthariyya (majority).
حكاية النقل الصريح (hikayat al-naql al-sarih): Narrating an explicit textual ruling from a recognized authority.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Refraining from issuing a fatwa when no explicit ruling is known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a mufti do if he cannot find an explicit transmitted ruling?
A) He may derive a ruling using general maxims.
B) He must stop answering or ask a more learned scholar.
C) He must refer to customary practice.
D) He may issue a fatwa based on his own ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh rules are majority-based (akthariyya); a mufti without explicit transmitted ruling must stop or consult—not derive from maxims.

The Nine Rules of Tarjih for the Hanafi Mufti
Nine poetic rules for preferring one Hanafi opinion over another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state each of the nine rules of tarjih and apply them to determine which opinion is preponderant in a given Hanafi fatwa scenario.

Core Idea
Nine precise rules guide a Hanafi mufti to choose the strongest opinion when faced with conflicting rulings.

A Hanafi mufti will often encounter multiple opinions on a single issue, whether from the three main imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) or from later scholars. To navigate this, the later masters distilled nine clear rules of preference (tarjih). These rules, memorized in poetic form, cover specific domains (worship, judicial matters, distant kindred) as well as general principles like preferring the explicit text, the sound narration, and the older source. Mastering them is essential for issuing consistent, authoritative fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the domain of the ruling
Determine whether the case falls under 'ibadat (worship), qada (judicial), dhawi al-arham (inheritance of distant kindred), or other. The first three rules are domain-specific.
Rule 1 (Imam's say in 'ibadat), Rule 2 (Abu Yusuf in qada), Rule 3 (Muhammad in dhawi al-arham).
2
Check for a sound narration or explicit text
If a sound narration (riwaya) supports the non-Imam position in 'ibadat, it overrides rule 1. Also, the apparent meaning of transmitted texts (zahir al-marwi) must not be abandoned.
Rules 4 and 6 deal with zahir and sound narratives.
3
Apply the general preference rules
Consider istihsan over qiyas (rule 5), diraya supported by riwaya (rule 7), saying that negates kufr (rule 8), retracted opinion (rule 9), and implicit tarjih from being in the mutun (rule 10).
These are the remaining general rules.
4
Apply the chronological hierarchy
Prefer older texts over commentaries, and commentaries over later fatwas. Also prefer an explicitly stated wording over a merely sound one.
Rules 11 and 12 (verse 51-52) establish the hierarchy of sources.
5
Compile the result and issue the fatwa
After applying all relevant rules, determine the preponderant opinion. If rules conflict, prioritize domain-specific rules first, then general principles, then hierarchy.
The mufta bihi is the opinion that emerges from this process.

40 - And here are refined rules, which have become established among people of intellect. 41 - In all chapters of worship, the saying of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is preponderant absolutely, unless a narration is sound by which the other is taken, like tayammum for one who has thrown away dates. 42 - 'anhu (relating to Zain al-Abidin as is the rule of attribution to the first part of a possessive compound; except Bakri and Zubairi in attribution to Abu Bakr and Ibn al-Zubair, they are excluded from this principle, as established in its place. (1) His saying: 'Fiqh rules are majority-based not absolute; thus you see jurists who authored books on rules mention after every rule what is excepted from it. Refer: al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym, the first art, and the introduction to Sharh al-Majalla, the first volume includes sixty-four rules, the second includes ninety-nine rules, and they share forty-two rules. (2) His saying: 'the mufti issues fatwa based on them' i.e., based on the rules and controls; the pronoun may refer to analogies. And it is proper for the mufti, when he issues a fatwa based on rules or analogies, to explicitly state that he is issuing fatwa by them due to not finding an explicit text and a matching specific case. (3) His saying: 'refined rules' i.e., polished and corrected rules. (4) His saying: 'became among the people of intellect' i.e., became established with the rational people. [PAGE_135] Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti - And every branch related to qada (judicial matters), the saying of Abu Yusuf therein is selected. 44 - And in matters of dhawi al-arham, they have given fatwa according to what Muhammad says. 45 - And they gave preference to their istihsan over qiyas, except for matters in which there is no confusion. 46 - And the apparent (zahir) of what is narrated is not to be deviated from to its opposite, if it is transmitted. 47 - It is not proper to deviate from a learned (diraya) opinion when its narration matches it. 48 - And every saying that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is chosen. 49 - And every saying from which the mujtahid retracted becomes like abrogated, so other than it is relied upon. 50 - And every saying established in the mutun (core texts) is an implicit tarjih for it. 51 - So the old (procedural) texts are given preponderance over commentaries, and commentaries over later fatwas, among those having preponderance. 52 - As long as the other is not established as a sound expression; the most preponderant is the one that is explicitly stated. A request regarding the nine rules of tarjih between different opinions: In these verses are collected rules that they have mentioned scattered in the books, and they made them a sign for the preponderant among opinions. (1) His saying: 'except for matters in which there is no confusion' – 'ma' is negative, meaning except matters in which there is no ambiguity because they are specific, and they are twenty-two as will come. (2) His saying: 'the old fatwas of preponderant nature' i.e., the older preponderant fatwas. (3) His saying: 'on the preponderant of opinions' – know that rules of tarjih are of two types: a type by which tarjih is made between opinions, and a type by which tarjih is made between corrections of opinions. The first is nine, the second is ten. Then the second type is general, useful for tarjih between different opinions as well as between conflicting corrections, and the first type is specific, by which tarjih is made only between different opinions. And it will come that five of them are common between the two types: being the saying of the Imam, or of Zahir al-Riwaya, or in the mutun.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage contains a set of poetic verses (40-52) that encapsulate the nine rules of tarjih (preference) for a Hanafi mufti when faced with differing opinions. The passage is a rasm al-mufti rule. It begins by stating that these rules are refined and established. The first rule (verse 41) gives precedence to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying in all matters of worship ('ibadat) unless there is a sound narration taking the other view, illustrated by a case of tayammum. Then verse 43 gives precedence to Abu Yusuf in qada-related branches. Verse 44 gives precedence to Muhammad in matters of dhawi al-arham (distant kindred). Verse 45 prefers istihsan over qiyas except twenty-two excluded cases. Verse 46 holds that the apparent meaning of transmitted texts must not be abandoned. Verse 47 says not to abandon a diraya (learned opinion) if supported by a narration. Verse 48 gives weight to any saying that negates disbelief from a Muslim. Verse 49 treats a retracted opinion like abrogated. Verse 50 considers a ruling in the mutun as implicit tarjih. Verse 51 ranks sources: old texts over commentaries, commentaries over fatwas. Verse 52 favors an explicitly stated wording over a merely sound one. The commentary at the end clarifies that these nine rules are for tarjih between different opinions, while there are ten for tarjih between corrections, with five common to both.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The apparent meaning of the transmitted narration from the six major works.
القول القديم (al-qawl al-qadim): The older version of the text or fatwa, given precedence over newer commentaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to verse 48, which kind of saying is given preference?
A) A saying that is most widely transmitted.
B) A saying that negates disbelief from a Muslim.
C) A saying from a later scholar.
D) A saying based on istihsan.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti must memorize and apply these nine tarjih rules to consistently select the preponderant opinion when multiple views exist.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

First Rule of Tarjih: Fatwa in 'Ibadat Defaults to Imam Abu Hanifa
Defining the first rule of preference for fatwa in worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first rule of tarjih to identify when fatwa defaults to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying and when it shifts to another view in acts of worship.

Core Idea
In 'ibadat, fatwa defaults to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying; exceptions occur only when scholars explicitly rule otherwise or necessity demands.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule of preference (tarjih) for fatwa in the Hanafi school: in matters of 'ibadat (acts of worship), the mufti should give fatwa based on the saying (qawl) of Imam Abu Hanifa, unless the later scholars have explicitly stated that fatwa is on another view. The rule is grounded in the Imam's deep insight and the school's inductive practice. We will explore its justification, the two illustrative examples of used water and nabidh, and the conditions for departing from the Imam's view.

Guided Path
1
State the rule and its scope
The rule: 'Fatwa is given in 'ibadat according to the saying of the Imam, unless they explicitly state contrary to it.' 'Ibadat here refers to acts like prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj, etc., not mu'amalat.
Rule applies specifically to 'ibadat; mu'amalat have different tarjih rules.
2
Understand the rationale
Scholars derived this by induction (istiqra') from the Imam's precision and the devotional nature (ta'abbud) of 'ibadat. The commentator praises the Imam's insight.
The rule is not arbitrary but based on the school's cumulative practice.
3
Identify exceptions
Departure occurs when (a) the Imam himself has a narration supporting the opponent's view (even if weak), or (b) scholars explicitly state fatwa is on another view, often due to necessity like 'umum al-balwa.
Exception is not a free choice; it must be justified.
4
Apply to examples
Used water: default Imam's view (najis), but fatwa is on Muhammad's view (tahir not tahur) due to widespread need. Nabidh: default Imam's view (wudu allowed), but fatwa on Abu Yusuf's view (tayammum) as the corrected madhhab.
Both examples show departure when later scholars explicitly adopt another view.
5
Memorize the rule and caveats
The rule is memorized with condition: 'as long as there is not from him a narration like the saying of the opponent.' Keep the examples in mind.
This ensures the rule is applied correctly, not mechanically.

Source Text

جمعت في هذه الأبيات قواعد ذكروها مفرقة في الكتب، وجعلوها علامة على المرجح من الأقوال (۱). (۱) قوله : "على المجح من الأقوال اعلم أن قواعد الترجيح على نوعين : نوع يرجح به بين الأقوال، ونوع يرجح به بين تصحيحات الأقوال، الأول تسعة والثاني عشرة . ثم النوع الثاني عام يفيد الترجيح بين الأقوال المختلفة، كما يفيد بين التصحيحات المتعارضة، والنوع الأول ،خاص لا يرجح به إلا بين الأقوال المختلفة. وسيأتي أن خمسة منها مشتركة بين النوعين وهى : كونه قول الإمام أو ظاهر الرواية أو فى المتون
القاعدة الأولى: يفتى فى العبادات بقول الإمام إلا إذا صرحوا بخلافه
الأولى : ما في شرح المنية " للبرهان إبراهيم الحلبي من فصل التيمم حيث قال : " فلله در الإمام الأعظم ما أدق نظره ! وما أسد فكره ! ولأمر ما جعل العلماء الفتوى على قوله في العبادات مطلقا، وهو الواقع بالاستقراء ما لم يكن عنه رواية كقول المخالف (۱) ، كما فى طهارة الماء المستعمل (۲) ، والتيمم فقط عند عدم غير نبيذ التمر " . أو الأقوى حجة أو استحسانًا في مقابلة القياس، فليحفظ
(۱) قوله: "ما لم يكن عنه رواية كقول المخالف " أى لا يفتي على قول غيره في العبادات إلا إذا وافقه رواية منه ولو كانت غير مشهورة، فيكون الفتوى حينئذ على قوله أيضاً، وإنما تترك روايته المشهورة لضعف الدليل أو لضرورة ونحوها .
(۲) قوله كما في طهارة الماء المستعمل " وكما في الماء التي وقعت فيه نجاسة ولا يدري متى وقعت راجع الهداية : ٤٣/١، ٤٤ والدر المختار : ١٤٥/١، ١٤٦ . وحكم الماء المستعمل مختلف فيه :
قال محمد - وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة - هو طاهر غير طهور، وقال أبو حنيفة وأبويوسف هو نجس، قالوا : وقول محمد هو المختار للفتوى لعموم البلوى . وكذلك التوضى بنبيذ التمر إن لم يجد غيره، قال أبو حنيفة : يتوضأ ولا يتيم، وقال أبو يوسف : يتيمم ولا يتوضأ به، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة وبه قال الأئمة الثلاثة، وقال محمد يتوضأ به ويتيمم . وقول أبي يوسف هو المذهب المصحح المختار المعتمد المفتى به عندنا ملخصاً من الهداية : ۳۸/۱، ورد المحتار : ۱/ ۲۲۷
A request concerning the nine rules of preference between different sayings. Collected in these verses are rules that they mentioned scattered in the books, and they made them a mark for the preponderant from the sayings. (1) His saying: 'on the preferred from the sayings know that the rules of preference are of two types: a type by which preference is made between sayings, and a type by which preference is made between corrections of sayings. The first are nine and the second are ten. Then the second type is general, benefitting preference between different sayings just as it benefits between conflicting corrections, and the first type is specific, not giving preference except between different sayings. It will come that five of them are common between the two types: being the saying of the Imam, or the apparent of the transmitted report, or in the texts.
The first rule: Fatwa is given in acts of worship according to the saying of the Imam, unless they explicitly state contrary to it.
The first: What is in Sharh al-Munya of Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi from the chapter of tayammum where he said: 'By Allah, what a great Imam! How precise his view! How sound his thought! For some reason, the scholars made fatwa on his saying in acts of worship absolutely, and it is established by induction, as long as there is not from him a narration like the saying of the opponent (1), as in the purity of used water (2), and tayammum only when there is no other than date nabidh.' Or the strongest proof or istihsan in the face of qiyas, so memorize.
(1) His saying: 'as long as there is not from him a narration like the saying of the opponent' means: fatwa is not given on the saying of another in acts of worship unless it agrees with a narration from him even if it is not well-known, then the fatwa at that time is also on his saying, and his well-known narration is left only due to weakness of evidence or necessity and the like.
(2) His saying: 'as in the purity of used water' and as in water in which impurity fell and it is not known when it fell. Refer to al-Hidayah 1/43, 44 and al-Durr al-Mukhtar 1/145, 146. The ruling of used water is differed: Muhammad said – and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa – it is tahir (pure) not tahur (purifying), and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said it is najis (impure). They said: the saying of Muhammad is chosen for fatwa due to general need. And likewise, wudu with date nabidh if he does not find other water: Abu Hanifa said: he makes wudu and does not do tayammum; Abu Yusuf said: he does tayammum and does not make wudu with it, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa and the three Imams said the same; Muhammad said: he makes wudu with it and also does tayammum. The saying of Abu Yusuf is the corrected, chosen, relied-upon, and fatwa-given madhhab according to us, summarized from al-Hidayah 1/38 and Radd al-Muhtar 1/227.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage explains the first rule of tarjih: In acts of worship ('ibādāt), the default position is to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying (qawl al-Imām), unless the scholars have explicitly stated otherwise. The commentary begins by introducing the nine rules of preference (tarjīḥ) between different transmitted sayings, noting that there are two categories: rules that prefer between sayings, and rules that prefer between corrections of sayings. Five rules are common to both, including the saying being from the Imam, from the apparent of the transmitted report, or being in the canonical texts. The first rule is then elaborated using a quote from Sharḥ al-Munyah by Burhān Ibrāhīm al-Ḥalabī, who praises Imam Abu Hanifa's precision and states that scholars have consistently based fatwa on his view in 'ibādāt by induction (istiqrā'), except when there is a more reliable narration from him that aligns with the opponent's view. Two examples are given: (1) the purity of water used in wudu (mā' musta'mal) – the well-known narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf says it is najis, but due to widespread need, the fatwa is on Muhammad's view that it is tahir but not tahur. (2) Wudu with date nabidh when water is unavailable – although Abu Hanifa allowed wudu with it, the corrected fatwa is Abu Yusuf's view that one must do tayammum instead. The passage emphasizes that departure from Imam Abu Hanifa's famous view is only for weak evidence or necessity, not as a default.

Key Terms
الْعِبَادَاتُ (al-ʿibādāt): Acts of worship in the narrow sense: prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj, etc., not including transactions.
قَوْلُ الْإِمَامِ (qawl al-imām): The juristic opinion of Abu Hanifa, the founder of the school.
رِوَايَةٌ (riwāyah): A transmitted narration from the Imam, whether well-known (mashhūrah) or rare (shādhdhah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first rule of tarjih, when may the mufti depart from Imam Abu Hanifa's saying in 'ibadat?
A) Whenever he prefers the view of Abu Yusuf
B) Only if the scholars have explicitly stated a contrary fatwa
C) When the opposing view is based on qiyas
D) Never, because Imam's view is always binding

Key Takeaway
In acts of worship, the fatwa defaults to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying unless later scholars have explicitly adopted another view or necessity requires departure.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The First Rule of Preference: Following Abu Hanifa in Acts of Worship
First rule of preference: follow Abu Hanifa in 'ibadat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first rule of tarjih in 'ibadat: identify when to follow Abu Hanifa's statement and when to depart based on explicit later rulings.

Core Idea
Fatwa in 'ibadat follows Abu Hanifa unless later scholars explicitly rule otherwise.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule of preference (tarjih) within the Hanafi school: in matters of worship, the fatwa is given according to Imam Abu Hanifa unless the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) explicitly state a contrary position. The ruling is derived from induction (istiqra) of the school's practice and is illustrated by examples like used water and tayammum with date nabidh. Understanding this rule is crucial for a mufti to give correct fatwas in 'ibadat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act as 'ibadah or mu'amalah
Determine if the fiqh issue is an act of worship (prayer, fasting, etc.) or a transaction (sales, marriage, etc.). The rule applies only to 'ibadat.
2
Locate the default ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa
Find the well-known position of Abu Hanifa on the issue from the zahir al-riwayah texts.
3
Check for an explicit later contrary ruling
Search the fatawa muta'akhkhirin texts (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Radd al-Muhtar) for a statement that 'the fatwa is on the view of so-and-so' or similar.
The exception clause 'إلا إذا صرحوا بخلافه' means a clear statement of preference by later scholars.
4
Apply the exception: follow the later ruling if based on stronger evidence or necessity
If later scholars have explicitly chosen a different view due to a stronger dalil or public need (like the used water case), then that view becomes mufta bihi.
Example: used water – Abu Hanifa said it is impure, but later scholars adopted Muhammad's view due to general need.
5
Practice with examples from the text
Test the rule on the used water and date nabidh cases given in the commentary. Determine the mufta bihi for each.

Fatwa is given according to the statement of the Imam in acts of worship unless they explicitly state otherwise.

First: What is in Sharh al-Munyah by Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi from the section on Tayammum, where he said: "So excellent is the Great Imam! How precise his view! How sound his thought! And for a reason the scholars fatwa is given according to his statement in acts of worship absolutely, and that is what is found by induction, as long as there is no narration from him like the statement of the opponent (1), as in the purity of used water (2), and tayammum only when there is no other than date nabidh."
Or the stronger in proof or istihsan in opposition to qiyas, so let it be memorized.

(1) His saying: "as long as there is no narration from him like the statement of the opponent" means: one does not give fatwa on the statement of someone else in acts of worship unless it is in agreement with a narration from him, even if it is not well-known. Then fatwa is on his statement as well. His well-known narration is only left due to weakness of evidence or necessity and the like.
(2) His saying: "as in the purity of used water" and as in the water into which impurity fell and it is not known when it fell, refer to al-Hidayah 1/43,44 and al-Durr al-Mukhtar 1/145,146. The ruling of used water is differed upon: Muhammad (and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa) said it is pure but not purifying; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said it is impure. They said: and the statement of Muhammad is chosen for fatwa due to general need. Similarly, performing wudu with date nabidh if one does not find other water: Abu Hanifa said: he performs wudu and does not perform tayammum; Abu Yusuf said: he performs tayammum and does not perform wudu with it, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa and the three Imams said it; and Muhammad said: he performs wudu with it and performs tayammum. And the statement of Abu Yusuf is the correct, chosen, relied-upon, and fatwa-giving school according to us, summarized from al-Hidayah 1/38 and Radd al-Muhtar 1/227.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents the first rule of preference (tarjih) among differing statements within the Hanafi school: in matters of 'ibadat (acts of worship, such as prayer, fasting, etc.), the default is to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, unless the later scholars explicitly state otherwise. The author cites Sharh al-Munyah which praises Abu Hanifa's insight and states that this rule is established by induction. The rule also includes that his narration is followed even if it is not well-known, unless there is weakness or necessity. The commentary then gives examples: used water (whether it is pure or impure) and the case of tayammum with date nabidh. These examples illustrate where the preferred fatwa may differ from Abu Hanifa's well-known view due to public need or stronger evidence. The passage emphasizes memorization of this foundational rule.

Key Terms
الإمام (al-Imām): Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit, the eponym of the Hanafi school.
العبادات (al-‘ibādāt): Acts of worship such as prayer, fasting, pilgrimage, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which category of fiqh is the default to follow Abu Hanifa's statement unless later scholars explicitly state otherwise?
A) Mu'amalat (transactions)
B) 'Ibadat (acts of worship)
C) Legal maxims (qawaid)
D) All categories equally

Key Takeaway
The first rule of fatwa preference: in worship, follow Abu Hanifa unless later scholars explicitly rule otherwise for stronger proof or need.

The Second Rule of Tarjih: Preferring Abu Yusuf in Judiciary Matters
Second rule of tarjīḥ: follow Abu Yūsuf in judiciary matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of preferring Abu Yusuf's opinion in judiciary matters, identify the reason (experience), and determine its scope (including testimonies and related cases).

Core Idea
In judiciary matters, Abu Yusuf's opinion is preferred because experience strengthens a mujtahid's knowledge.

This lesson explains the second rule of preference in the Hanafi school: when giving fatwa on judicial matters (qaḍā') and related areas, the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is given priority over that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The basis for this rule is Abu Yusuf's extensive practical experience as a chief qadi, which enhanced his juristic insights. The rule is supported by Abu Hanifa's own retraction of an earlier opinion after performing Hajj, illustrating the value of experience. Specific applications include the treatment of a silent defendant and the rules of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
Read the passage and note that the rule states: 'Fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf in matters relating to judiciary.' Identify that the scope includes judiciary itself and its subsidiaries, such as testimonies, as added by some commentators.
2
Understand the rationale: experience
The reason given in the source is 'due to his increased experience' (ziyādat tajribatih). Recognize that experience is a recognized factor in tarjih within the Hanafi school.
Abu Hanifa's retraction on charity vs. Hajj shows that experience can change a jurist's view.
3
Analyze the evidence from Abu Hanifa's retraction
The passage cites Abu Hanifa retracting his earlier view that voluntary charity is better than voluntary Hajj after himself performing Hajj and experiencing its hardships. This illustrates that experience can lead to a more informed ruling.
This is used to analogously support Abu Yusuf's preference due to his judicial experience.
4
Apply to a specific case: the silent defendant
Consider the scenario: a defendant remains silent in court. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), he is considered denying. But according to Abu Yusuf, he is imprisoned until he responds. The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf because it is a judiciary matter.
This shows the practical consequence (thamarāt al-khilāf) of following this rule.
5
Extend to testimonies and other judiciary-related matters
The commentary of al-Bayrī extends the rule to testimonies (shahādāt). The author agrees, noting that testimonies are subsidiaries of judiciary. Also, in al-Tanwīr, the rule is applied to not prompting a witness – Abu Yusuf's istiḥsān is followed.
Confirm that any matter directly or indirectly connected to court proceedings falls under this rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And likewise in al-Bazzaziyyah from the chapter on judiciary. End. i.e., due to his obtaining increased knowledge through his experience, and for this reason Abu Hanifa retracted from the statement that voluntary charity is better than voluntary Hajj, when he performed Hajj and knew its hardship.

He added in Sharh al-Bayri on al-Ashbah: 'That fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf also in testimonies.' I (the author) say: but they (testimonies) are among the subsidiary matters of judiciary. And in al-Bahr from the Book of Claims: 'If the defendant remains silent and does not respond, he is considered denying according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). As for Abu Yusuf, he is imprisoned until he responds, as Imam al-Sarakhsi said, and fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's statement in matters relating to judiciary, as in al-Qunyah and al-Bazzaziyyah. Therefore I gave fatwa that he is imprisoned until he responds.'

(1) His saying: 'Fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf in matters relating to judiciary.' He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: 'And the witness is not prompted to give his testimony, and Abu Yusuf deemed it good (istihsan) as a means to obtain additional knowledge, and fatwa is on his statement in matters relating to judiciary.' (Radd al-Muhtar 5/375)

And this rule is based on a principle from the Imam derived from his retraction mentioned in the issue of charity: that when experience is joined to the knowledge of a mujtahid, his statement is preferred over the statement of others.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents the second rule of preference: in matters related to judiciary (qada') and its subsidiaries, including testimonies (shahadat), the relied-upon position is that of Imam Abu Yusuf. The reason given is his extensive experience and practical knowledge in judicial matters. The author supports this by noting that even Abu Hanifa retracted his opinion on the superiority of charity over voluntary Hajj after gaining personal experience. The rule is further extended to testimonies by some scholars, and the author agrees as it falls under judiciary. A specific application is given: if a defendant remains silent in court, according to Abu Yusuf he is imprisoned until he responds, whereas according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) he is considered denying. The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf. The passage concludes by deriving a general principle: when a mujtahid's knowledge is combined with experience, his opinion is preferred.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qaḍā’): Judiciary, the process of adjudication by a qadi.
الشهادات (al-shahādāt): Testimonies, a subset of judiciary rules.
التجربة (al-tajribah): Experience, which gives added weight to a jurist's opinion.
الرجوع (al-rujūʿ): Retraction, changing one's opinion upon obtaining better knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Imam Abu Yusuf
D) The consensus of all three

Key Takeaway
In judiciary matters, the Hanafi mufti must follow the opinion of Abu Yusuf due to his practical experience, even if it contradicts Abu Hanifa or Muhammad.

Fourth Rule: Tarjih of Istihsan over Qiyas
States the rule that istihsan is preferred over qiyas with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that istihsan prevails over qiyas when its evidence is strong, and identify the exceptions where qiyas is retained.

Core Idea
Istihsan prevails over qiyas only when its evidence is stronger; otherwise qiyas remains the rule.

In the Hanafi tradition, istihsan (juristic preference) is a key tool for deriving rulings that account for exceptional circumstances. The fourth rule of Rasm al-Mufti states that istihsan is given precedence over qiyas, but only when the evidence underlying the istihsan is strong. If the istihsan aspect is weak, the general rule of qiyas continues to apply. This lesson unpacks the rule, its rationale, and its application through examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states the fourth rule: 'Istihsan is preponderated over qiyas'. Recognize this as a foundational maxim for the mufti.
2
Understand the condition
The rule is not absolute; it applies only when the istihsan aspect is strong. If weak, qiyas is not abandoned. This is explicitly stated: 'if its aspect is not strong, one does not leave the qiyas'.
The strength is determined by the underlying evidence.
3
Define 'qiyas' in this context
Qiyas here means the continuous general rule of Sharia (al-qa'idah al-mustamirrah), not any analogical reasoning. This is clarified by referring to Ibn al-Humam's commentary on al-Hidayah.
Exceptional cases like kaffarat al-sawm are not part of this continuous rule.
4
Apply to the example
The example from al-Hidayah: The expiation for intercourse during fasting (kaffarat al-sawm) is an exceptional ruling established by istihsan and cannot be extended by qiyas to other acts.
Thus the ruling is specific to that act.
5
Consider broader application
The rule is not limited to a fixed number of issues (e.g., twenty-two). It can apply wherever a strong istihsan exists, as noted in the footnote.
The mufti must evaluate each case on its merits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٤) قوله : "ترجح الاستحسان على القياس " لقوة الدليل الذي اشتمل عليه كما يُعرف من تعريفه، فلو لم يقو وجهه لا يعدل عن القياس كما في المسائل المستثناة . ثم اعلم أن المراد بالقياس في مثل هذا الموضع القاعدة المستمرة في الشرع، قاله ابن الهمام عند قول صاحب الهداية : لأنها [ كفارة الصوم] شرعت في الوقاع بخلاف القياس، فلا يقاس عليه غيره " . (فتح القدير : ٢/ ٢٦٥
(۱) قوله : إلى اثنتين وعشرين ولا تنحضر في هذا بل يمكن أن تزيد عليه .
(۲) قوله : وظاهر كلام فخر الإسلام ... إلخ " قال الإمام فخر الإسلام البزدوي في :أصوله : إنما الاستحسان عندنا أحد القياسيين لكنه يسمى به إشارة إلى أنه الوجه
(4) His statement: 'Istihsan is preponderated over qiyas' due to the strength of the evidence it contains, as known from its definition. So if its aspect is not strong, one does not leave the qiyas, as in the exceptional issues. Then know that by 'qiyas' in such a place is meant the continuous rule in the Sharia, as stated by Ibn al-Humam at the statement of the author of al-Hidayah: 'Because it [expiation of fasting] was legislated for intercourse contrary to analogy, so nothing else is analogized to it.' (Fath al-Qadir 2/265) (1) His statement: 'to twenty two' and it is not limited to that, rather it can be increased. (2) His statement: 'And the apparent statement of Fakhr al-Islam...' Said Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in his Usul: 'Indeed istihsan according to us is one of the two analogies, but it is named thus indicating that it is the preferable aspect.'
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth rule of preference: istihsan (juristic preference) is given precedence over qiyas (analogy). The reason is that istihsan contains a stronger evidence, as defined earlier. If the istihsan aspect is weak, qiyas remains. The author clarifies that 'qiyas' here means the general continuous rule in the Sharia, not just any analogy. The example from al-Hidayah about kaffarat al-sawm (expiation for breaking fast by intercourse) shows that the ruling is exceptional and cannot be extended. The footnotes add that the number of issues is not limited to twenty-two, and that according to al-Bazdawi, istihsan is actually one of the two analogies (the other being qiyas jali), but it is called istihsan to indicate its preference.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): The continuous general rule in the Sharia, not just any analogy.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; adopting a different ruling than what qiyas would indicate due to stronger evidence or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The fourth rule establishes that istihsan overrides qiyas only when its evidence is stronger; otherwise the general rule remains.
