Rule 5: Zahir al-Riwayah is Preferred
States the rule that Zahir al-Riwayah takes precedence over other transmissions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that Zahir al-Riwayah is the default source for fatwa and identify when an exception applies.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary source for Hanafi fatwa; other riwayat are retracted unless scholars explicitly adopt them.

This rule establishes the hierarchy of Hanafi legal sources for a mufti. The passage from Al-Bahr and Anfa' al-Wasa'il clarifies that Zahir al-Riwayah—the six core books of Imam Muhammad—holds precedence. However, exceptions exist: scholars may explicitly state that the fatwa is on a different riwaya, or a case may be absent from Zahir al-Riwayah and must be taken from another authentic transmission. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for sound fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default hierarchy
Zahir al-Riwayah is preponderant over all other riwayat. This means a mufti must first look for the ruling in the six core books.
The six books are: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat.
2
Recognize the exceptions
If scholars explicitly state that the fatwa is upon a different riwaya, that riwaya may be followed. Also, if a ruling is not found in Zahir al-Riwayah but is established in another authentic riwaya, that riwaya must be used.
The key phrase is: 'unless they explicitly state otherwise' — mere existence of another riwaya is not enough.
3
Understand the consequence of non-Zahir rulings
Rulings outside Zahir al-Riwayah are considered retracted (marju' 'anh) and are no longer valid opinions of the mujtahid. A muqallid qadi cannot act upon them without explicit authorization.
This ensures that the madhhab's positions remain stable and reliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظاهر الرواية راجحة على غيرها إلا إذا صرحوا بخلافه
الخامسة : ما في قضاء "البحر " : "من أن ما خرج عن ظاهر الرواية، فهو مرجوع عنه . والمرجوع عنه لم يبق قولا للمجتهد كما ذكروه" . اهـ . وقدمنا عن أنفع الوسائل " : "أن القاضى المقلد لا يجوز له أن يحكم إلا بما هو ظاهر المذهب، لا بالرواية الشاذة إلا أن ينصوا على أن الفتوى عليها . اهـ .
وفي قضاء الفوائت من "البحر": "أن المسألة إذا لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية ، وثبتت فى رواية أخرى، تعين المصير إليها " . اهـ .
Zahir al-Riwayah is preponderant over other than it, unless they explicitly state otherwise. The fifth: What is in Qada' al-Bahr: 'That which departs from Zahir al-Riwayah is retracted. And the retracted is no longer a saying of the mujtahid as they mentioned.' End quote. And we have previously presented from Anfa' al-Wasa'il: 'The muqallid qadi is not permitted to judge except by what is the apparent position of the madhhab, not by the shadhdh riwaya, unless they specify that the fatwa is upon it.' End quote. And in Qada' al-Fawa'it from al-Bahr: 'If a matter is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah, and is established in another riwaya, it is necessary to resort to it.' End quote.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage sets forth a fundamental rule of tarjeeh in the Hanafi madhhab. The first line states the rule: Zahir al-Riwayah—the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani—is given precedence over other riwayat (narrations) from the mujtahid imams, unless later scholars explicitly indicate that the fatwa is on a different riwaya. The commentary from Al-Bahr and Anfa' al-Wasa'il reinforces this: anything outside Zahir al-Riwayah is considered retracted (marju' 'anh) and is no longer a valid opinion of the mujtahid. A muqallid qadi must only judge according to the zahir of the madhhab; he cannot rely on a shadhdh (irregular) riwaya unless the scholars have specifically designated it as the basis for fatwa. However, if a case is not found in Zahir al-Riwayah but is established in another authentic riwaya, then that riwaya must be followed. This ensures hierarchy and reliability in fatwa practice.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat) which contain the primary transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school.
مرجوع عنه (marju' 'anh): A ruling that has been retracted or abandoned; it is no longer considered a valid opinion of the mujtahid.
رواية شاذة (riwaya shadhdhah): An irregular or isolated transmission that is not part of the mainstream Hanafi corpus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule, which riwaya is preferred for fatwa?
A) Any riwaya from Abu Hanifa
B) Zahir al-Riwayah unless scholars specify otherwise
C) The rarest riwaya
D) The most recent riwaya

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi default is Zahir al-Riwayah, and other riwayat must be explicitly authorized to override it.

Rule 6: Stronger Proof is Preponderant – Clarifying Abandonment of Weak Qiyas
Clarifies the abandonment of weak qiyas and application to riwaya conflict.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that when two proofs conflict, the weaker is completely abandoned (matruk) and cannot be acted upon, and identify the mufta bihi position among conflicting riwayat.

Core Idea
When proofs conflict, the weaker falls entirely; it is not merely less preferred but invalid.

This lesson unpacks a crucial rule of tarjeeh (preponderance) in Hanafi usul: when two proofs conflict and one is clearly stronger, the weaker is not merely less preferred — it is completely abandoned and cannot be acted upon. We begin with a clarification from Imam Abd al-Aziz al-Bukhari that corrects a common misunderstanding about qiyas that contradicts istihsan. The same principle then guides us in choosing between conflicting riwayat from Abu Hanifa himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent permission
Read the quote from Sharh al-Munya: it seems to say that acting upon the weaker qiyas is permissible, though istihsan is preferred. Understand why this appears to allow the weaker proof.
The phrase 'al-awwal fi al-amal bihi, wa inna al-amal bi al-akhar jaiz' is the source of the ambiguity.
2
Recognize the correction
Imam al-Bukhari in Kashf al-Asrar rejects this interpretation. He cites the standard wording: 'illa anna tarakna hadha al-qiyas' — 'except that we left this qiyas.' The key term is 'matruk' (abandoned). Something abandoned cannot be acted upon at all.
The shift from 'jaiz' (permissible) to 'matruk' (abandoned) is the core of the refinement.
3
Generalise the rule
Al-Bukhari states the general principle: whenever two proofs conflict and one is clearly stronger, the weaker falls completely. This applies to any proof conflict, not just qiyas vs istihsan.
'Al-da'if yasqut fi muqabil al-aqwa' — the weak falls in the face of the strong.
4
Apply to conflicting riwayat
The passage then turns to ikhtilaf in riwayat from Abu Hanifa on tuma'nina, qawma, jalsa. When riwayat differ, the one that agrees with the stronger proof (diraya/dalil) is preferred. The riwaya that is supported by strong evidence is taken, and others are abandoned.
Diraya here means dalil (proof), as clarified from al-Mustasfa.
5
State the operative rule
The final quote from al-Hawi al-Qudsi: when riwayat differ from Abu Hanifa, the one with the strongest proof is taken. This is the mufta bihi approach: rely on the proof, not merely on the number of transmissions.
This ensures fatwa is based on the soundest evidence, not just on popularity of a riwaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادسة : ما في شرح المنية في بحث تعديل الأركان بعـد مـا ذكـر الأولى في العمل به، وإن العمل بالآخر جائز " . وقال الإمام عبد العزيز البخارى رحمه الله في شرحه المسمى بـ "كشف الأسرار " : "ظاهر هذا الكلام يوهم أن العمل بالقياس الذي عارضه استحسان جائز لكن العمل بالاستحسان أولى ... وليس كذلك ؛ فإن شمس الأئمة رحمه الله قال : وهذا وهم عندى فإن اللفظ المذكور فى عامة الكتب : "إلا أنا تركنا هذا القياس " ، والمتروك لا يجوز العمل به . . . فعرفنا أن القياس متروك في معارضة الاستحسان أصلا، وأن الأضعف يسقط في مقابلة الأقوى ... وهذا هو الحكم في كل معارضة ؛ فإن الدليلين إذا تعارضا وظهر لأحدهما رجحان على الآخر، وجب العمل به وسقط الآخر أصلا، فكذلك في القياس مع الاستحسان " . كشف الأسرار على أصول فخر الإسلام البزدوي : ٤/٤).

اختلاف الرواية عن الإمام فى الطمانينة ، هل هي سنة أو واجبة؟ وكذا القومة والجلسة ، قال : " وأنت علمت أن مقتضى الدليل الوجوب كما قاله الشيخ كمال الدين، ولا ينبغى أن يعدل عن الدراية إذا وافقتها رواية " . اهـ. والدراية - بالدال المهملة - تستعمل بمعنى الدليل كما في "المستصفى " . ويؤيده ما في آخر "الحاوى القدسي " : "إذا اختلفت الروايات عن أبي حنيفة في مسألة ، فالأولى بالأخذ أقواها حجة" .
The sixth: What is in Sharh al-Munya in the discussion of ta'dil al-arkan after he mentioned that the first is to act upon it, and acting upon the other is permissible. And Imam 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari said in his Sharh called Kashf al-Asrar: 'The apparent meaning of this statement suggests that acting upon the qiyas that is contradicted by istihsan is permissible, but acting upon istihsan is preferable... but it is not so; for Shams al-A'imma said: This is a misunderstanding in my view, for the wording found in most books is: "Except that we have left this qiyas," and that which is left is not permissible to act upon... So we know that the qiyas is completely abandoned in the face of istihsan, and that the weaker falls in the presence of the stronger... And this is the ruling in every opposition: when two proofs conflict and one of them appears preponderant over the other, it becomes obligatory to act upon it, and the other falls completely, so likewise in qiyas with istihsan.' (Kashf al-Asrar 4/4). The difference of riwaya from the Imam regarding tuma'nina, whether it is sunna or wajib, likewise qawma and jalsa. He said: 'And you know that the requirement of the dalil is obligation as Shaykh Kamal al-Din said, and one should not turn away from diraya if a riwaya agrees with it.' End quote. And diraya (with an important dal) is used in the sense of dalil as in al-Mustasfa. And it is supported by what is at the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'When the riwayat differ from Abu Hanifa on a matter, the first to take is the one with the strongest proof.'
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth rule of tarjeeh: the stronger proof is preponderant and must be followed. The initial quote from Sharh al-Munya appears to allow acting upon the weaker proof (qiyas) while preferring the stronger (istihsan). However, Imam 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari in Kashf al-Asrar corrects this misunderstanding: the expression 'we left this qiyas' indicates that the qiyas is completely abandoned and cannot be acted upon at all. The principle is general: whenever two proofs conflict and one is clearly stronger, the weaker falls away entirely; it is not merely less preferred. The second part applies this to conflicting riwayat from the Imam regarding the rulings on tuma'nina (tranquility in prayer), qawma (standing), and jalsa (sitting). The stronger proof (dalil/diraya) should be followed, and the riwaya that agrees with that proof is to be taken. The quote from al-Hawi al-Qudsi reinforces that among different riwayat, the one with the strongest proof is to be preferred. This rule ensures that fatwa is based on the soundest evidence.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from a direct analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or equity.
الدراية (diraya): Knowledge derived from reasoning and evidence (dalil); used synonymously with dalil in this text.
متروك (matruk): Left or abandoned; here refers to a qiyas that is no longer considered valid because it conflicts with istihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, what is the status of a qiyas that contradicts istihsan?
A) It is permissible to act upon it but istihsan is preferable
B) It is completely abandoned and cannot be acted upon
C) It is stronger than istihsan
D) It is valid only in emergencies

Key Takeaway
When proofs conflict, the stronger proof invalidates the weaker entirely; the weaker is matruk and cannot be used in fatwa.

Rule 7: Riwaya Avoiding Takfir is Preferred
Rule with expansion of protected categories and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a riwaya avoiding takfir is preferred over a stronger riwaya that leads to takfir, and identify the categories of persons protected from takfir.

Core Idea
A weak riwaya that prevents takfir beats a strong one that would declare a Muslim a kafir.

This lesson introduces a fundamental rule in Hanafi fatwa: the preservation of a Muslim's Islamic status takes precedence over the risk of error in takfir. Even if a riwaya is weak, if it allows avoiding declaring someone a kafir, it is preferred over a stronger riwaya that would necessitate takfir. The passage also clarifies who is protected and who is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
The passage states: a riwaya that preserves a Muslim from takfir is preferred, even if weak. This is the seventh rule of tarjeeh in Rasm al-Mufti.
This is a principle of caution (ihtiyat) in matters of kufr.
2
Recognize the two protected categories
One who says words that can be given a good interpretation (mahmal hasan), and one who holds a belief regarding which mujtahids differ (ikhtilaf) – these are not declared kafir.
The doubt (shubha) from interpretation or disagreement blocks takfir.
3
Identify the exceptions
Explicit statement of kufr, clear signs like prostrating to an idol, insulting sacred matters, denying a necessary of religion, or invalid interpretation contradicting ijma – these remove protection.
These are clear indicators (amarat al-takdhib) that override the rule.
4
Connect to broader principle
The rule applies to people of the qibla: sins or denying obscure matters do not cause takfir. Only clear and established markers of kufr matter.
This aligns with Ahl al-Sunna's cautious approach.
5
Apply the mufti's duty
The mufti must search for any riwaya—even weak—that avoids takfir, and give fatwa accordingly. He should not rush to declare kufr.
This is part of the adab al-mufti and reflects the gravity of takfir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة : ما فى "البحر " من باب المرتد نقلا عن "الفتاوى الصغرى " : الكفر شيء عظيم فلا أجعل المؤمن كافراً متى وجدت رواية أنه لا يكفّر " .اهـ. ثم قال : " والذى تحرر : أنه لا يفتى بكفر مسلم أمكن حمل كلامه على محمل حسن، أو كان في كفره اختلاف (۱)، ولو رواية ضعيفة " . اهـ . (۱) قوله : "محمل حسن أو كان في كفره اختلاف " علم منه أن المنع عن التكفير في حق رجلين : رجل تكلم بكلام يحتمل الكفر وغيره، ويمكن تأويله، ولم يصرح هو بخلافه، ورجل اعتقد عقيدة اختلف المجتهدون في أنها كفر ؛ أما من صرّح بالكفر أو باشر شيئًا من أمارات التكذيب كسجود الصنم والإهانة بأمر شرعى، أو أنكر شيئًا علم كونه من الدين بالضرورة، أو تأول في معناه بتأويل باطل يخالف المعنى المجمع عليه، فلا يتوقف فى تكفيره. ومعنى عدم تكفير أهل القبلة : أن لا يكفر بارتكاب المعاصي، ولا بإنكار الأمور الخفية غير المشهورة هذا ما حققه المحققون، كذا في النبراس شرح العقائد النسفية". وقال الملا على القارى في شرح الفقه الأكبر " : المراد بعدم تكفير أحد من أهل القبلة عند أهل السنة : أنه لا يكفر أحد ما لم يوجد شيء من أمارات الكفر وعلاماته، ولم يصدر عنه شيء من موجباته " . فافهم.
The seventh: What is in al-Bahr from the chapter of apostate, quoting from al-Fatawa al-Sughra: 'Kufr is a grave matter, so I do not consider a believer a kafir whenever I find a riwaya that he is not to be declared kafir.' End quote. Then he said: 'And what is established is that one should not give a fatwa of kufr against a Muslim if his speech can be interpreted in a good way, or if there is a difference of opinion regarding his kufr, even if it is a weak riwaya.' End quote. (1) His statement: 'a good interpretation or there is a difference regarding his kufr' indicates that the prohibition of takfir applies to two types of people: one who speaks words that could be kufr or otherwise and can be interpreted, and he did not explicitly state otherwise; and one who holds a belief regarding which mujtahids differ as to whether it is kufr. As for one who explicitly states kufr, or engages in any signs of denial such as prostrating to an idol or insulting a sacred matter, or denies something known necessarily to be of the religion, or interprets it with an invalid interpretation that contradicts the consensus meaning, then there is no hesitation in declaring him kafir. And the meaning of not declaring the people of the qibla as kafir is that one is not declared kafir for committing sins, nor for denying hidden matters that are not well-known. This is what the verifiers have confirmed, as in al-Nibras Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya. And Mulla 'Ali al-Qari said in Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar: 'The meaning of not declaring any of the people of the qibla as kafir according to Ahl al-Sunna is that no one is declared kafir as long as none of the signs and markers of kufr exist, and nothing from its causes issues from him.' So understand.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh rule of tarjeeh: the riwaya that preserves a Muslim from takfir is preferred, even if it is weak. The first quote from al-Fatawa al-Sughra shows the gravity of takfir—the mufti should withhold takfir as long as there is any riwaya that avoids it. The second quote adds that a fatwa of kufr should not be given if the person's speech can be interpreted in a good way, or if there is a difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) among mujtahids on whether that belief is kufr, even if the riwaya supporting non-takfir is weak. The footnote then clarifies two categories of people who are protected from takfir: one whose words are ambiguous and can be interpreted favorably, and one who holds a belief that is disputed among scholars. However, if someone clearly states kufr, commits acts of disbelief like prostrating to an idol, insults sacred matters, denies a necessary of religion, or interprets with an invalid interpretation that contradicts consensus, then there is no hesitation in declaring them kafir. The passage then explains the broader principle that 'not declaring the people of the qibla as kafir' means that one is not declared kafir for committing sins or denying obscure matters, only for clear and established markers of kufr. The quotes from al-Nibras and Mulla 'Ali al-Qari reaffirm this cautious approach in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
تكفير (takfir): The act of declaring a Muslim to be a kafir (disbeliever).
محمل حسن (mahmal hasan): A plausible good interpretation of someone's words that avoids the implication of kufr.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement among mujtahids over whether a particular belief constitutes kufr.
أمارات التكذيب (amarat al-takdhib): Signs of denial or rejection of Islam, such as prostrating to an idol.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule, in which two cases is a person not declared a kafir?
A) When he explicitly states kufr, or when he commits shirk
B) When his speech can be interpreted favorably, or when there is ikhtilaf among scholars
C) When he denies a necessary of religion, or when he insults a sacred matter
D) When he commits a sin, or when he performs an invalid interpretation

Key Takeaway
A mufti must prefer any riwaya—even weak—that avoids takfir, and only declare kufr when clear signs of disbelief are present.

Eighth Rule: The Retracted Statement is Like the Abrogated
Eighth rule: retracted ruling treated as abrogated, retracting is the madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a mujtahid's retracted statement is treated as abrogated, and prefer the later statement when it is known.

Core Idea
A retracted ruling is like an abrogated one — only the later opinion is the madhhab.

This lesson introduces the eighth rule of rasm al-mufti, which governs how a mufti handles contradictory rulings from a single mujtahid. The rule draws an analogy between retraction (ruju') and abrogation (naskh): once a mujtahid withdraws an earlier opinion, that opinion loses its authority. Understanding this rule is crucial for a mufti when determining the operative position of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the rule in Arabic and English
Begin by memorising the qawida: 'المرجوع عنه بمنزلة المنسوخ فالمرجوع إليه هو الراجح'. Understand that the retracted statement is treated like an abrogated ruling, so the retracting statement is the preponderant one.
This is the foundation of the lesson.
2
Understand the analogy with abrogation
Just as an abrogated (mansukh) ruling is no longer valid and is replaced by the abrogating (nasikh) ruling, a retracted opinion is no longer part of the mujtahid's madhhab. The later opinion replaces it.
The analogy is based on the shared effect: both lose authority.
3
Apply to a concrete scenario
Suppose Imam Abu Hanifa initially ruled that a certain sale is valid due to public need, but later retracted and ruled it invalid. According to the eighth rule, the later ruling (invalid) is his madhhab, and the earlier one is not to be acted upon.
This example illustrates the practical consequence.
4
Recognise the exception
Examine the nuance from Sharh al-Tahrir: if it is not known which statement is later, then both are simply narrated without judging retraction. The rule only applies when the later statement is identified.
This prevents premature dismissal of earlier opinions.
5
Review the cited sources
The passage quotes al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Tawshih, and Sharh al-Tahrir. These are authoritative later Hanafi works that establish this rule. Note how they expand on the basic principle.
Expansion probe: see how later commentators develop the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرجوع عنه بمنزلة المنسوخ فالمرجوع إليه هو الراجح الثامنة : ما في البحر " مما قدمناه قريبا : " من أن المرجوع عنه لم يبق مذهبا للمجتهد، وحينئذ فيجب طلب القول الذي رجع إليه والعمل به ؛ لأن الأول صار بمنزلة الحكم المنسوخ " . وفى "البحر " أيضا عن "التوشيح " : "أن ما رجع عنه المجتهد لا يجوز الأخذ به " . اهـ . وذكر في "شرح التحرير " : إن علم المتأخر فهو مذهبه، ويكون الأول منسوخا ، وإلا حكى عنه القولان من غير أن يحكم على أحدهما بالرجوع " .
The retracted statement is in the position of the abrogated, so the retracting statement is the preponderant. Eighth: What is in al-Bahr from what we recently presented: 'The retracted statement is no longer the madhhab of the mujtahid, and then it is obligatory to seek the statement he retracted to and act upon it, because the first has become like an abrogated ruling.' And in al-Bahr also from al-Tawshih: 'What the mujtahid has retracted from is not permissible to act upon.' And it is mentioned in Sharh al-Tahrir: 'If the later [statement] is known, then it is his madhhab, and the first is abrogated; otherwise, both statements are narrated from him without ruling that one is a retraction.'
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage articulates the eighth principle for preferencing among different rulings. It compares retraction (ruju') to abrogation (naskh). The key idea is that when a mujtahid (in this context, an imam of the madhhab like Abu Hanifa) retracts an earlier opinion, the earlier opinion is no longer considered part of his madhhab; it is like an abrogated ruling (mansukh). Therefore, it is obligatory to seek and act upon the later opinion. The passage quotes al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Tawshih to support this, and then adds a nuance from Sharh al-Tahrir: if it is known which opinion is later, that one is the madhhab and the earlier is abrogated; if not, both opinions are simply narrated without judging which is the retraction.

Key Terms
المرجوع عنه (al-marju' 'anhu): The statement that the mujtahid has retracted.
المرجوع إليه (al-marju' ilayhi): The statement that the mujtahid retracted to (his later opinion).
المنسوخ (al-mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that is no longer valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eighth rule, what is the status of a mujtahid's retracted statement?
A) It is still valid but less preferred
B) It is like an abrogated ruling and not to be acted upon
C) It is only abrogated if explicitly stated
D) It retains equal weight with the retracting statement

Key Takeaway
When a mujtahid retracts an earlier opinion, that opinion becomes like an abrogated ruling and must not be acted upon; only the later opinion is his madhhab.

Explicit Authentication Overrides Implicit: The Ninth Rule
Ninth rule: precedence of explicit over implicit authentication in Hanafi source hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of precedence of explicit authentication over implicit authentication to determine the relied-upon position when a matn and sharh differ.

Core Idea
Explicit authentication in a sharh overrides the implicit authentication of a matn.

When a Hanafi matn (foundational text) states a ruling, it carries implicit authentication because its author committed to transmitting only the correct opinion. However, a sharh (commentary) may explicitly state which ruling is correct. The ninth rule in Rasm al-Mufti clarifies that this explicit authentication takes precedence. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti when conflicting indications appear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sources
Locate the ruling in both a matn (e.g., al-Mukhtar) and a sharh (e.g., commentary by Qasim). Note whether each is presented as a statement or explicitly authenticated.
The matn's statement is presumed correct implicitly; the sharh may add 'al-sahih' or 'al-mu'tamad'.
2
Determine the type of authentication
Classify the matn's authentication as implicit (iltizami) — it is correct because the author committed to only including correct rulings. Classify the sharh's statement as explicit (sarih) if it directly says 'the correct view is...' or 'the relied-upon position is...'.
Implicit authentication is assumed; explicit authentication must be stated clearly.
3
Apply the rule
Apply the qawida: Explicit authentication takes precedence over implicit authentication. Therefore, the ruling explicitly authenticated in the sharh is the mufta bihi.
This rule is a specific sub-maxim that qualifies the general maxim 'mutun are preferred over shuruh'.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi
State the relied-upon ruling as the one from the sharh's explicit authentication. This is the operative position for fatwa.
If the sharh does not explicitly authenticate but only comments, the matn's implicit authentication remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التاسعة ما ذكره العلامة قاسم في "تصحيحه " : "أن ما في المتون مصحح تصحيحا التزاميا، والتصحيح الصريح مقدم على التصحيح الالتزامي". قلت : حاصله أن أصحاب المتون التزموا وضع القول الصحيح، فيكون ما في غيرها مقابل الصحيح ما لم يصرح بتصحيحه، فيقدم عليها؛ لأنه تصحيح صريح، فيقدم على التصحيح الالتزامى . وفي شهادات الخيرية " فى جواب سؤال : "المذهب الصحيح المفتى به الذي مشت عليه أصحاب المتون الموضوعة لنقل الصحيح من المذهب الذي هو ظاهر الرواية: أن شهادة الأعمى لا تصح . ثم قال : "وحيث علم أن القول هو الذى تواردت عليه المتون، فهو المعتمد المعمول به ؛ إذ صرحوا بأنه
Ninth: What Allamah Qasim mentioned in his Tashih: 'What is in the mutun is authenticated with implicit authentication, and explicit authentication takes precedence over implicit authentication.' I say: The summary is that the authors of the mutun committed themselves to stating the correct ruling, so what is in other works is in contrast to the correct unless it is explicitly authenticated, so [explicit authentication] takes precedence over it because it is explicit authentication, so it takes precedence over implicit authentication. And in Shahadat al-Khayriyyah, in answer to a question: 'The correct madhhab that is given fatwa upon, which the authors of the mutun that were written to transmit the correct from the madhhab (which is Zahir al-Riwayah) followed, is that the testimony of a blind person is invalid.' Then he said: 'And when it is known that the statement is that upon which the mutun are consistent, it is the relied-upon and acted-upon, since they stated that...'
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This ninth rule deals with hierarchy of sources within the Hanafi madhhab. The author explains that the mutun (foundational texts like al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqayah, etc.) implicitly contain the correct ruling because their authors committed themselves to reporting only the sound position (Zahir al-Riwayah). This is called 'implicit authentication' (tasheeh iltizami). However, when a commentary (sharh) explicitly authenticates a ruling (tasheeh sarih), that explicit authentication takes precedence over the implicit one. The author then illustrates with an example from Shahadat al-Khayriyyah regarding the testimony of a blind person: the mutun agree it is invalid, so that is the relied-upon opinion. The passage cuts off mid-explanation.

Key Terms
التصحيح الالتزامي (al-tasheeh al-iltizami): Implicit authentication: the commitment of matn authors to only transmit the sound ruling (Zahir al-Riwayah), without explicitly stating it.
التصحيح الصريح (al-tasheeh al-sarih): Explicit authentication: when a commentator explicitly states that a particular ruling is the correct and relied-upon one.
المتون (al-mutun): Foundational texts of the Hanafi madhhab that compile the correct rulings (e.g., al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ninth rule, what takes precedence: a ruling implicitly authenticated in a matn, or a ruling explicitly authenticated in a sharh?
A) The matn is always preferred
B) Explicit authentication in the sharh takes precedence
C) Both are equal
D) It depends on the subject

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi source hierarchy, explicit authentication in a sharh overrides the implicit authentication of a matn.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Preference of Mutun over Shuruh and Fatawa
Hierarchy of textual authority in Hanafi iftaa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of mutun, shuruh, and fatawa in Hanafi tarjih, and identify the exception when explicit tashih overrides.

Core Idea
Explicit tashih overrides the implicit tashih of mutun — but otherwise, mutun take precedence over shuruh and fatawa.

In the Hanafi madhhab, not all sources carry equal weight. The core texts (mutun) are presumed to transmit the correct ruling, but later commentaries and fatwa collections may explicitly correct a ruling. This lesson unpacks the ninth rule of tarjih: how to prioritize when these sources conflict. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti to issue sound fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its sources
The rule states: al-mutun muqaddam 'ala al-shuruh wa al-shuruh 'ala al-fatawa. The passage draws from Allamah Qasim's Tashih and other works. Note that the rule is not absolute; it has a restriction mentioned in the marginal notes.
The rule is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) under the larger principle of tarjih.
2
Differentiate implicit vs. explicit tashih
Mutun contain implicit tashih (iltizami) because their authors committed to transmitting only the correct opinion. Explicit tashih (sarih) is a later, deliberate correction found in shuruh or fatawa. The passage stresses that explicit tashih takes precedence over implicit tashih.
Implicit tashih is weaker; it is assumed but not stated outright.
3
Apply the rule to a concrete example
The example from the text: testimony of a blind person. The mutun agree it is invalid. If a fatwa book claims it is valid, the mutun are followed because they have implicit tashih. However, if a sharh explicitly corrects the ruling (e.g., stating that it is valid), then the explicit tashih prevails.
The rule applies when there is no explicit tashih to the contrary.
4
Recognize the restriction (istithna)
The marginal note (1) clarifies: 'This is restricted to when there is no explicit tashih to the contrary.' If explicit tashih exists, it overrides even the mutun. This is rare but possible.
Explicit tashih can come from a later sharh or fatwa compilation.
5
Integrate with related principles
The rule interacts with the broader principle that explicit tashih is stronger than implicit. Also noted: if a fatwa is found in both shuruh and fatawa, it may be given precedence over mutun if it constitutes explicit tashih. Understand that mutun are foundational but not infallible.
The passage also cites a view that fatawa are choices of mashayikh and do not contradict codified madhhab books—this reinforces the default priority of mutun.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۲) وفى فصل الحبس من "البحر " : "والعمل على ما في المتون ؛ لأنه إذا تعارض ما في المتون والفتاوى، فالمعتمد ما في المتون، كما في أنفع الوسائل " ، وكذا يقدم ما في الشروح على ما في الفتاوى".. اهـ. أى لما صرح به في "أنفع الوسائل " أيضاً في مسألة قسمة الوقف حيث قال : " لا يفتى بنقول الفتاوى، بل نقول الفتاوى إنما يستأنس بها إذا لم يوجد ما يعارضها من كتب الأصول ونقل المذهب، أما مع وجود غيرها لا يلتفت إليها خصوصا إذا لم يكن نضع فيها على الفتوى " . ورأيت في بعض كتب المتأخرين نقلا عن "إيضاح الاستدلال على إبطال الاستبدال " لقاضي القضاة شمس الدين الحريري، أحد شراح الهداية " : "أن صدر الدين سليمان قال : إن هذه الفتاوى هي اختيارات المشايخ فلا تعارض كتب المذهب " . قال (۳) : وكذا كان يقول غيره من مشايخنا، وبه أقول . اهـ . (۱) قوله : "فالمعتمد ما في المتون " هذا مقيد بما إذا لم يوجد التصحيح الصريحي بخلافه، فإن وجد قدم القول المصرح بتصحيحه ؛ لأن التصريح بتصحيح قول يجعله المعتمد في المذهب حتى لو كان معارضا بما فى المتون، لكن هذا قليل في المذهب جدا. (۲) قوله : "وكذا يقدم ما في الشروح على ما في الفتاوى " نعم ! إذا وجد ما يدل على الفتوى فى الشروح والفتاوى، فحينئذ يقدم ما فيهما على ما في المتون؛ لأن التصحيح الصريحي أولى من التصحيح الالتزامي. (مظ) . (۳) قوله : "قال أى الحريري، شمس الدین قاضی القضاة، رحمه الله تعالى :
Ninth: What Allamah Qasim mentioned in his Tashih: 'What is in the mutun is corrected with implicit tashih, and explicit tashih is given precedence over implicit tashih.' I say: Its summary is that the authors of the mutun committed themselves to putting the correct opinion, so what is in other books is mukhalif (opposed) to the correct until it is explicitly corrected, so [the explicit] is given precedence over them because it is explicit tashih, thus it takes precedence over implicit tashih. And in Shahadat al-Khayriyah, in answer to a question: 'The correct madhhab to give fatwa on, which the authors of the mutun have followed—the mutun composed to transmit the correct from the madhhab which is Zahir al-Riwayah—is that the testimony of a blind person is not valid.' Then he said: 'And where it is known that a saying is the one that the mutun agree upon, it is the relied-upon and acted upon; for they declared that when what is in the mutun and the fatawa conflict, the relied-upon is what is in the mutun.' Likewise, what is in the shuruh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa. End. And in the chapter of Hubs from al-Bahr: 'And practice is upon what is in the mutun, because if what is in the mutun and the fatawa conflict, the relied-upon is what is in the mutun, as in Anfa' al-Wasa'il.' Likewise, what is in the shuruh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa. End. That is because it is stated in Anfa' al-Wasa'il also in the issue of division of waqf: 'Fatwas are not given from the transmissions of fatawa; rather, the transmissions of fatawa are only used for finding comfort if there is no opposing material from the books of usul and transmitted madhhab, but if other material exists, they are not paid attention to, especially if they were not compiled for fatwa.' And I saw in some later books a transmission from Idah al-Istidlal 'ala Ibtal al-Istibdal by Qadi al-Qudah Shams al-Din al-Hariri, one of the commentators of al-Hidayah: 'Sadr al-Din Sulayman said: Indeed these fatawa are the choices of the mashayikh, so they do not contradict the books of the madhhab.' He (al-Hariri) said: 'And others among our mashayikh used to say the same, and I say it.' End. (1) His saying: 'So the relied-upon is what is in the mutun' is restricted to when there is no explicit tashih to the contrary. If it is found, the opinion explicitly corrected is given precedence, because explicit correction makes it the relied-upon in the madhhab even if it contradicts what is in the mutun, but this is very rare in the madhhab. (2) His saying: 'Likewise, what is in the shuruh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa'—Yes! If something indicating the fatwa is found in the shuruh and fatawa, then what is in them is given precedence over what is in the mutun, because explicit tashih is better than implicit tashih. (Mazhar). (3) His saying: 'He said' means al-Hariri, Shams al-Din Qadi al-Qudah, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth rule of tarjih, explaining the hierarchy of textual authority in the Hanafi madhhab. The author begins by quoting Allamah Qasim that the mutun (core texts) contain implicit tashih (correction) because their authors committed themselves to transmitting only the correct opinion. In contrast, shuruh (commentaries) and fatawa books may contain explicit tashih. Explicit tashih takes precedence over implicit tashih. Therefore, if a ruling is explicitly corrected in a sharh or fatwa work, it overrides the mutun. However, in the absence of explicit tashih, the mutun are prioritized over shuruh and fatawa. This is supported by the example of the testimony of a blind person, where the mutun agree on its invalidity. The passage then quotes al-Bahr and Anfa' al-Wasa'il reinforcing that mutun take precedence when there is conflict. A later quote from al-Hariri adds that fatawa are choices of the mashayikh and do not contradict the codified madhhab books. The marginal notes clarify: the rule that mutun are preferred is restricted to when no explicit tashih contradicts; if explicit tashih is found, that takes precedence even over mutun. Similarly, if a fatwa appears in shuruh and fatawa, it can take precedence over mutun due to explicit tashih. This balances the authority of foundational texts with later scholarly corrections.

Key Terms
المتون (al-mutun): Core texts of the madhhab, e.g., al-Mukhtar, al-Kanz, etc., that commit to transmitting the correct ruling.
التصحيح الصريح (al-tashih al-sarih): Explicit correction of a ruling found in commentaries or fatwa works.
التصحيح الالتزامي (al-tashih al-iltizami): Implicit correction assumed by the author of a matn based on his commitment to transmit only what is correct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Whenever it differs from the matn.
B) When it explicitly corrects the ruling (tashih sarih).
C) When it is from a later century.
D) Never; mutun are always final.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi tarjih, the implicit tashih of mutun is overridden by explicit tashih in shuruh or fatawa; otherwise, mutun are preferred.

The Reliable Texts in the Hanafi Madhhab
Listing and defining the reliable matns for transmitting the madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the reliable texts (mutun mu'tabara) in the Hanafi madhhab, explain the hierarchy among them, and apply the rule that these texts are the primary source for fatwa but with the nuance that they may occasionally include non-Zahir al-Riwayah opinions.

Core Idea
Not all matns are equal: only those transmitting the soundest positions (rajih) from Zahir al-Riwayah are reliable for fatwa.

A mufti must know which texts to rely on when issuing fatwa. This passage from the Rasm al-Mufti literature provides crucial guidance: not every text called a 'matn' is equally authoritative. The reliable matns are those whose authors sift between strong and weak opinions, transmitting only the preponderant (rajih) from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus. This lesson unpacks the list of these texts, their hierarchy, and important caveats.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of 'al-mutun al-mu'tabara'
Understand that 'reliable texts' refers to a specific set of works that transmit the soundest positions of the madhhab, as opposed to every matn.
The authors of these texts must be able to distinguish between preponderant and weak opinions.
2
List the seven named reliable matns
From the passage: Al-Bidaya, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Al-Mukhtar, Al-Niqaya, Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Al-Multaqa. Memorise these as the core reliable sources.
These are contrasted with Al-Ghurar and Al-Tanwir, which contain many later fatwa issues.
3
Distinguish between early and later terminology
The passage notes that 'mutun' for later scholars means works by authors who sift opinions, while early scholars referred to works of senior Hanafis like al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, etc.
This distinction affects how one interprets the phrase 'what is in the texts is given precedence'.
4
Understand the 'three texts' and 'four texts' hierarchy
The most famous and strongest are Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the 'three texts'). The 'four texts' adds either Al-Mukhtar or Al-Majma' (Majma' al-Bahrayn).
These are the most authoritative for fatwa in the later school.
5
Recognize the dominant but not universal nature of the rule
The passage warns that it is a dominant (ghalibi) rather than universal (kulli) rule that matns transmit only Zahir al-Riwayah and only the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. They sometimes include later derivations (e.g., 'al-ushr fi al-ushr') or the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad when those are preponderant.
A mufti must verify the source even in reliable matns.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلب في المتون المعتبرة
ثم لا يخفى أن المراد بالمتون المتون المعتبرة كـ "البداية"، و "مختصر القدوري"، و "المختار"، و "النقاية"، و "الوقاية"، و "الكنز"، و "الملتقى"؛
فإنها الموضوعة لنقل المذهب مما هو ظاهر الرواية، بخلاف متن "الغرر" لملاخسرو، ومتن "التنوير" للتمرتاشى الغزى؛ فإن فيهما كثيراً من مسائل الفتاوى.
(۱) قوله: المراد بالمتون المتون المعتبرة كالبداية " قال المولى عبد الحى : " ولم يريدوا بالمتون كل المتون، بل المتون التي مصنفوها مميزون بين الراجح والمرجوح، والمقبول ،والمردود، والقوى والضعيف، فلا يوردون فى متونهم إلا الراجح والمقبول والقوى . وأصحاب هذه المتون كذلك. وهذا في عرف المتأخرين، وأما في عرف المتقدمين قبل أزمنة المصنّفين المذكورين، فحيث قالوا: "ما في المتون مقدم " أرادوا متون كبار مشايخنا وأجلة فقهاءنا، كتصانيف الطحاوى، والكرخي، والجصاص
والخصاف، والحاكم، وغيرهم.

(۲) قوله : " فإنها الموضوعة لنقل المذهب أعلم أنه قد اشتهر أن المتون موضوعة لنقل أصل المذهب، ومسائل ظاهر الرواية . وهذا حكم غالبى لا كلى، فإنه كثيراً ما يذكر أرباب المتون مسألة هي من تخريجات المشايخ المتقدمين مخالفة المسلك الأئمة المتبوعين، كمسألة "العشر في العشر" في باب نجاسة الحوض وظهارته، وأصل المذهب خال عن هذا فاحفظ. وكذا ما اشتهر المتون موضوعة لنقل مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة " - حكم غالبي لاكلى، فكثيراً ما ذكروا فيها مذهب صاحبيه إذا كان راجحا، كما في بحث السجدة بالجبهة والأنف، وغيره. (مظ)
Section on the reliable texts. Then it is not hidden that what is meant by 'the texts' is the reliable texts, such as Al-Bidaya, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Al-Mukhtar, Al-Niqaya, Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Al-Multaqa. For they are established to transmit the madhhab from what is Zahir al-Riwayah, unlike the text of Al-Ghurar by Mulla Khusraw and the text of Al-Tanwir by al-Tamurtashi al-Ghazzi, for in them are many issues from the fatawa. (1) The saying: the meant by 'the texts' is the reliable texts such as Al-Bidaya. Al-Mulla 'Abd al-Hayy said: 'They did not mean by 'the texts' every text, but rather the texts whose authors distinguish between the preponderant and the preponderated, the accepted and the rejected, the strong and the weak, so they only include in their texts the preponderant, accepted, and strong. And the authors of these texts are like that. This is in the terminology of the later scholars. As for the terminology of the early scholars before the times of the mentioned authors, when they said 'what is in the texts is given precedence', they meant the texts of our great shaykhs and senior jurists, like the works of al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, al-Jassas, al-Khassaf, al-Hakim, and others. Then know that the most famous texts in mention and strongest in reliance are Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri. They are what is meant by their saying 'the three texts', and if they say 'the four texts' they mean these three and Al-Mukhtar or Al-Majma' i.e. Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn by Ibn al-Sa'ati. (Mazhar) (2) His saying: 'for they are established to transmit the madhhab'. Know that it has become famous that the texts are established to transmit the foundation of the madhhab and the issues of Zahir al-Riwayah. This is a dominant rule, not universal, for often the authors of the texts mention an issue that is from the derivations of the early shaykhs contrary to the way of the followed imams, such as the issue of 'one-tenth in one-tenth' in the chapter of impurity of the tank and its purification, while the original madhhab is devoid of this, so memorize. Similarly, what is famous that the texts are established to transmit the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is a dominant rule, not universal, for they often mention in them the madhhab of his two companions when it is preponderant, as in the discussion of prostration with the forehead and nose, and other issues. (Mazhar)
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage establishes a rule for muftis: not all matns (texts) are equally authoritative. The reliable matns (al-mutun al-mu'tabara) are those that transmit the soundest positions (al-rajih, al-maqbul, al-qawi) from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus. The text names seven key matns: Al-Bidaya, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Al-Mukhtar, Al-Niqaya, Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Al-Multaqa. These are contrasted with Al-Ghurar and Al-Tanwir, which include many later fatwa issues. The commentary clarifies that 'mutun' in the terminology of later scholars refers to works by authors who sift between strong and weak opinions. For early scholars, 'mutun' referred to works of major early Hanafis like al-Tahawi and al-Karkhi. The three most relied-upon matns are Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the 'three texts'), and the 'four texts' adds either Al-Mukhtar or Al-Majma'. The second note warns that the rule about matns transmitting only the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and only Zahir al-Riwayah is dominant (ghalibi) not universal (kulli). Occasionally, matns include issues from later derivations (e.g., 'al-ushr fi al-ushr' which is not in the original madhhab). They also include the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani when their view is preponderant. This is important for muftis: one cannot assume that every ruling in a matn is necessarily from Imam Abu Hanifa or from Zahir al-Riwayah without verification.

Key Terms
الظاهر الرواية (al-zāhir al-riwāyah): The well-known transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school from the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) as compiled by Imam Muhammad in his six books.
المتون الثلاثة (al-mutūn al-thalāthah): The three most authoritative matns: Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Bidaya
B) Mukhtasar al-Quduri
C) Al-Tanwir
D) Al-Kanz

Key Takeaway
The reliable matns are those that transmit the soundest opinions from Zahir al-Riwayah; among them, the three most authoritative are Al-Wiqaya, Al-Kanz, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri, but even they may occasionally include non-standard rulings.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Explicit and Implicit Correction in Fatwa Books
Explaining the principle of preferring early opinions in Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya and Multaqa al-Abhur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rule for preferring the first-mentioned opinion in Al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhur, and apply the principle of implicit correction to determine the mu'tamad in other fatwa works.

Core Idea
The first opinion in some books is preferred; in others, the one with stronger proof.

The mufti often faces multiple opinions in fatwa collections. This passage from Rasm al-Mufti provides key guidance: in Al-Fatawa al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhur, the first-mentioned opinion is given preference because the authors state they begin with the most preponderant. In other works like Al-Hidayah, the mufti must rely on the opinion whose proof is stronger and more verified. This lesson unpacks the method of 'implicit correction' (al-tashih al-iltizami) to extract the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific books
Note which books are mentioned: Al-Fatawa al-Khaniyya (Qadikhan) and Multaqa al-Abhur (al-Halabi) for the first-opinion rule; Al-Hidayah and similar works for the alternate rule.
The same rule does not apply to all books; each may have its own convention.
2
Apply the first-opinion rule
In Al-Khaniyya and Multaqa, the first-mentioned opinion has merit (zhu maziyya) and is the mu'tamad, because the authors explicitly state they begin with the most apparent and famous.
Qadikhan’s introduction is key evidence.
3
Apply the strong-proof rule for other books
In works like Al-Hidayah, rely on the opinion whose proof is delayed (i.e., the one with stronger proof). The proof is considered the 'verified' (muharrar).
The delayed opinion is often the one with more detailed evidence.
4
Recognize implicit correction by proof presentation
When a book provides a proof for one opinion and neglects the other, that indicates the preferred view. This is a form of implicit correction.
Absence of a proof for an opinion implies it is marjuh (weak).
5
Understand the two types of implicit correction
The two types: (1) presenting the preponderant opinion first in some books and delaying it in others, and (2) providing proof for the preponderant opinion and leaving or answering the proof for the preponderated.
These help the mufti navigate conflicting apparent signals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلب في التصحيح الصريحي والالتزامي
٥٣ - وسابق الأقوال في الخانيه ومُلتَقَى الأبحُرِ ذُو مَزيه (١)
٥٤ - وَفِي سِوَاهُمَا اعْتَمَدَ مَا أَخَرُوا دَليْلَه لأنّهُ الْمُحَرَر
٥٥- كَمَا هُوَ العَادَةُ فِي الْهِدَايَه وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحِ الدرايه (۲)
٥٦ كَذَا إِذَا مَا وَاحدًا قَد عَلَلُوا لَه وَتَعْلَمْلَ . وَاهُ أَهْمَلُوْا
مطلب التصحيح الالتزامى على نوعين (٣)
(٤) أى إن أول الأقوال الواقعة في فتاوى الإمام قاضيخان " له مزية على غيره في الرجحان ؛ لأنه قال في أول الفتاوى : " وفيما كثرت فيه الأقاويل من المتأخرين ، اقتصرت (4) على قول أو قولين، وقدمت ما هو الأظهر، وافتتحت بما هو الأشهر ؛ إجابة للطلبين وتيسيراً على الراغبين " . اهـ . وكذا صاحب ملتقى الأبحر التزم تقديم القول المعتمد .
(۱) قوله : ذو مزية" أى ذو فضيلة على المسألة المتأخرة، وهو خبر لقوله : "وسابق الأقوال فى الخانية وملتقى الأبحر " .
(۲) قوله : "الراجح الدراية " أى للقول الذي دليله أقوى وأرجح.
(۳) قوله : نوعين " أي تقديم القول الراجح في بعض الكتب وتأخيره في بعضها، وتعليل الراجح وترك تعليل المرجوح والجواب عنه .
(٤) كذافي الأصل المطبوع بمصر، والصحيح المطابق للخانية بدله : اقتصرت " . (مظ)
Section on explicit and implicit correction. 53 - And the first of the statements in Al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhur has merit (1). 54 - And in other than these two, rely on what they delayed its proof because it is the verified (muharrar). 55 - As is the custom in Al-Hidayah and similar works for the preponderant of knowledge (2). 56 - Likewise, when they have given a proof for one [opinion] and you find it, and they have neglected it. Section: Implicit correction is of two types (3). (4) That is, the first of the statements occurring in the Fatawa of Imam Qadikhan has merit over others in preponderance, because he said at the beginning of his Fatawa: 'And in those matters where there are many statements among the later scholars, I limited myself (4) to one or two statements, and I presented the most apparent, and began with the most famous, in response to seekers and to facilitate those who desire.' End. Similarly, the author of Multaqa al-Abhur committed himself to presenting the relied-upon statement. (1) His saying: 'has merit' i.e., has excellence over the later statement, and it is the predicate of his saying: 'And the first of the statements in Al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhur'. (2) His saying: 'the preponderant of knowledge' i.e., for the statement whose proof is stronger and more preponderant. (3) His saying: 'two types' i.e., presenting the preponderant statement in some books and delaying it in others, and providing proof for the preponderant and leaving proof for the preponderated and responding to it. (4) As in the printed original in Egypt, and the correct one matching Al-Khaniyya is instead of it: 'I limited myself'. (Mazhar)
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage explains how the mufti can determine the relied-upon ruling (al-mu'tamad) in two authoritative fatwa collections: Al-Fatawa al-Khaniyya (by Qadikhan) and Multaqa al-Abhur (by Ibrahim al-Halabi). The rule is: the first-mentioned opinion in these books is given preference ( ذو مزية ). The reason is that the authors themselves state that they begin with the most preponderant and most famous opinion. For other books (like Al-Hidayah), the mufti should rely on the opinion whose proof is stronger and more verified ( al-muharrar ). The verse also mentions that when a book provides a proof for one opinion but neglects the other, that indicates the preferred view. The section concludes that 'implicit correction' (al-tashih al-iltizami) is of two types: (1) presenting the preponderant opinion in some books and delaying it in others, and (2) providing proof for the preponderant opinion and leaving it for the preponderated (or answering it). This helps the mufti navigate when multiple opinions are present.

Key Terms
التصحيح الالتزامي (al-taṣḥīḥ al-iltizāmī): Implicit correction: Determining the relied-upon opinion by the author's method of presentation (e.g., placing it first or providing its proof) rather than by explicit statement.
سابق الأقوال (sābiq al-aqwāl): The first-mentioned statement in a sequence; in Al-Khaniyya and Multaqa, this carries a presumption of being the relied-upon opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which book's first-mentioned opinion is given preference due to the author's own statement?
A) Al-Hidayah
B) Al-Fatawa al-Khaniyya
C) Mukhtasar al-Quduri
D) Al-Wiqaya

Key Takeaway
The first-mentioned opinion in Al-Khaniyya and Multaqa is the mu'tamad; in other books like Al-Hidayah, the opinion with stronger proof is preferred.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Types of Tashih: Explicit and Implicit Correction in Hanafi Books
Explaining rules of explicit and implicit tashih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of tashih (sarih and iltizami) and apply the rules to determine the preferred opinion in Hanafi books based on the book's method and the presence of ta'lil.

Core Idea
The method of a Hanafi book dictates which opinion is preferred — explicit or implicit correction guides fatwa.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, not all opinions are equal. Books follow specific patterns to signal the preferred view. This lesson explains the difference between explicit correction (tashih sarih) and implicit correction (tashih iltizami), and how to read books like al-Hidayah and al-Khaniyah to extract the mufta bihi ruling. Understanding this is essential for any mufti to avoid issuing fatwa on a weaker opinion.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish explicit vs implicit correction
Identify whether a book explicitly states which opinion is preferred (tashih sarih) or relies on patterns like delaying evidence or giving ta'lil (tashih iltizami).
Explicit: 'the fatwa is on this' or 'this is the most apparent'. Implicit: no direct statement, but method indicates preference.
2
Learn the method of books like al-Khaniyah and Multaqa al-Abhar
In these books, the author begins with the most famous or most apparent opinion, so the first mentioned is preferred.
Qadikhan states: 'I presented what is most apparent and began with what is most famous.'
3
Learn the method of detailed books like al-Hidayah
In al-Hidayah and similar books, the author delays the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, then gives his evidence after others, which is an implicit preference.
Ibn al-Shalabi: 'This is a sign of acting by his statement, even if not explicit.'
4
Recognize ta'lil as a sign of preponderance
If one opinion is given a reasoning (ta'lil) while the other is not, the reasoned opinion is preferred.
Example from al-Hidayah on weaning: Imam Muhammad's opinion is preferred because it includes ta'lil.

Commentary on Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Page 145. Explicit and implicit correction. Section on explicit and implicit correction. 53 - And the first of the statements in al-Khaniyah and Multaqa al-Abhar has merit (1) 54 - And in other than them, rely on what they delayed its evidence because it is the verified. 55 - As is the custom in al-Hidayah and similar works for the rajih of knowledge. (2) 56 - Likewise, if they gave a reasoning for one and left his counterpart unaddressed. Section: Implicit correction is of two types (3). (4) That is, the first of the statements occurring in the Fatawa of Imam Qadikhan has merit over others in preponderance; because he said at the beginning of the Fatawa: 'And in matters where the statements of the later scholars are numerous, I confined myself to one or two statements, and I presented what is most apparent, and I began with what is most famous, as a response to seekers and ease for those who desire.' End. Likewise, the author of Multaqa al-Abhar committed to presenting the relied-upon statement. (1) His saying 'has merit' means it has virtue over the later issue, and it is the predicate of his saying: 'And the first of the statements in al-Khaniyah and Multaqa al-Abhar.' (2) His saying 'the rajih of knowledge' means the statement whose evidence is stronger and more preponderant. (3) His saying 'two types' means presenting the rajih statement in some books and delaying it in others, and giving reasoning for the rajih and leaving the marjuh without reasoning and answering it. (4) As in the printed original in Egypt, and the correct corresponding to al-Khaniyah is instead: 'I confined myself.' (Muzhir) Page 146. Implicit correction is of two types. Commentary on Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. And other than these two books, among the books that mention statements with their evidences, like al-Hidayah and its commentaries, and commentaries of al-Kanz, and Kafi al-Nasafi, and al-Badai' and other detailed books, the custom therein when relating statements is that they delay the statement of Imam, then mention the evidence of each statement, then mention the evidence of Imam containing the answer to what others used as evidence. And this is a preponderance for him unless they explicitly state a preponderance for another. Shaykh al-Islam Allamah Ibn al-Shalabi said in his Fatawa: 'The principle is that practice is on the statement of Abu Hanifa, and therefore the scholars preponderate his evidence over the evidence of those who oppose him from his companions, and they answer what his opponent used as evidence, and this is a sign of acting by his statement, even if they do not explicitly give fatwa upon it; because preponderance is an explicit correction.' End. And at the end of al-Mustasfa by Imam al-Nasafi: 'If three statements are mentioned in an issue, the rajih is the first or the last, not the middle.' End. I say: It should be restricted to when the custom of the author of that book is not known and the evidences are not mentioned. If it is known as passed regarding al-Khaniyah and al-Multaqa, then follow; and if the evidences are mentioned, then the last is preponderant as we said. Likewise, if they mention two statements and give reasoning for one of them, it is a preponderance for it over the one not given reasoning, as al-Khair al-Ramli stated in the book of Ghasp from his Fatawa al-Khairiyyah. And similar is what is in al-Tahrir and its commentary in the chapter on preponderance between conflicting evidences: 'That (1) His saying 'preponderance for it over the one not given reasoning' and this type of correction is frequently found in al-Hidayah; among that is his statement in the book of rada': 'And weaning is not considered before the period except in a narration from Abu Hanifa if the child becomes independent of it, and its reason is the cessation of growth due to change of milk.' (2/351). (2) His saying 'as al-Khair al-Ramli stated' and the phrase from which what is mentioned is derived is his saying: 'And the apparent in their expressions is the preponderance of non-liability due to their giving reasoning for it without liability.' And he said it when he was asked about a village whose custom was to send their horses to pasture and that became known among them - does the partner become liable by sending the shared horse or not, due to implied permission? (Muzhir)
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti explains the rules for determining the preferred (rajih) opinion in Hanafi fatwa based on the method of the book. The author opens by distinguishing between 'explicit correction' (tashih sarih) and 'implicit correction' (tashih iltizami). The poetic verse (line 53-56) states: In al-Khaniyah and Multaqa al-Abhar, the first mentioned opinion has merit; in other books, rely on the opinion whose evidence is delayed (i.e., the last mentioned); and if one opinion is given a reasoning (ta'lil) while the other is not, that opinion is preferred. The commentary elaborates: In al-Khaniyah, Imam Qadikhan explicitly states that he begins with the most famous and most apparent opinion, so the first is preferred. The same applies to Multaqa al-Abhar. In other detailed books like al-Hidayah, their custom is to delay the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa and then present his evidence after presenting the evidence of others, which constitutes an implicit preference for his opinion. Even if they do not explicitly say 'the fatwa is on this,' the act of preponderating evidence is a form of correction. The passage then gives two types of implicit correction: (1) presenting the rajih in some books and delaying it in others, and (2) giving ta'lil to the rajih and leaving the marjuh without ta'lil. The author further notes a restriction from al-Nasafi that when three opinions are given, the rajih is either the first or the last, not the middle. However, he cautions that this rule applies only when the author's custom is unknown and no evidences are mentioned; if the custom is known (like in al-Khaniyah), the first is preferred; if evidences are mentioned, the last (i.e., the one whose evidence is given later) is preferred. Finally, he gives a concrete example from al-Hidayah on the issue of weaning (rada'), where Imam Muhammad's opinion (with ta'lil) is preferred over Abu Hanifa's narration because the reason (cutting off growth) is given. Another example from al-Khair al-Ramli's Fatawa on liability for a shared horse illustrates the same principle: when one opinion (non-liability) is given a reasoning, it is preferred over the opposing view (liability) that lacks reasoning. This passage is crucial for a mufti to understand how to extract the correct ruling from Hanafi texts without confusion. The key lesson: the method of each book must be known before determining which opinion is rajih.

Key Terms
التصحيح الصريح (al-tashih al-sarih): Explicit correction: when a book author states directly which opinion is preferred or gives fatwa upon it.
التصحيح الالتزامي (al-tashih al-iltizami): Implicit correction: when preference is inferred from the author's method, such as delaying an opinion or giving ta'lil.
الخانية (al-Khaniyah): Fatawa of Imam Qadikhan (al-Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi), a major Hanafi fatwa collection.
ملتقى الأبحر (Multaqa al-Abhar): A Hanafi fiqh work by Ibrahim al-Halabi, known for presenting the relied-upon opinion first.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani; its method is to delay Imam's opinion and give his evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the two types of implicit correction (tashih iltizami)?
A) Preferring the first opinion and preferring the last opinion
B) Presenting the rajih in some books and delaying it in others, and giving ta'lil to the rajih while leaving the marjuh without ta'lil
C) Explicitly stating which opinion is preferred and providing evidence for it
D) Only using al-Khaniyah and Multaqa al-Abhar for fatwa

Key Takeaway
The method of the book and the presence of ta'lil are the keys to identifying the rajih opinion.

Alfaz al-Tashih: Degrees of Correction Terms
Enumeration and ranking of fatwa-issuing phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to rank the Hanafi correction terms for fatwa and identify which terms indicate the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Fatwa terms (like 'alayhi al-fatwa') are stronger than correctness terms ('sahih'); 'ashah' is stronger than 'sahih' by default.

In this passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, the author lists the various phrases used by Hanafi scholars to indicate that a particular ruling is the operative position for fatwa. Understanding the hierarchy of these terms is critical for a mufti, as the strength of the term determines which ruling should be given in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms listed
Read the matn and commentary to find all the phrases that signal a relied-upon position.
2
Distinguish fatwa terms from correction terms
Notice that phrases containing 'fatwa' (e.g., 'alayhi al-fatwa') are placed above terms like 'sahih' and 'ashah'.
3
Understand the dispute between sahih and ashah
The matn states that ashah is stronger, but a minority says the opposite. Recognize that the majority holds ashah as stronger.
4
Apply the hierarchy in practice
When two conflicting rulings exist, the mufti must look at the terms used: any phrase with fatwa prevails over sahih/ashah; ashah prevails over sahih unless a fatwa term appears.
This is a preponderant preference, not obligatory, as per the commentary.

(٤) قوله : "فلفظ الفتوى" أى اللفظ الذى فيه حروف الفتوى الأصلية بأي صيغة عبر بها . (مظ)

The ruling in which a cause is mentioned is preferable to the ruling in which it is not mentioned; because mentioning its cause indicates concern for it and encouragement. End. -57- And whenever you find two statements and one has been corrected, that is the relied-upon. -58- Like this: 'upon it is the fatwa', 'the most similar', 'the most apparent', 'the chosen', 'the most preponderant', -59- or 'the correct', and 'the more correct' is stronger than it, and it is said the opposite is emphasized. -6- Likewise, 'by it fatwa is given', 'upon it is the fatwa' and these two from all of those are strongest. + Section on the words of correction and their degrees. He said at the end of 'al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya' and at the beginning of 'al-Mudmarat': "As for the signs for ifta: his saying 'upon it is the fatwa' (1), and 'by it fatwa is given', and 'by it we take', and 'upon it is reliance', and 'upon it is the practice today' (2), and 'upon it is the practice of the ummah', and 'it is correct', and 'it is more correct', and 'it is more apparent', and 'it is the chosen in our time', and 'fatwa of our scholars', and 'it is the most similar' (3), and 'it is the most appropriate' (4)
and other phrases mentioned in the text of this book in its place, in the margin of al-Bazdawi. End. And some of these phrases are stronger than others: the phrase 'fatwa' is stronger than the phrase 'correct', 'more correct', 'most similar', and others. And the phrase 'by it fatwa is given' is stronger than the phrase 'chosen'.
(4) His saying: 'it is the most appropriate' means it is more apparent in terms of an aspect because the evidence for it is clearly more apparent than others. (mazh)
(1) His saying: 'and others' like their saying: 'and by it custom has proceeded', 'and it is customary', 'and by it our scholars have taken'. (mazh)
(2) His saying: 'in the margin of al-Bazdawi' – this is in the copy I have. The phrase is not free from some defect and disorder, as appears upon reflection. Perhaps the word 'kadha' has fallen out. Al-Haskafi also mentioned this very same in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and instead of his saying 'in the text of this book etc.' he said: 'and similar to what is mentioned in the margin of al-Bazdawi.' (Athar Husayn al-Ajrarawi) (3) His saying: 'stronger than some' means stronger, so it takes precedence over others, and this precedence is preponderant not obligatory, as benefits from what comes from Sharh al-Munya. (mazh)
(4) His saying: 'so the phrase fatwa' means the word that contains the original letters of fatwa in whatever form it is expressed. (mazh)
(5) His saying: 'stronger than the phrase 'correct' because the opposite of 'correct' or 'more correct' may be the one given fatwa due to being more precautionary, more convenient for people, or in accordance with their practice, and other reasons that the preferrers in the school see as a cause for issuing fatwa. So when they explicitly state the word 'fatwa' in a statement, it is known that it is the taken one. It appears to me that the phrase 'with it we take' and 'upon it is practice' are equal to the phrase 'fatwa', and likewise preferably the phrase 'upon it is the practice of the ummah' because it indicates consensus on it – reflect – as the author mentioned in Radd al-Muhtar. (mazh)
(6) His saying: 'and others' like 'more precautionary' and 'more apparent'. And in al-Diya' al-Ma'nawi: the word 'fatwa' is stronger and more eloquent than the word 'chosen'. (mazh)
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti deals with the hierarchy of terms used to indicate that a particular ruling is the relied-upon position for fatwa. The matn (verses 57-59) sets out key principles: first, that a ruling which explicitly mentions its cause (illa) is preferable to one that does not. Then it lists the terms of correction: when two opinions exist and one is declared 'corrected' (sahhaha), that is the mu'tamad (relied-upon). The terms that follow include 'alayhi al-fatwa', 'al-ashbah', 'al-azhar', 'al-mukhtar', 'al-arjah', 'al-sahih', and 'al-ashah'. The matn further states that 'al-ashah' (more correct) is stronger than 'al-sahih' (correct), but a counter-opinion reverses this. The final line emphasizes that 'al-fatwa' and 'bihi yufta' are the strongest among all.

The commentary expands by listing the detailed phrases collected from al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya and al-Mudmarat. These include: 'alayhi al-fatwa', 'bihi yufta', 'bihi na'khudh', 'alayhi al-i'timad', 'alayhi amal al-yawm', 'alayhi amal al-ummah', 'huwa al-sahih', 'huwa al-ashah', 'huwa al-azhar', 'huwa al-mukhtar fi zamanina', 'fatwa mashayikhina', 'huwa al-ashbah', 'huwa al-awjah'. The commentator explains that some of these terms are stronger than others. Specifically, any phrase containing the word 'fatwa' is stronger than 'sahih', 'ashah', 'ashbah', etc. 'Bihi yufta' is stronger than 'mukhtar'. The editor (mazh) adds further clarifications: 'al-awjah' means the most apparent evidence; 'al-ashbah' means most similar to the explicit text (mansus); the hierarchy is a preferred (rajih) not obligatory; the phrase 'fatwa' is the strongest because it directly indicates the operative position, while 'sahih' may sometimes be abandoned for a contrary fatwa due to need. The editor also notes that 'bihi na'khudh' and 'alayhi al-amal' are equal to 'fatwa', and 'alayhi amal al-ummah' implies consensus.

Key Terms
وعليه الفتوى (wa 'alayhi al-fatwa): Strongest indicator that a ruling is the relied-upon position for fatwa; implies it is the operative verdict
به يفتى (bihi yufta): Equivalent to 'علیه الفتوی' in strength; indicates fatwa is given accordingly
الصحيح (al-sahih): A term meaning 'correct' but may be weaker than 'الفتوى' because a different ruling might be given fatwa due to considerations like ease or custom
الأصح (al-ashah): Comparative form meaning 'more correct'; stronger than sahih in the Hanafi hierarchy
الأشبه (al-ashbah): Meaning 'most similar' to the explicit text; weaker than fatwa terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the strongest phrase indicating the relied-upon position for fatwa?
A) وهو الأصح
B) وهو الصحيح
C) وعليه الفتوى
D) وهو الأشبه

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, phrases like 'alayhi al-fatwa' are the strongest markers of the mufta bihi, outweighing terms of correction like 'sahih' or 'ashah'.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Authenticity vs. Preference: Al-Sahih and Al-Asahh
Terminological rule for mufti's hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'sahih' and 'asahh' in Hanafi fatwa methodology and apply the rule that 'asahh' does not invalidate the opposite opinion.

Core Idea
Al-sahih negates the other; al-asahh affirms it—a mufti may follow the opposite when 'asahh' is used.

This lesson unpacks a critical terminological distinction for the mufti: the difference between 'sahih' (authentic/correct) and 'asahh' (more correct). A mufti who misunderstands these terms may wrongly dismiss valid alternative rulings. We will trace the Hanafi position through key authorities and see how 'asahh' gives latitude in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Recognize 'sahih' as a term that, according to al-Bazdawi, implies exclusivity (the opposite is invalid). 'Asahh' is a comparative form that implies the opposite is also valid, just less preferred.
The core distinction is about whether the opposite ruling retains any validity.
2
State al-Bazdawi's rule
Al-Bazdawi says: 'Sahih requires that other than it is not sahih; asahh requires that other than it is sahih.' This is the foundational Hanafi position.
This rule is explicitly quoted in the source text.
3
Examine hadith scholars' usage
Look at examples from Abu Dawud, al-Suyuti, and others who use 'asahh' for the less weak of two weak narrations. This shows 'asahh' does not mean fully authentic.
These examples are given in the source to support al-Bazdawi's interpretation.
4
Contrast the opposing view
Ibn Abd al-Razzaq cites the majority (jumhur) holding that 'asahh' is stronger than 'sahih' and implies exclusivity. Understand their linguistic argument based on comparative form intensity.
This disagreement is documented in the commentary on al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
5
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon Hanafi position, confirmed by later scholars like al-Bayri and the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar, is that 'asahh' allows the mufti to choose the opposite opinion. The mufta bihi is that 'asahh' does not invalidate the other.
This practical outcome is the key takeaway for fatwa.

Source Text

(تدريب الراوي : ٤٠/١) وقال العلامة ظفر أحمد العثماني رحمه الله تعالى في مقدمة إعلاء السنن: "لا يلزم من قولهم : ليس في الباب شيء أصح من هذا ، صحة الحديث، بل المراد أنه أصح شيء في هذا الباب . قلت : فيجوز أن يكون ضعيفاً ولكنه أمثل من غيره " . وقال الشيخ العلامة عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله تعالى في تعليقاته على هذه المقدمة : " قلت : ومن هذا الاصطلاح أيضًا قول أبي داود في سننه في كتاب الطلاق في باب البتة عقب حديث أورده فيه : " وهذا أصح من حديث ابن جريج " ، قال ابن القيم في تهذيب سنن أبي داود: إن أبا داود لم يحكم بصحته، وإنما قال بعد روايته : " هذا أصح من حديث ابن جريج ، وهذا لا يدل على أن الحديث عنده صحيح ، حديث ابن جريج ،ضعيف، وهذا ضعيف أيضاً ، فهو أصح الضعيفين عنده . وكثيراً ما يطلق أهل الحديث هذه العبارة على أرجح الحديثين الضعيفين، وهو كثير في كلام المتقدمين، ولو لم يكن اصطلاحا لهم، لم تدل اللغة على إطلاق الصحة عليه ؛ فإنك تقول لأحد المريضين : هذا أصح من هذا ، ولا يدل على أنه صحيح مطلقا " .
