الصحيح أكد أو الأصح؟ البزدوي : "قوله : "هو الصحيح يقتضى أن يكون غيره غير صحيح، ولفظ الأصح يقتضى أن يكون غيره صحيحًا . أقول (۱): ينبغي أن يقيد ذلك بالغالب ؛ لأنا وجدنا مقابل الأصح الرواية الشاذة، كما في شرح المجمع " . اهـ . (۱) قوله : "أقول " القائل العلامة البيرى .
Is al-sahih stronger or al-asahh? (Sahih) And as for one who says 'sahih', in his view that other ruling is invalid, so taking what they both agree is sahih is preferable to taking what according to one of them is invalid. End. And the scholar Ibn Abd al-Razzaq mentioned in his commentary on al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'The well-known according to the majority is that al-asahh is stronger than al-sahih.' And in Sharh al-Bayri: 'He said in al-Tiraz al-Madhhab, quoting from a margin note of the Ahl al-Hadith: "This is the most authentic (asahh) thing in the chapter." For their saying this does not necessarily entail the soundness of the referred-to hadith, let alone that the opposing hadith be sound.' Al-Suyuti said: 'The third point relevant to this issue: the restrictive phrase "the most authentic of hadiths" such as saying "the most authentic thing in the chapter is such-and-such." This occurs frequently in Jami' al-Tirmidhi and in Tarikh al-Bukhari and others.' And the author of al-Adhkar said: 'This expression does not necessarily imply the hadith's authenticity, for they say that even if it is weak, and they mean it is more likely or less weak.' (from Tadrib al-Rawi 1/40). And Zafar Ahmad al-Uthmani said in the introduction to I'la al-Sunan: 'Their saying "there is nothing more authentic (asahh) than this in the chapter" does not imply the hadith's authenticity, rather it means it is the most authentic in this chapter. I say: so it may be weak but better than others.' And Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah commented: 'And from this usage is also Abu Dawud's statement in his Sunan in the Book of Divorce, chapter of al-Battah, after a hadith: "This is more authentic (asahh) than the hadith of Ibn Jurayj." Ibn al-Qayyim said in Tahdhib Sunan Abi Dawud: Abu Dawud did not judge it to be authentic, only said that it is more authentic than the hadith of Ibn Jurayj, and this does not indicate that the hadith is authentic according to him. The hadith of Ibn Jurayj is weak, and this is also weak, so it is the more authentic of the two weak ones. The people of hadith often use this expression for the preferable of two weak hadiths, and it is frequent in the speech of the early scholars. If it were not their convention, language would not permit calling it authentic, for you say of one of two sick persons: "this one is healthier (asahh) than this one," and that does not indicate he is completely healthy.' (Qawa'id fi Ulum al-Hadith / Introduction to I'la al-Sunan p.92). (Footnote 1) His statement 'And the scholar Ibn Abd al-Razzaq mentioned' – what the scholar said agrees with al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya and contradicts what is in Sharh al-Munya, Sharh al-Bayri, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. So understand. Is al-sahih stronger or al-asahh? Al-Bazdawi: 'His statement "it is sahih" implies that other than it is not sahih, and the word "asahh" implies that other than it is sahih. I say: this should be qualified by majority, for we find the opposite of asahh is the shadhdh narration, as in Sharh al-Majma'. End.' (Footnote 1) His statement 'I say' – the speaker is the scholar al-Bayri.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a terminological discussion essential for muftis. It addresses the difference between the terms 'sahih' and 'asahh' as used in fiqh and hadith literature. The text first presents a view that 'sahih' implies the contradictory is invalid, so taking the agreed-upon sahih is preferred. Then it cites Ibn Abd al-Razzaq transmitting the majority view that 'asahh' is stronger than 'sahih'. However, numerous quotes from hadith scholars demonstrate that 'asahh' does not necessarily mean fully sahih; it may only indicate relative preference, even among weak narrations. For example, Abu Dawud's statement 'this is asahh than the hadith of Ibn Jurayj' does not prove authenticity, as Ibn al-Qayyim explains that both may be weak, and 'asahh' means the less weak of the two. Al-Bazdawi clarifies that 'sahih' negates the other while 'asahh' affirms the other's validity, though al-Bayri qualifies this as general rule with exceptions. The later part from al-Durr al-Mukhtar and the commentary on it show that the mufti's practical rule is that when a book says 'asahh', he may opt for the opposite, but when it says 'sahih' in an exclusive sense, he cannot.

Key Terms
الصحيح (al-sahih): The correct or authentic ruling/hadith; in this context, a term that (according to some) negates the validity of other opinions.
الأصح (al-asahh): The more correct; a term that indicates preference but does not necessarily invalidate the opposite.
أفعل التفضيل (af'al al-tafdil): The comparative/superlative form (e.g., asahh, awla); used to indicate relative strength without absolute judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, what does the term 'al-asahh' imply about the opposing opinion?
A) It is invalid (fasid).
B) It is also valid (sahih).
C) It is equally strong.
D) It is the only correct opinion.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must understand that 'asahh' is a comparative term that does not invalidate the opposite opinion, providing flexibility in fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Rules for Mufti's Choice Between Tashih Labels
Explains mufti's discretion when rulings are labeled as sahih, asahh, etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the tashih labels 'as-sahih' and 'al-asahh' and apply the rule of mufti's choice when these labels conflict.

Core Idea
'As-sahih' binds the mufti; 'al-asahh' gives discretion to choose either ruling.

This lesson examines a critical methodological rule (dabit) for muftis: how to interpret and apply authoritative tashih labels. When two narrations are corrected with different terms, the mufti must know which rulings are binding and which allow discretion. The passage from the classical texts clarifies the distinction between exclusive correction (as-sahih) and preferential correction (al-asahh), along with the mufti's scope of choice.

Guided Path
1
Define the two key tashih terms
Understand that 'as-sahih' means exclusive correctness (the opposite is incorrect), while 'al-asahh' means more correct but the opposite is still acceptable.
Based on al-Bazdawi's analysis.
2
Determine the mufti's binding vs. discretionary authority based on the label
If the label is 'as-sahih', 'bihi yufta', or similar, the mufti is bound to that ruling unless an equally authoritative source corrects the opposite. If the label is 'al-asahh', 'al-awla', etc., the mufti may choose either ruling.
The passage cites al-Durr al-Mukhtar for this distinction.
3
Identify the exception for conflicting authoritative sources
When two equally reliable books each use a binding label for opposite rulings, the mufti may choose the one he deems stronger, more suitable, and more appropriate.
Example: al-Hidayah says 'as-sahih' for one, al-Kafi says 'as-sahih' for the opposite.
4
Apply the restriction on absolute choice
The mufti's choice is not absolute; it is conditional on the absence of a preponderating factor (murajjih). The author mentions that there are ten such factors to be studied later.
This prevents arbitrary selection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصحيح أكد أو الأصح؟ البزدوي : "قوله : \"هو الصحيح\" يقتضى أن يكون غيره غير صحيح، ولفظ الأصح يقتضى أن يكون غيره صحيحًا . أقول (۱): ينبغي أن يقيد ذلك بالغالب ؛ لأنا وجدنا مقابل الأصح الرواية الشاذة، كما في شرح المجمع \" . اهـ . وفي \"الدر المختار\" بعد نقله حاصل ما مر : \"ثم رأيت في رسالة آداب المفتين (۲) - : إذا ذيلت (۳) رواية في كتاب معتمد بالأصح، أو الأولى، أو الأرفق، ونحوها، فله أن يفتى بها وبمخالفتها أيضا أيا شاء. وإذا ذيلت بالصحيح، أو المأخوذ به، أو به يفتى أو عليه الفتوى، لم يفت بمخالفها، إلا إذا كان في \"الهداية (۱) مثلا \" هو الصحيح\" وفي \"الكافي \" بمخالفه هو الصحيح، فيخير، فيختار الأقوى (۲) عنده، والأليق (۳)، والأصلح. اهـ . فليحفظ . مطلب حاصل ضابطة التصحيح سبعة أمور قلـت : وحاصل هذا كله ١ - أنه إذا صحح كل من الروايتين بلفظ واحد كأن ذكر في كل واحدة منهما هو الصحيح ، أو الأصح ، أو به يفتى - تخير المفتى ۲ - وإذا اختلف اللفظ ، فإن كان أحدهما لفظ الفتوى، فهو أولى ؛ لأنه لا يفتى إلا بما هو صحيح وليس كل صحیح یفتی به ؛ لأن الصحيح في نفسه قد لا يفتى به ؛ لكون غيره أوفق لتغيّر الزمان وللضرورة، ونحو ذلك . ، فما فيه لفظ الفتوى يتضمن شيئين: أحدهما: الإذن بالفتوى به، والآخر الصحة. ٣ - ثم اعلم أن قولهم : \"فالخيار للمفتى\" ليس على إطلاقه، بل هو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن لأحد القولين مرجح قبل التصحيح أو ،بعده والمرجحات عشرة سيذكرها المصنف .
[Question:] Is 'as-sahih' more emphatic or 'al-asahh'? Al-Bazdawi said: 'His statement "huwa as-sahih" requires that something else is not sahih, while the word al-asahh requires that something else is sahih.' I (the commentator) say: It should be qualified by the majority; for we have found in contrast to al-asahh the rare transmission, as in Sharh al-Majma'. End. In al-Durr al-Mukhtar after quoting the summary of what passed: 'Then I saw in the treatise Adab al-Muftin: When a narration in a reliable book is annotated with al-asahh, or al-awla, or al-arfaq, and the like, the mufti may give fatwa with it and with its opposite as he wishes. And when it is annotated with as-sahih, or al-ma'khudh bihi, or bihi yufta, or 'alayhi al-fatwa, he does not give fatwa contrary to it, except if in al-Hidayah for example it says "huwa as-sahih" and in al-Kafi the opposite is stated as sahih, then he has a choice: he chooses the stronger in his view, the more suitable, and the most appropriate. End. So preserve it. Section: Summary of the Rule of Tashih - Seven Matters. I said: The summary of all this: 1. If each of the two narrations is corrected with the same word, such as both being said to be as-sahih or al-asahh or bihi yufta, the mufti has a choice. 2. If the wording differs, and one of them is the wording of fatwa, it is preferable because fatwa is only given with what is sahih, and not every sahih is given fatwa with, because the sahih in itself may not be given fatwa due to something else being more suitable due to change of time or necessity, etc. So what contains the wording of fatwa includes two things: permission to give fatwa with it and soundness. 3. Then know that their statement 'the mufti has a choice' is not absolute, but restricted to when there is no preponderating factor for either statement before or after the tashih, and the preponderating factors are ten which the author will mention.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (dabit) for muftis regarding how to deal with conflicting rulings that have been authoritatively corrected (tashih) by different scholars. It begins by addressing the difference between the terms 'as-sahih' and 'al-asahh' as analyzed by al-Bazdawi. 'As-sahih' implies exclusivity—only this ruling is correct, while its opposite is incorrect. 'Al-asahh' (more correct) implies that the opposite is also correct, but this one is more correct. The commentator notes that this general rule is subject to exceptions; sometimes the opposite of 'al-asahh' is a rare (shadhdh) narration. The passage then quotes from al-Durr al-Mukhtar, which cites a treatise on the etiquette of muftis. It states that if a narration is annotated with terms like 'al-asahh', 'al-awla', or 'al-arfaq', the mufti may choose to give fatwa with either that narration or its opposite because these terms do not invalidate the opposite. However, if the annotation uses 'as-sahih', 'al-ma'khudh bihi', 'bihi yufta', or ''alayhi al-fatwa', then the mufti is bound to that ruling and cannot give fatwa contrary to it. An exception is when two equally authoritative sources differ—e.g. al-Hidayah says 'as-sahih' for one, and al-Kafi says 'as-sahih' for the opposite—then the mufti may choose between them, preferring the stronger proof and what is suitable for his time and people. The passage then provides a concise summary of seven points, though only the first three are fully stated here. The remaining points (4-7) will follow later. The key principle: the mufti's choice is not absolute; it is conditional on the absence of any preponderating factor (murajjih). The author mentions that there are ten such factors to be discussed later. This is a crucial rule for a mufti's practice, ensuring that fatwa is given with proper authority and without issuing weak or rejected rulings.

Key Terms
الصحيح (as-sahih): A term of tashih implying that this specific ruling is correct and its opposite is not correct (exclusive correction).
الأصح (al-asahh): A term of tashih implying that this ruling is more correct, but its opposite is still considered correct (non-exclusive correction).
به يفتى (bihi yufta): A phrase meaning 'by it fatwa is given', indicating that this is the operative ruling for fatwa, similar in effect to 'as-sahih' in restricting the mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a ruling in a reliable book is annotated with 'al-asahh', what is the mufti's option regarding the opposite ruling?
A) He may not give fatwa with the opposite under any circumstances.
B) He may give fatwa with the opposite only if no other source corrects it.
C) He may give fatwa with either the annotated ruling or its opposite as he wishes.
D) He must prefer the annotated ruling and cannot give fatwa with the opposite.

Key Takeaway
The label 'as-sahih' restricts the mufti, 'al-asahh' allows discretion, and the mufti's choice is always subject to preponderating factors.

The Sequential Rules of Tashih Preference
Explaining the priority rules for conflicting tashih labels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the four sequential rules of tashih preference to determine which ruling a mufti should select when faced with conflicting authentication labels.

Core Idea
Not every 'sahih' is fit for fatwa; 'bihi yufata' is the key that unlocks operational authorization.

When a mufti opens two Hanafi books and finds different rulings both labeled correct, he cannot simply pick one arbitrarily. The Hanafi usul al-iftaa provides a clear hierarchy of preference based on the wording used. This lesson guides you through the four rules summarized in the hasil dabt al-tashih, transforming a confusing set of labels into a structured decision tree.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the General Duty to Follow a Tashih Label
Identify in the passage the baseline rule: if a ruling is labeled 'sahih', 'ma'khudh bihi', 'bihi yufata', or 'alayhi al-fatwa', the mufti must not give fatwa contrary to it. Note the strictness of this starting principle.
The exception comes when two different books authenticate opposite rulings.
2
Identify the Exception: Two Books Contradict
Understand that when, for example, al-Hidayah says 'it is sahih' and al-Kafi says the opposite is sahih, the mufti is no longer bound. He now has a choice, but must select the strongest, most fitting, and most suitable.
This exception only applies across different books.
3
Apply Rule 1: Same Wording in Both Sources
If both narrations are authenticated with the same term (e.g., both say 'it is sahih' or both 'the correct view'), the mufti has a free choice between them.
Sameness of wording eliminates any built-in priority.
4
Apply Rule 2: Fatwa Wording vs. Other Wording
If the wordings differ, the one containing fatwa language (bihi yufata or alayhi al-fatwa) is automatically preferred because it implies both correctness and permission to act.
This is because fatwa wording grants operational authorization, unlike mere theoretical correctness.
5
Apply Rule 3: Both Use Fatwa Wording
When both rulings come with fatwa terms, look for additional strength: if one uses a restrictive phrase (e.g., 'the fatwa is given by it' alone) or a consensus-indicating phrase (e.g., 'upon it is the practice of the Ummah'), that one is preferred.
Consensus phrasing is even stronger than simple fatwa wording.
6
Apply Rule 4: Sahih vs. Asahh When No Fatwa Wording
If neither ruling uses fatwa language, and one says 'asahh' and the other 'sahih', a known disagreement exists over which is stronger. But if both corrections appear in the same book, then 'asahh' is unanimously preferred.
This rule is a bridge to the next lesson on the sahih vs asahh dispute.

Source Text

مطلب
حاصل ضابطة التصحيح سبعة أمور
قلت : وحاصل هذا كله
1 - أنه إذا صحح كل من الروايتين بلفظ واحد كأن ذكر في كل واحدة منهما هو الصحيح ، أو الأصح ، أو به يفتى - تخير المفتى (4) 2 - وإذا اختلف اللفظ ، فإن كان أحدهما لفظ الفتوى، فهو أولى ؛ لأنه لا يفتى إلا بما هو صحيح وليس كل صحیح یفتی به ؛ لأن الصحيح في نفسه قد لا يفتى به ؛ لكون غيره أوفق لتغيّر الزمان وللضرورة، ونحو ذلك . فما فيه لفظ الفتوى يتضمن شيئين: أحدهما: الإذن بالفتوى به، والآخر صحته ؛ لأن الإفتاء به تصحيح له، بخلاف ما فيه لفظ الصحيح، أو الأصح مثلا.
- وإن كان لفظ الفتوى فى كل منهما : فإن كان أحدهما يفيد الحصر مثل به يفتى أو عليه الفتوى، فهو الأولى. ومثله بل أولى لفظ "عليه عمل الأمة" ؛ لأنه يفيد الإجماع.
4 - وإن لم يكن لفظ الفتوى فى واحد منهما : فإن كان أحدهما بلفظ الأصح ، والآخر بلفظ الصحيح، فعلى الخلاف السابق (1).
لكن هذا (2) فيما إذا كان التصحيحان في كتابين، أما لو كانا (3) في كتاب واحد، فالأصح مقدم باتفاق.
Summary of the rule of correction: By 'sahih', or 'the taken (opinion)', or 'by it fatwa is given', or 'upon it is the fatwa', one does not give fatwa contrary to it, unless for example in 'al-Hidayah' it says 'it is sahih' and in 'al-Kafi' its contrary is sahih, then he chooses, selecting the strongest in his view, the most fitting, and the most suitable. End. So memorize. Section: Summary of the rule of correction: seven matters. I say: The summary of all this: 1. If each of the two narrations is authenticated with the same wording, such that each one states 'it is sahih' or 'asahh' or 'by it fatwa is given', then the mufti has a choice. 2. If the wording differs, and one of them is the wording of fatwa, then it is preferable, because one only gives fatwa with what is sahih, and not every sahih is given fatwa with; because the sahih in itself may not be given fatwa with due to another being more in harmony with changing times, necessity, and the like. So what contains the wording of fatwa implies two things: one is permission to give fatwa with it, and the other is its correctness; because giving fatwa with it is a correction for it, unlike what contains the wording 'sahih' or 'asahh' for example. 3. If the wording of fatwa is in each of them, then if one of them indicates restriction, like 'by it fatwa is given' or 'upon it is the fatwa', it is preferable. Similarly, even more so, the wording 'upon it is the practice of the Ummah', because it indicates consensus. 4. If there is no wording of fatwa in either of them, and one of them is with the wording 'asahh' and the other with 'sahih', then the previous difference applies. However, this is when the two corrections are in two books; if they are in one book, then 'asahh' is given precedence by agreement.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (dabt) from the Hanafi usul al-iftaa tradition, summarizing how a mufti should navigate conflicting authentication labels. The 'hasil dabt al-tashih' consolidates the earlier discussion into a list of seven matters, of which four are detailed here. The core principle is that the mufti must adhere to a ruling labeled as 'sahih', 'ma'khudh bihi', 'bihi yufata', or 'alayhi al-fatwa', unless a specific exception arises. The exception occurs when two different books authenticate opposing rulings; then the mufti chooses the strongest, most fitting, and most suitable. The passage then lists the rules: (1) If both narrations are authenticated with the same term (e.g., both 'sahih'), the mufti has a free choice. (2) If the terms differ, the one using 'fatwa' terminology is preferable because it implies both permission to give fatwa and the correctness of the ruling. (3) If both use fatwa wording, the one that indicates restriction or consensus takes precedence. (4) If neither uses fatwa wording, and one says 'asahh' and the other 'sahih', there is a scholarly disagreement over which is stronger; this is discussed later. However, if both corrections are in the same book, then 'asahh' is unanimously preferred. The footnote explains that the dispute about 'sahih' vs 'asahh' depends on whether the two corrections are from different imams or the same. In practice, the mufti must consider the strength of evidence and contextual appropriateness.

Key Terms
التصحيح (al-tashih): The act of declaring a ruling as correct (sahih) or preferred for fatwa
به يفتى (bihi yufata): A phrase indicating that a particular ruling is the one authoritatively given as fatwa
الصحيح (al-sahih): A ruling deemed correct in itself, but not necessarily the one used for fatwa
الأصح (al-asahh): A comparative/superlative form meaning 'more correct' or 'most correct'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hasil dabt al-tashih, if one source says 'هو الصحيح' and another says 'به يفتى', which is preferred?
A) The one with 'به يفتى' because it implies both correctness and permission
B) The one with 'هو الصحيح' because it is more definitive
C) Both are equally preferred, and the mufti chooses
D) Neither is preferred; one must ask a senior scholar

Key Takeaway
A mufti must learn to read the hierarchy in tas-hih labels: fatwa wording overrides mere 'sahih' or 'asahh', and in a single book, 'asahh' trumps 'sahih'.

Prioritizing Conflicting Tasheeh Statements
Rules for a mufti when choosing between differing tasheeh statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of conflicting tashih statements to determine the preferable ruling and justify the preference based on the madhhab's methodology.

Core Idea
When tasheeh statements conflict, the mufti prefers exclusive fatwa phrases, then 'al-asahh', then the more knowledgeable imam.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, a mufti often encounters different statements indicating that a particular ruling is 'correct' (sahih) or 'more correct' (asahh). This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti lays down a clear hierarchy for prioritizing such tashih statements. By mastering these rules, you will be able to navigate conflicting corrections and issue fatwas with confidence, following the established methodology of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tashih phrase
Look for explicit phrases like 'bihi yuffta', 'alayhi al-fatwa', 'al-asahh', 'as-sahih', 'al-ahwat', 'al-awla', or 'al-arfaq'. Each has a different weight.
Also note if the phrase is 'alayhi amal al-ummah' which implies consensus.
2
Check for exclusive fatwa language
If one side uses an exclusive fatwa phrase ('bihi yuffta', 'alayhi al-fatwa'), that side is preferable. If it uses 'alayhi amal al-ummah', it is even stronger.
Exclusive fatwa phrases indicate the established practice.
3
Apply the rule for 'al-asahh' vs 'as-sahih'
If neither side has fatwa language, the mufti must weigh 'al-asahh' against 'as-sahih'. The relied-upon view is that 'al-asahh' is stronger because it is a superlative.
This dispute only applies when the corrections come from different imams and involve different opinions.
4
Consider the source authority
If one correction comes from a more knowledgeable imam (e.g., Qadikhan vs. author of al-Bazzaziyya), his tashih is preferred regardless of wording.
The rank of the imam is a factor when imams are of different levels.
5
Determine the mufti's choice when equal
If both corrections are from equal-ranking imams and both use 'al-asahh' or 'as-sahih', the mufti may choose. But it is better to take the one explicitly marked as 'al-asahh' or with a superlative.
If one is explicit and the other silent, the explicit one is preferred.

لكن هذا (۲) فيما إذا كان التصحيحان في كتابين، أما لو كانا (۳) في
(۱) قوله : فعلى الخلاف السابق " حاصله : أن عند بعضهم الأصح أقوى من الصحيح؛ لأنه اسم التفضيل ، وقال آخرون : الصحيح أقوى من الأصح؛ لأن الصحيح مقابله الخطأ، والأصح مقابله الصحيح، وما كان مقابله خطأ أكد مما كان مقابله صحيحاً. والراجح الأول ؛ لأن صيغة اسم التفضيل يفيد زيادة المادة، وأما قولهم: "الصحيح مقابله الخطأ " فليس على الإطلاق كما أن قولهم : "الأصح مقابله الصحيح ليس على إطلاقه، فقد وجدنا مقابل الصحيح صحيحا ومقابل الأصح رواية ضعيفة، فهذا اصطلاح لهم ويريدون به نحو ما يريده المحدثون بقولهم : هذا أصح ما جاء في الباب " ؛ فإنه لا يكون ذلك حكمًا منهم بصحة الحديث، بل كثيراً ما يطلقونه على أرجح الحديثين الضعيفين، فهذا قريب منه ، وقد مر الكلام عليه مفصلا فراجعه .

Summary of the rule of correction:

Its correctness; because issuing fatwa by it is a correction of it, unlike what contains the word 'as-sahih' or 'al-asahh' for example.

- And if the word 'fatwa' occurs in each of them: if one of them implies exclusivity such as 'bihi yufta' or 'alayhi al-fatwa', then it is preferable. And similarly, rather more preferable, is the phrase 'alayhi amal al-ummah' because it implies consensus. 4- And if the word 'fatwa' is not in either of them: if one of them uses 'al-asahh' and the other 'as-sahih', then the previous disagreement applies (1).
But this (2) applies when the two corrections are in two books; as for if they are (3) in one book from one imam, then the disagreement about preferring 'al-asahh' over 'as-sahih' does not arise; because the implication of 'as-sahih' that its opposite is invalid does not apply after stating that its opposite is 'asahh', unless there is a third opinion which is the invalid one. Similarly, if two corrections are mentioned from two imams then he says that the second correction is 'asahh' than the first, then there is no doubt that his intention is to prefer what he expressed as 'asahh', and this occurs frequently in the correction of Allamah Qasim.

- And if each of them is with the word 'al-asahh' or 'as-sahih', there is no doubt that he may choose between them if the two imams who corrected are of equal rank.
6- But if one of them is more knowledgeable, then he chooses his correction, like if one is in 'al-Khaniyya' and the other in 'al-Bazzaziyya' - for example; then the correction of Qadikhan is stronger, for Allamah Qasim said: Qadikhan is among those most entitled to rely on his correction. - And similarly he may choose (1) if only one of them is explicitly corrected with the word 'al-asahh', or 'al-ahwat', or 'al-awla', or 'al-arfaq', and is silent about the correction of the other; for this wording implies the validity of the other, but it is better to take what is explicitly stated as 'al-asahh' because of its increased correctness.
-
Similarly, if one explicitly states 'al-asahh' and the other 'as-sahih', then by 'al-asahh', and it is better to take 'al-asahh'.
(1) His statement: 'And similarly he may choose' is coordinated with his statement: 'there is no doubt that he may choose between them', and his statement: 'And similarly if he explicitly states' is coordinated with this coordinated phrase. The meaning: if the correction is in the form of the superlative, and he is silent about the correction of the other, or he explicitly corrects it but not in the superlative form, then the mufti has a choice, but it is better to take what is corrected with the superlative form because it indicates increased substance.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti continues the discussion of 'Dabit al-Tashih' (the rule of correction). The author presents a series of rules for a mufti when he encounters conflicting statements of tashih (correction) in the Hanafi madhhab. The passage type is a rasm rule: a methodological rule for issuing fatwas. The author begins by stating a general principle: issuing a fatwa based on a particular ruling is itself a tashih (correction) of that ruling, unlike merely using the word 'as-sahih' or 'al-asahh'. This means that when a later scholar issues a fatwa on a view, it effectively confirms that view. Then, the author discusses cases where the word 'fatwa' appears on both sides. If one side uses an exclusive phrase like 'bi hi yuffta' (by it fatwa is given) or 'alayhi al-fatwa' (upon it is the fatwa), that side is preferable. Even more preferable is the phrase 'alayhi amal al-ummah' (upon it is the practice of the ummah) because it implies ijma (consensus). Fourthly, if neither uses 'fatwa', then the dispute arises between 'al-asahh' and 'as-sahih'. The commentary explains that some hold 'al-asahh' stronger (because it is a superlative), others hold 'as-sahih' stronger (because its opposite is clear error). The relied-upon position (ar-rajih) is the first: 'al-asahh' is stronger due to the superlative form. This disagreement, however, only applies when the two corrections come from different imams and involve different opinions. If the same imam corrects, or if it is about preferring one tashih over another tashih, then 'al-asahh' is agreed to be stronger. The author then states a fifth rule: if both are with 'al-asahh' or 'as-sahih' from imams of equal rank, the mufti can choose. Sixth: if one of the imams is more knowledgeable (e.g., Qadikhan vs. the author of al-Bazzaziyya), his tashih is preferred. Finally, if only one is explicitly corrected with a superlative (al-asahh, al-ahwat, al-awla, al-arfaq) and the other is silent, the mufti may choose but it is better to follow the explicit one due to increased correctness. The same applies when one is 'al-asahh' and the other is 'as-sahih': the mufti may choose but it is better to take 'al-asahh'. The commentary clarifies that the choice exists when the correction uses a superlative form while the other is either silent or corrected with a non-superlative form.

Key Terms
تصحيح (tasḥīḥ): The act of declaring a particular opinion or narration as correct (sahih) within the Hanafi madhhab.
الأصح (al-aṣaḥḥ): A term used to indicate that a particular ruling is more correct than another correct ruling.
الصحيح (al-ṣaḥīḥ): A term indicating that a ruling is correct, without explicit comparison.
به يفتى (bihi yufftā): An exclusive fatwa phrase meaning 'by it fatwa is given', indicating that this is the operative ruling.
عليه الفتوى (ʿalayhi al-fatwā): Another exclusive fatwa phrase meaning 'upon it is the fatwa'.
عليه عمل الأمة (ʿalayhi ʿamal al-ummah): A phrase meaning 'upon it is the practice of the Ummah', implying consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when one authority states 'al-asahh' and another states 'as-sahih', and both corrections are from different imams in different books, what should the mufti do?
A) Prefer the one with 'as-sahih' because it is absolute.
B) Prefer the one with 'al-asahh' because it indicates a higher degree of correctness.
C) He may choose either, but 'as-sahih' is more reliable.
D) He must follow the later scholar's opinion.

Key Takeaway
When conflicting tashih statements arise, the mufti follows a hierarchy: exclusive fatwa phrases, then 'al-asahh' over 'as-sahih', then the more knowledgeable imam, and if all equal, he may choose but prefers the explicit superlative.

Rules for Preferring One Tas-heeh Over Another
Rules for the mufti when facing conflicting authoritative corrections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for preferring one authoritative correction (tas-hih) over another when encountering conflicting rulings within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
'Asahh' beats 'sahih', but other factors like imam's rank and explicit preponderators also decide the mufti's choice.

A mufti often faces two or more authoritative corrections (tas-hih) for the same issue. This lesson introduces the criteria for choosing between them. The source passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti provides the hierarchy: from wording (asahh vs sahih) to the scholar's rank and additional preponderators like consensus and benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two tas-hih and their wording
Check whether the tas-hih uses 'asahh' (more correct) or 'sahih' (correct). This is the first preponderator.
If both are same wording, proceed to the next steps.
2
Determine if they come from the same book of the same imam
If yes, there is no real conflict: 'asahh' automatically outweighs 'sahih', unless a third invalid opinion exists.
From the same imam, the 'asahh' is clearly preferred.
3
If from different imams, compare their rank
If one imam is more knowledgeable, his tas-hih is chosen. For example, Qadikhan's tas-hih is considered stronger.
If both imams are equal in rank, the mufti may choose freely when wording is the same.
4
Apply additional preponderators from the poem
If conflict remains, consider: consensus (fatwa is given with it), appearance in the authoritative texts (mutun), imam's own statement, istihsan, benefit for endowments, suitability for the time, or clarity of proof.
These preponderators tip the scale when wording alone does not decide.
5
Formulate the mufta bihi
Synthesize the above steps to determine the operative ruling for fatwa.
Document the reasoning using the hierarchy.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاصل ضابطة التصحيح: كتاب واحد من إمام واحد، فلا يتأتى الخلاف في تقديم الأصح على الصحيح؛ لأن إشعار الصحيح بأن مقابله فاسد لا يتأتى فيه بعد التصريح بأن مقابله أصح، إلا إذا كان في المسألة قول ثالث يكون هو الفاسد. وكذا لو ذكر تصحيحين عن إمامين ثم قال: إن هذا التصحيح الثاني أصح من الأول مثلا، فإنه لا شك أن مراده ترجيح ما عبر عنه بكونه أصح، ويقع ذلك كثيراً في تصحيح العلامة قاسم. وإن كان كل منهما بلفظ الأصح أو الصحيح، فلا شبهة في أنه يتخيّر بينهما إذا كان الإمامان المصححان في رتبة واحدة. أما لو كان أحدهما أعلم فإنه يختار تصحيحه، كما لو كان أحدهما في "الخانية" والآخر في "البزازية" - مثلا -؛ فإن تصحيح قاضيخان أقوى، فقد قال العلامة قاسم: إن قاضيخان من أحق من يعتمد على تصحيحه. وكذا يتخيّر إذا صرح بتصحيح إحداهما فقط بلفظ الأصح، أو الأحوط، أو الأولى، أو الأرفق، وسكت عن تصحيح الأخرى؛ فإن هذا اللفظ يفيد صحة الأخرى، لكن الأولى الأخذ بما صرح بأنها الأصح؛ لزيادة صحتها. وكذا لو صرح في إحداهما بالأصح، وفي الأخرى بالصحيح، فإن الأولى الأخذ بالأصح. [ثم النظم:] وَإِنْ تَجد تصحيح قولين ورد فَاخْتَر لما شئتَ فَكُلُّ مُعْتَمَدْ - إلا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحًا وَأَصَحَ أو قِيلَ ذَا يُفْتَى بِهِ فَقَدْ رُجح - أوْ كَانَ فِي المُتونِ أوْ قَوْلَ الإِمَامِ أَوْ ظَاهِرَ المَرْوِى أو جُلَ العِظَامِ - قَالَ بِهِ ، أَوْ كَانَ الاسْتِحْسَانَا أَوْ زَادَ للأوقاف نَفْعًا بَانَا - أَوْ كَانَ ذَا أَوْفَقَ للزَّمَانُ أَوْ كَانَ ذَا أَوضَحَ فِي البُرْهَانَ - هَذَا إِذَا تَعَارَضَ التَصْحِيحُ أو لَمْ يَكُنْ أَصْلا بِه تَصْرِيح - فَتَاحُدُ الّذى لَهُ مُرَبِّعٌ مِمَّا عَلِمْتَهُ فَهَذَا الأوضَحْ. [ثم شرح:] لما ذكرت علامات التصحيح لقول من الأقوال، وأن بعض ألفاظ التصحيح أكد من بعض، وهذا إنما تظهر ثمرته عند التعارض بأن كان التصحيح لقولين - فصلتُ ذلك تفصيلا حسنًا لم أسبق إليه، أخذا مما مهدته قبل هذا وذلك أن قولهم: "إذا كان في المسألة قولان مصححان، فالمفتى بالخيار - ليس على إطلاقه، بل ذاك إذا لم يكن لأحدهما مرجح قبل التصحيح أو بعده . الأول من المرجحات : ما إذا كان تصحيح أحدهما بلفظ الصحيح، والآخر بلفظ الأصح، وتقدّم الكلام فيه، وأن المشهور ترجيح الأصح على الصحيح.
Summary of the rule of tas-hih: From one book of one imam, there is no room for disagreement in giving precedence to the asahh over the sahih; because the implication of sahih that its opposite is invalid does not occur after stating that its opposite is asahh, unless there is a third opinion in the matter that is the invalid one. Similarly, if he mentions two tas-hihs from two imams and then says: 'This second tas-hih is more correct (asahh) than the first,' then there is no doubt that his intent is to prefer what he expressed as asahh, and this occurs frequently in the tas-hih of Allama Qasim. And if each of them is expressed with the wording asahh or sahih, then there is no doubt that he may choose between them if the two imams who made the tas-hih are of the same rank. But if one of them is more knowledgeable, then he chooses his tas-hih, as if one is in al-Khaniyyah and the other in al-Bazzaziyyah – for example – then the tas-hih of Qadikhan is stronger, as Allama Qasim said: 'Qadikhan is among the most deserving of reliance on his tas-hih.' And similarly, he may choose if he explicitly declares the tas-hih of one of them only with the wording asahh, or ahwat, or awla, or arfaq, and remains silent about the tas-hih of the other; for this wording indicates the correctness of the other, but it is better to take what he explicitly declared as asahh, due to its increased correctness. And similarly, if he explicit in one with asahh and in the other with sahih, then it is better to take the asahh. [Then the poem:] If you find tas-hih of two statements that have come, then choose whatever you wish, for each is relied upon – except when they are sahih and asahh, or it is said 'this is the one given fatwa with' – then it has been given preference – or if it is in the texts, or the imam's statement, or the apparent of that which is narrated, or the great ones – said by it – or if it is istihsan, or it brings more benefit for endowments – or if it is more suitable for the time, or it is clearer in proof – this is when the tas-hih are in conflict, or there is no original explicit statement regarding it – then follow the one that has a qualifier from what you have learned, and this is the clearest. [Then commentary:] When I mentioned the signs of tas-hih for any statement, and that some wordings of tas-hih are more emphatic than others, the fruit of this only appears when there is conflict, where there is tas-hih of two statements – I explained that in a good detail not done before, taking from what I laid out before this. That is because their statement: 'If there are two authoritative statements in a matter, the mufti has the choice' is not unconditional, but rather that is when there is no preponderance for one of them before or after the tas-hih. The first of the preponderators: when the tas-hih of one is with the wording sahih and the other with asahh, and the discussion preceded it, and that the well-known view is to prefer asahh over sahih.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti discusses the rules for a mufti when he encounters two 'tas-hih' – authoritative corrections or endorsements – of different rulings, particularly when they appear to conflict. The author begins by summarizing a key principle: if both tas-hihs come from the same book of a single imam, there is no real conflict, because designating one as 'asahh' (more correct) implicitly prioritizes it over the other, which is simply 'sahih' (correct). The only exception is if a third opinion exists that is actually invalid. If the tas-hihs come from two different imams, and one of them explicitly says the second is more correct, then clearly the more correct one is preferred. When both are expressed with the same wording (both asahh or both sahih) and the imams are of equal rank, the mufti may choose. But if one imam is more knowledgeable, his tas-hih should be chosen. For instance, Qadikhan's tas-hih is given more weight than that of others due to his expertise. The mufti also has a choice if only one tas-hih is explicitly labeled as ‘asahh’ while the other is left unlabeled; however, it is better to choose the explicitly stronger one. When one is labeled ‘asahh’ and the other ‘sahih’, the asahh is again preferable. The poem (lines 61-67) enumerates additional preponderators: when one statement is recognized by consensus as the one given fatwa; when it appears in the authoritative texts (mutun) or is the imam's own statement; when it is istihsan; when it brings more benefit for endowments; when it is more suitable for the time or clearer in proof. The commentary then clarifies that the general rule of free choice applies only when there is no preponderating factor before or after the tas-hih. The first and most common preponderator is the difference between 'sahih' and 'asahh', with the latter taking precedence, especially when from the same imam's book; from different imams, the well-known view is to prefer 'asahh' as well.

Key Terms
تصحيح (tas-hīh): An authoritative correction or endorsement of a legal opinion, declaring it to be the correct or preferred view.
أصح (aṣaḥḥ): A term meaning 'more correct' or 'most correct', used to designate one of two or more corrected opinions as superior.
صحيح (ṣaḥīḥ): A term meaning 'correct' or 'sound', used for a corrected opinion that is less emphatic than 'asahh'.
معتمد (muʿtamad): Relied upon; a legal opinion that is authoritative and can be used to issue fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two tas-hih are found for a ruling, one labeled 'sahih' and the other 'asahh' in the same book by the same imam, what is the mufti's preferred course of action?
A) He may choose either freely.
B) He should prefer the 'asahh' because it gives a stronger indication of correctness.
C) He should prefer the 'sahih' because it is more established.
D) He should reject both and seek a third opinion.

Key Takeaway
When facing conflicting tas-hih, the mufti must apply preponderators: wording (asahh > sahih), imam's rank, and additional factors like consensus or textual authority, rather than rely on free choice.

Ten Rules for Preponderance (Tarjih) When Corrected Statements Conflict
Ten preponderance rules for conflicting tasheeh, with poetic summary and prose explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten preponderance factors for conflicting tasheeh and apply them to resolve a mufti's choice between two corrected rulings.

Core Idea
When two statements are both corrected, the mufti does not choose freely — preponderance rules break the tie.

In Hanafi iftaa, a mufti often encounters multiple 'corrected' positions on a single issue. While it was once said that he may choose any, this lesson reveals that scholars have developed ten clear factors to determine which correction prevails. Mastery of these rules distinguishes a precise mufti from a mere follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two corrected statements
Begin by confirming that both statements have been explicitly tagged with tasheeh (e.g., 'sahih', 'asah', 'al-fatwa', or similar). If not, the rules for conflicting corrections may not apply directly.
The passage assumes both have been corrected.
2
Check for linguistic strength: 'asah' vs 'sahih'
If one is labeled 'asah' and the other 'sahih', the former is given precedence. This is the first and most basic rule.
The well-known view prefers 'asah' over 'sahih'.
3
Check for the 'fatwa' indicator
If one statement is accompanied by the phrase 'upon this is the fatwa', that statement is preferred over one without such a label.
This rule comes second, after the linguistic strength.
4
Check if the statement appears in the mutun (core texts)
A statement found in the authoritative mutun (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Hidayah) takes precedence over one in commentaries or fatwa collections, even if both are corrected.
The mutun are the primary transmission of the madhhab.
5
Consider other factors in order
Apply remaining rules: statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, istihsan, benefit for endowments, suitability for the time, clarity of proof, etc. If no factor breaks the tie, the mufti has a choice.
The commentary suggests these are applied sequentially.

Source Text

شرح عقود رسم المفتی

مطلب في قواعد الترجيح عند تعارض التصحيح وتلك عشرة

٦١ - وَإِنْ تَجد تصحيح قولين ورد فَاخْتَر لما شئتَ فَكُلُّ مُعْتَمَدْ
٦٢ - إلا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحًا وَأَصَحَ أو قِيلَ ذَا يُفْتَى بِهِ فَقَدْ رُجح
٦٣- أوْ كَانَ فِي المُتونِ أوْ قَوْلَ الإِمَامِ أَوْ ظَاهِرَ المَرْوِى أو جُلَ العِظَامِ
٦٤ - قَالَ بِهِ ، أَوْ كَانَ الاسْتِحْسَانَا أَوْ زَادَ للأوقاف: أوْ زَادَ للأوقاف نَفْعًا بَانَا
٦٥ - أَوْ كَانَ ذَا أَوْفَقَ للزَّمَانُ أَوْ كَانَ ذَا أَوضَحَ فِي البُرْهَانَ
٦٦ - هَذَا إِذَا تَعَارَضَ التَصْحِيحُ أو لَمْ يَكُنْ أَصْلا بِه تَصْرِيح
٦٧- فَتَاحُدُ الّذى لَهُ مُرَبِّعٌ مِمَّا عَلِمْتَهُ فَهَذَا الأوضَحْ
لما ذكرت علامات التصحيح لقول من الأقوال، وأن بعض ألفاظ التصحيح أكد من بعض، وهذا إنما تظهر ثمرته عند التعارض بأن كان التصحيح لقولين - فصلتُ ذلك تفصيلا حسنًا لم أسبق إليه ، أخذا مما مهدته قبل هذا وذلك أن قولهم: "إذا كان في المسألة قولان مصححان، فالمفتى بالخيار - ليس على إطلاقه، بل ذاك إذا لم يكن لأحدهما مرجح قبل التصحيح أو بعده . الأول من المرجحات : ما إذا كان تصحيح أحدهما بلفظ الصحيح، والآخر بلفظ الأصح، وتقدّم الكلام فيه، وأن المشهور ترجيح الأصح على الصحيح
(1)
الثاني : ما إذا كان أحدهما بلفظ الفتوى، والآخر بغيره (2) كما تقدم بيانه .
الثالث : ما إذا كان أحد القولين المصححين في المتون، والآخر في غيرها ؛ لأنه عند عدم التصحيح لأحد القولين يقدم ما في المتون ؛ لأنها الموضوعة لنقل المذهب كما مر ، فكذا إذا تعارض التصحيحان، ولذا قال في البحر في باب قضاء الفوائت : فقد اختلف التصحيح والفتوى، والعمل بما وافق المتون أولى ((2)
الرابع : ما إذا كان أحدهما قول الإمام الأعظم والآخر قول بعض
Explanation of the contract of the Mufti's drawing. A request regarding the rules of preponderance when there is a conflict in correction, and they are ten. 61 - And if you find a correction of two statements narrated, then choose whichever you wish, for each is relied upon. 62 - Except when they are 'sahih' and 'asah', or when it is said 'this is followed in fatwa', then it has been preferred. 63 - Or if it is in the texts, or the statement of the Imam, or the apparent of the narrated, or the majority of the great ones. 64 - He said by it, or if it is by istihsan, or it is more beneficial for endowments. 65 - Or if it is more suitable for the time, or if it is clearer in proof. 66 - This is when the correction conflicts, or if there is no explicit statement on it originally. 67 - Then the one that has a 'murabba'' from what you know, that is the clearer. Because I mentioned the signs of correction for a statement among statements, and that some terms of correction are stronger than others. This fruit appears only when there is conflict, i.e., when there is correction for two statements. I detailed that in a good detail that I have not been preceded in, taking from what I established before this. This is because their saying: 'If there are two corrected statements in a matter, then the mufti has a choice' is not absolute; rather that is when there is no preponderance for either before or after correction. The first of the preponderances: when the correction of one is with the term 'sahih' and the other with 'asah', and the discussion preceded, and that the well-known is to prefer 'asah' over 'sahih'. The second: when one is with the term 'fatwa' and the other with something else. The third: when one of the two corrected statements is in the texts (mutun) and the other outside them, because when there is no correction for either statement, what is in the texts is given precedence, since they are set up to transmit the school, as passed. So likewise when two corrections conflict. Hence he said in al-Bahr in the chapter of making up missed prayers: 'The correction and fatwa have differed, and acting according to what agrees with the texts is more proper.' The fourth: when one is the statement of the Greatest Imam and the other the statement of someone else.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti presents the rules of preponderance (tarjih) when there is a conflict between two corrected positions. The author first gives a poetic summary (nazm) listing ten rules, then provides explanatory commentary. The key principle is that when two statements are both 'corrected' (musahhah), the mufti is not automatically free to choose; rather, certain factors tip the balance. The first rule: if one is called 'sahih' and the other 'asah', the latter is preferred. The second: if one is labeled 'al-fatwa' (the view on which fatwa is given), that one is preferred. The third: statements found in the authoritative mutun (texts) take precedence over those in commentaries or fatwa collections. The fourth: the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa (al-Imam al-A'zam) is given preference over statements of other Hanafi scholars. The rules continue to include istihsan, benefit for endowments, suitability for the time, clarity of proof, and others. The commentary explains each rule with examples. This passage is foundational for muftis to navigate internal Hanafi ikhtilaf and issue sound fatwas.

Key Terms
تصحيح (tasheeh): The act of declaring a ruling or statement to be correct and reliable for practice.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of giving preponderance to one evidence or opinion over another based on specific criteria.
صحيح (sahih): A term of correction indicating that a statement is deemed correct, but weaker than 'asah'.
الأصح (al-asah): The most correct; a term indicating a higher degree of correction than 'sahih'.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The expression 'upon this is the fatwa' indicates a ruling that is to be given in practice.
المتون (al-mutun): The core texts of the madhhab, such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Hidayah, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the ten preponderance factors?
A) The statement is labeled 'asah' vs 'sahih'
B) The statement is accompanied by 'al-fatwa'
C) The statement is from the mutun
D) The statement is from a later Hanafi scholar's personal opinion

Key Takeaway
The ten rules of tarjih ensure systematic preference when corrected statements conflict, preventing arbitrary fatwas and preserving internal coherence.

Preference for Fatwa Wording in Tas-hih
Rule for preferring a tas-hih with fatwa wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a tas-hih containing the phrase 'عليه الفتوى' is preferred over one without it, and identify the mufta bihi ruling when two corrected sayings conflict.

Core Idea
When two corrections conflict, the one bearing the mark of fatwa wording ('عليه الفتوى') is the operative authority.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology (Rasm al-Mufti), not all corrections are equal. When two different rulings are each declared to be 'the correct position' (tas-hih), the mufti needs a clear rule to decide which to follow. This lesson presents a key rule: if one tas-hih is explicitly marked with the phrase 'عليه الفتوى' (upon it is the fatwa) and the other is not, the former is preferred. The rationale is that this wording is the strongest indicator of the relied-upon position and is chosen for the convenience of the people.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting tas-hih
First, locate the two corrected sayings (قولان مصححان) in the sources. Each is a valid correction within the madhhab.
For example, in the case of impurity from urine smell, one tas-hih says it is pure (in al-ashah by Qadikhan), another says it is impure.
2
Check for the phrase 'عليه الفتوى'
Examine each tas-hih to see if it is accompanied by the phrase 'عليه الفتوى' or a synonym like 'وبه يفتى'. This phrase explicitly marks the operative ruling.
The passage cites an example from al-Tanwir where the tas-hih with 'عليه الفتوى' is preferred.
3
Apply the rule of preference
If one tas-hih has 'عليه الفتوى' and the other does not, the one with the fatwa wording is taken as the mufta bihi (operative ruling). This is the second rule of preference.
The author in Radd al-Muhtar states: 'Corrected their saying because upon it is the fatwa, and the wording of fatwa is the strongest of correction wordings.'
4
Justify with the rationale
The preference is because this wording is the strongest form of correction and is chosen as it is more convenient (أرفق) for the people, meaning it is easier to act upon.
This rationale is explicitly given in the text: 'especially since it is more convenient for people'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قواعد الترجيح عند تعارض التصحيح الثاني : ما إذا كان أحدهما بلفظ الفتوى، والآخر بغيره (١) كما تقدم بيانه . رد المحتار: قوله : في الأصح قاله قاضيخان ومقابله القول بنجاسته ؛ لأنه ينجس فيه شم البول . (٢٢٥/١ ) . (١) قوله : " والآخر بغيره قال في التنوير وشرحه : "أو كان المبيع طعاما فأكله أو بعضه أو أطعمه عبده ... يرجع بالنقصان استحسانًا عندهما وعليه الفتوى". وقال في رد المحتار : " والحاصل أنهما قولان مصححان ولكن صححوا قولهما بأن عليه الفتوى ولفظ الفتوى أكد ألفاظ التصحيح، ولا سيما هو أرفق بالناس كما يأتى فلذا اختاره المصنف في متنه " . (٢٢/٥)
Second: When one of them is with the wording of fatwa, and the other is without it (1) as previously explained. Radd al-Muhtar: He said: 'In al-ashah' said by Qadikhan, and its opposite is the saying of impurity because it becomes impure by the smell of urine. (225/1). (1) He said: 'And the other without it,' he said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: 'Or if the sold item was food and he ate it or part of it or fed it to his slave... he recovers the deficiency by istihsan according to them, and upon it is the fatwa.' And he said in Radd al-Muhtar: 'The conclusion is that they are two correct sayings, but they corrected their saying because upon it is the fatwa, and the wording of fatwa is the strongest of correction wordings, especially since it is more convenient for people as will come, so the author chose it in his matn.' (22/5)
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage states the second rule for preferring one corrected ruling over another when two corrections conflict. The rule is that if one correction is explicitly stated with the phrase 'upon it is the fatwa' (عليه الفتوى) and the other is not, then the one with the fatwa wording is preferred. The reason is that such wording is a strong indicator that the ruling is the relied-upon position in the school. The footnote from Radd al-Muhtar illustrates with an example from Qadikhan about impurity, and another from al-Tanwir about a sale of food where the buyer consumes part; the preferred ruling is that the buyer recovers the deficiency by istihsan, and this is the fatwa. The commentary emphasizes that the phrase 'upon it is the fatwa' is the strongest form of correction, and it is chosen because it is more convenient for people.

Key Terms
لفظ الفتوى (lafz al-fatwa): The expression 'عليه الفتوى' used to indicate the relied-upon position in a madhhab
تصحيح (tas-hih): The act of identifying and declaring a particular ruling as the correct position in the madhhab
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one ruling or evidence over another when they conflict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred tas-hih when one has 'عليه الفتوى' and the other does not?
A) The one without 'عليه الفتوى'
B) The one with 'عليه الفتوى'
C) They are equal
D) The one mentioned in the matn

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'عليه الفتوى' is the strongest indicator of the operative ruling in Hanafi fatwa.

Preferring Matn Corrections in Hanafi Iftaa
Rule and example for preferring matn corrections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a tas-hih in the matn is preferred over one outside, and identify the hierarchy of Hanafi sources: matn > sharh > fatwa collections.

Core Idea
A tas-hih in the matn outranks all later fatwas — the matn is the madhhab's backbone.

This lesson explains the third rule of rasm al-mufti: when two conflicting 'corrected' positions exist, one in the matn and one outside, the matn's ruling takes precedence. This hierarchy ensures fatwa is based on the most authoritative transmission of the madhhab. The passage uses the example of debtor imprisonment to show how later fatwas (like Qadikhan's) must yield to the matn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting tas-hihs
Locate the two corrected positions: one in the matn, one elsewhere (commentary or fatwa collection).
Example: al-Hidayah (matn) vs Qadikhan's fatwa.
2
Apply the rule of preference
State: the matn's tas-hih is preferred because the matn is established for transmitting the madhhab.
The rule applies even if the matn is older.
3
Examine the supporting dalil
The matn is the primary vehicle for the madhhab; commentaries and fatwa collections are secondary sources.
From the passage: 'لما صرحوا به من أن ما في المتون مقدم على ما في غيره'
4
Note the extension to commentaries
If the matn has no clear ruling, the commentary (sharh) is preferred over fatwa collections.
The passage states: 'وكذا يقدم ما في الشروح على ما في الفتاوى'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : ما إذا كان أحد القولين المصححين في المتون، والآخر في غيرها ؛ لأنه عند عدم التصحيح لأحد القولين يقدم ما في المتون ؛ لأنها الموضوعة لنقل المذهب كما مر ، فكذا إذا تعارض التصحيحان، ولذا قال في البحر في باب قضاء الفوائت : فقد اختلف التصحيح والفتوى، والعمل بما وافق المتون أولى ((٢) قوله : والعمل بما وافق المتون أولى"؛ لما صرحوا به من أن ما في المتون مقدم على ما في غيره من الشروح والفتاوى . (مظ) قال في التنوير وشرحه : ويحبس المديون في كل دين هو بدل مال أو ملتزم بعقد . . . مثل الثمن ... والقرض ... والمهر المعجل وما لزمه بكفالة . . . هذا هو المعتمد خلافًا لفتوى قاضيخان حيث قال : إن كان الدين بدلا عن مال كالقرض، وثمن المبيع، فالقول للمدعى، وعليه الفتوى : وإن لم يكن بدل مال فالقول للمديون اهـ . وعليه فلا يحبس فى المهر والكفالة . وقال في البحر : وهو خلاف مختار المصنف تبعاً لصاحب الهداية . وذكر الطرسوسي فى أنفع الوسائل : أنه أى ما فى الهداية المذهب المفتى به " . فقد اختلف الإفتاء في ما التزمه بعقد ولم يكن بدل، والعمل على ما في المتون كما في أنفع الوسائل. وكذا يقدم ما في الشروح على ما في الفتاوى اهـ . راجع رد المحتار: ۳۸۱/۵ ، ۳۸۲
Third: When one of the two corrected sayings is in the matn, and the other is outside it; because when there is no correction for either saying, that which is in the matn is given precedence; since they (the matn) are established for transmitting the madhhab as has passed, so likewise when two corrections conflict. Therefore, he said in al-Bahr in the chapter of making up missed prayers: 'Correction and fatwa differed, and acting upon that which agrees with the matn is better.' (2) He said: 'And acting upon that which agrees with the matn is better' because they have stated that what is in the matn is given precedence over what is in other commentaries and fatwa collections. (maz) He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: 'The debtor is imprisoned for every debt that is a substitute for property or obligated by a contract... like the price... and the loan... and the prompt dower and what becomes obligatory by guarantee... this is the relied-upon view contrary to the fatwa of Qadikhan who said: If the debt is a substitute for property like a loan or the price of a sale, then the statement of the claimant is accepted, and upon it is the fatwa; if it is not a substitute for property, then the statement of the debtor is accepted... thus he is not imprisoned for the dower and guarantee.' And he said in al-Bahr: 'This is contrary to the choice of the author following the author of al-Hidayah.' And al-Tarsusi mentioned in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: 'That which is in al-Hidayah is the madhhab to be given fatwa upon.' Thus the fatwa differed regarding what is obligated by a contract and is not a substitute, and the practice is according to what is in the matn as in Anfa' al-Wasa'il. Likewise, what is in the commentaries is given precedence over what is in fatwa collections. See Radd al-Muhtar 5:381, 382.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage explains the third rule: if one corrected saying is found in the foundational matn (like al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, etc.) and the other is in commentaries or fatwa books, the one in the matn is preferred. The reasoning is that the matn is specifically composed to transmit the madhhab. The footnote provides an example: in the issue of imprisoning a debtor for different types of debts, the matn's ruling (imprisonment for all debts) is preferred over Qadikhan's fatwa (which distinguishes between debts). The rule extends to preferring commentaries over fatwa collections: if the matn is unclear, the commentary (sharh) takes precedence over later fatwa books.

Key Terms
المتون (al-mutun): The concise, authoritative texts of the madhhab like al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, etc.
الشروح (al-shuruh): Commentaries on the matn, considered secondary but still authoritative over fatwa collections
التصحيح (al-tas-hih): A correction or preference for one of two conflicting rulings within the madhhab

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this rule, what is preferred when one tas-hih is in the matn and the other in a fatwa collection?
A) The fatwa collection
B) The matn
C) They are equal
D) The one with 'عليه الفتوى'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi iftaa, a tas-hih found in the matn takes precedence over any tas-hih found in later commentaries or fatwa collections.

Fifth Rule: Preference for Zahir al-Riwayah
Rule for preferring corrections that are Zahir al-Riwayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of preferring Zahir al-Riwayah when fatwa opinions differ, and identify whether a ruling originates from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
When fatwa opinions conflict, the one transmitted in Zahir al-Riwayah prevails.

Not all transmitted rulings carry equal authority in the Hanafi school. The mufti must know which transmission comes from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah). This rule establishes that when corrections or fatwa opinions conflict, the mufti must investigate and prefer whatever is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah. The source illustrates this with a case of differing opinions on the amount of recitation that necessitates sajdah al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting opinions
When you encounter multiple rulings on the same issue, list them clearly. In the example, three opinions exist regarding sajdah al-sahw.
2
Determine Zahir al-Riwayah status
Check which of these opinions is recorded in the six core books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah). The opinion in al-Hidayah is considered Zahir al-Riwayah.
Refer to reliable sources like al-Bahr al-Raiq to identify Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Apply the preference rule
Prefer the opinion that is Zahir al-Riwayah over others. The text says 'it is given precedence over the other' and 'one should not deviate from Zahir al-Riwayah.'
This rule is a wusta maxim; it does not override other tarjih methods when both opinions are Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : ما إذا كان أحدهما ظاهر الرواية فيقدم على الآخر قال في البحر" من كتاب الرضاع: الفتوى إذا اختلفت كان الترجيح لظاهر الرواية" . وفيه من باب المصرف : إذا اختلف التصحيح وجب الفحص عن ظاهر الرواية والرجوع إليه " . (۲) قوله : "فيقدم على الآخر " ذكر صاحب البحر ثلاثة أقوال في مقدار ما يجب به السجود إذا جهر فيما يخافت أو عكسه : الأول : ما فى الهداية من تقديره بما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين. والثاني : ما فى الخانية وغيرها من عدم التقدير بشيء منهما . والثالث : ما في الولوالجية من عدم التقدير فيما إذا جهر فيما يخافت والتقدير في عكسه. ثم قال : فقد اختلف الترجيح على ثلاثة أقوال وينبغي عدم العدول عن . ظاهر الرواية. راجع البحر الرائق: ۱۷۱/۲ .
Fifth: When one of them is Zahir al-Riwayah, it is given precedence over the other. He said in al-Bahr from the chapter of suckling: 'When the fatwa differs, the preference is for Zahir al-Riwayah.' And in it from the section of the currency exchange house: 'When the correction differs, it is obligatory to investigate Zahir al-Riwayah and to refer to it.' (2) He said: 'It is given precedence over the other.' The author of al-Bahr mentioned three sayings regarding the amount that necessitates prostration of forgetfulness if one recites aloud when he should be quiet or vice versa: First: What is in al-Hidayah – estimating by that which makes the prayer valid in both cases. Second: What is in al-Khaniyah and others – no estimation of anything from them. Third: What is in al-Walwaljiyah – no estimation when he recites aloud when he should be quiet, and estimation in the opposite case. Then he said: 'Thus the preference differs according to three sayings, and one should not deviate from Zahir al-Riwayah.' See al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:171.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This rule states that when two corrections conflict, the one that is transmitted as Zahir al-Riwaya (i.e., from the well-known transmitted books of Imam Muhammad) is preferred. The evidence is from al-Bahr, quoting that in cases of differing fatwa, preference is given to Zahir al-Riwayah. The footnote illustrates with the example of the amount of recitation that necessitates sajdah al-sahw when one recites aloud in a quiet prayer or vice versa. There are three sayings, but the correct approach is to not deviate from Zahir al-Riwayah. This underscores the high epistemological weight of the six books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books (al-Mabsut, etc.)
التصحيح (al-tas-hih): The act of determining the correct ruling from among multiple transmissions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Follow the majority
B) Follow the matn
C) Investigate and refer to Zahir al-Riwayah
D) Choose the latest fatwa

Key Takeaway
When fatwa opinions differ, the mufti must prefer the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah unless a valid reason overrides.

Sixth Rule: Preference for the Majority of Senior Scholars
Rule for preferring majority opinion in ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that when two corrected sayings conflict, the opinion held by the majority of senior scholars is preferred in fatwa.

Core Idea
In disagreement, the majority opinion of senior scholars is the criterion for fatwa.

This lesson introduces a key principle for the mufti: when faced with differing opinions within the Hanafi school, the view supported by the majority of senior scholars (jull al-mashayikh al-'izam) is given precedence. The rule is grounded in the established maxim 'al-'ibra bima qalahu al-akthar' (consideration is with what the majority said). We'll explore the rule's basis and see it applied to a concrete example regarding additions in the first tashahhud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
Read the rule: when one of two corrected sayings is held by the majority of senior scholars, it is preferred. Understand that this applies to disagreements within the madhhab where both sayings are considered valid (musahhah).
This rule is part of Rasm al-Mufti, the mufti's methodology.
2
Grasp the evidence from the mashayikh
The commentary cites Sharh al-Bayri stating the established principle: 'whenever there is disagreement in a matter, the consideration is with what the majority said.' This is the dalil (proof) for the rule.
The rule is not from primary sources but from the collective practice of later Hanafi masters.
3
Study the applied example
The example concerns adding blessings upon the Prophet in the first tashahhud of the obligatory prayer. There are different views: some say it always necessitates sajdah al-sahw, others say only if a specific condition is met. The majority view (of al-Qadi Imam and others) is that sajdah al-sahw is required only if one says 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad' without adding 'wa 'ala aalihi'.
The passage notes that al-Qadi Imam's view is what the majority hold and is 'asahh' (most correct).
4
Apply the rule to tarjih
In a fatwa context, the mufti identifies which opinion has the support of the majority of senior scholars. If both opinions are corrected (musahhah), the majority view is preferred unless a stronger indicator exists (e.g., a explicit text or a later consensus).
This rule does not override a clear nass or a more specific principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : ما إذا كان أحد القولين المصححين قال به جلّ المشايخ العظام ) . ففى "شرح البيرى على الأشباه " : "إن المقرر عن المشايخ أنه متى اختلف في المسألة، فالعبرة بما قاله الأكثر " . اهـ . وقدمناه نحوه عن الحاوي (۳) قوله : قال به جلّ المشايخ العظام " قال في التنوير وشرحه : ولا يزيد في الفرض على التشهد في القعدة الأولى إجماعاً ، فإن زاد عامداً كره فتجب الإعادة، أو ساهيا وجب عليه سجود السهو إذا قال : اللهم صل على محمد فقط. وقال في رد المحتار: وقيل : لا يجب ما لم يقل "وعلى آل محمد" ذكره القاضي الإمام، وقيل: ما لم يؤخر مقدار أداء ركن ... ولكن ذكر في شرحه الصغير : أن ما ذكره القاضي الإمام هو الذي عليه الأكثر وهو الأصح ... وينبغي ترجيح ما ذكره القاضي الإمام (رد المحتار : ١ / ٥١١،٥١٠) .
Sixth: When one of the two corrected sayings is held by the majority of the senior scholars. In Sharh al-Bayri on al-Ashbah: 'It is established from the mashayikh that whenever there is disagreement in a matter, the consideration is with what the majority said.' End. We have already presented something similar from al-Hawi. (3) He said: 'Held by the majority of the senior scholars.' He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: 'And one should not add in the obligatory prayer to the tashahhud in the first sitting by consensus. If he adds deliberately, it is disliked and he must repeat; if forgetfully, prostration of forgetfulness becomes obligatory if he said: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad only.' And he said in Radd al-Muhtar: 'It is said that it is not obligatory unless he says "and upon the family of Muhammad" mentioned by al-Qadi Imam, and it is said: unless he delays the performance of a pillar... But he mentioned in his small commentary: that what al-Qadi Imam mentioned is that upon which the majority are, and it is the most correct... And one should prefer what al-Qadi Imam mentioned.' (Radd al-Muhtar 1:510-511)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This rule states that when two corrected sayings conflict, the one that is held by the majority of the great mashayikh (senior scholars) is preferred. The evidence is from Sharh al-Bayri on al-Ashbah, stating that the established principle is that the majority opinion prevails. The footnote provides an example: in the issue of adding blessings upon the Prophet in the first tashahhud of the obligatory prayer. There are different opinions, but the majority and the most correct view is that if one adds, it necessitates sajdah al-sahw only if he says 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad' without 'Al' Muhammad, as reported by al-Qadi Imam. This is the view that should be given preference.

Key Terms
جل المشايخ العظام (jull al-mashayikh al-'izam): The majority of the great senior scholars of the madhhab
العبرة بما قاله الأكثر (al-'ibra bima qalahu al-akthar): The criterion is what the majority said

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The view of the oldest scholar
B) The view of the majority
C) The view of the author of al-Hidayah
D) The view with 'عليه الفتوى'

Key Takeaway
When two corrected sayings conflict, the opinion held by the majority of senior Hanafi scholars is preferred in fatwa.
