The Ten Rules of Tarjih When Corrections Conflict
Listing ten rules of tarjih for conflicting tashih in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the ten rules of tarjih (preference) when conflicting corrections (tashih) are present in a fatwa, and identify which rule governs a given scenario.

Core Idea
When fatwa corrections conflict, ten rules guide preference—from Zahir al-Riwayah to the clearest proof.

In the practice of ifta, a mufti may encounter multiple corrections (tashih) for a single issue. This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti enumerates ten authoritative rules for preferring one correction over another. These rules are not arbitrary; they reflect the epistemological hierarchy of Hanafi usul, from textual authority (Zahir al-Riwayah) to the strength of evidence and contemporary custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting corrections
Recognize that there are multiple tashihs (corrections/opinions) for the same issue. This is the prerequisite for applying any tarjih rule.
2
Check for Zahir al-Riwayah
Apply rule 5: if one correction is from Zahir al-Riwayah, it is preferred over others. This is the highest textual authority in the Hanafi school.
Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the well-known rulings transmitted in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
3
Check majority opinion
Apply rule 6: if one correction is held by the majority of great scholars (al-jumhur), it is preferred. This reflects scholarly consensus within the school.
The majority here means the weight of scholarly authority, not a mere count.
4
Check for istihsan vs qiyas
Apply rule 7: if one correction is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the other on qiyas (analogy), the istihsan-based correction is preferred, except in exceptional cases.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi source that may override strict analogy.
5
Check for benefit to waqf
Apply rule 8: if one correction is more beneficial (anfa) for a waqf (endowment), it is preferred, as stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi.
This rule applies specifically to issues involving waqf property.
6
Check for harmony with time
Apply rule 9: if one correction is more in harmony with the custom (urf) of the people or easier for them, it is preferred. This allows fatwa to adapt to changing circumstances.
Example: the shift from presuming witness uprightness to requiring verification due to increased dishonesty.
7
Check for strength of proof
Apply rule 10: prefer the correction whose proof (dalil) is clearer and stronger. This is the overriding principle when earlier rules do not resolve the conflict.
Example: the takbir of tashriq—the Sahibayn's view was preferred over Imam Abu Hanifa's because their evidence was stronger.
8
Fallback: Imam's statement
If no other rule applies, the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is given precedence over his companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), unless necessity dictates otherwise.
This is the default rule stated at the beginning of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتی قواعد الترجيح عند تعارض التصحيح . أصحابه ؛ لأنه عند عدم الترجيح لأحدهما يقدم قول الإمام لأحدهما يقدم قول الإمام كما مر بيانه ، فكذا بعده. (۲) الخامس : ما إذا كان أحدهما ظاهر الرواية فيقدم على الآخر قال في البحر من كتاب الرضاع: الفتوى إذا اختلفت كان الترجيح لظاهر الرواية . وفيه من باب المصرف : إذا اختلف التصحيح وجب الفحص عن ظاهر الرواية والرجوع إليه . (۳) السادس : ما إذا كان أحد القولين المصححين قال به جلّ المشايخ العظام . ففى شرح البيرى على الأشباه : إن المقرر عن المشايخ أنه متى اختلف في المسألة، فالعبرة بما قاله الأكثر . اهـ . وقدمناه نحوه عن الحاوى (۱) قوله : يقدم قول الإمام كما أن وقت الظهر من زوال الشمس إلى بلوغ الظل مثليه عند الإمام. وقالا : إلى بلوغ الظل مثليه . وقال في رد المحتار: لا يعدل عن قول الإمام إلى قولهما أو قول أحدهما إلا لضرورة . (٣٥٩/١) (۲) قوله : فيقدم على الآخر ذكر صاحب البحر ثلاثة أقوال في مقدار ما يجب به السجود إذا جهر فيما يخافت أو عكسه : الأول : ما فى الهداية من تقديره بما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين. والثاني : ما فى الخانية وغيرها من عدم التقدير بشيء منهما . والثالث : ما في الولوالجية من عدم التقدير فيما إذا جهر فيما يخافت والتقدير في عکسه. ثم قال : فقد اختلف الترجيح على ثلاثة أقوال وينبغي عدم العدول عن ظاهر الرواية. راجع البحر الرائق: ۱۷۱/۲ . (۳) قوله : قال به جلّ المشايخ العظام قال في التنوير وشرحه : ولا يزيد في الفرض على التشهد في القعدة الأولى إجماعاً ، فإن زاد عامداً كره فتجب الإعادة، أو ساهيا وجب عليه سجود السهو إذا قال : اللهم صل على محمد فقط. وقال في رد المحتار: وقيل : لا يجب ما لم يقل وعلى آل محمد ذكره القاضي الإمام، وقيل: ما لم يؤخر مقدار أداء ركن ... ولكن ذكر في شرحه الصغير : أن ما ذكره القاضي الإمام هو الذي عليه الأكثر وهو الأصح ... وينبغي ترجيح ما ذكره القاضي الإمام (رد المحتار : ١ / ٥١١،٥١٠) . السابع : ما إذا كان أحدهما الاستحسان والآخر القياس؛ لما قدمناه من أن الأرجح الاستحسان (۱) إلا فى مسائل . الثامن : ما إذا كان أحدهما أنفع للوقف (۲)؛ لما صرحوا به في الحاوى القدسي وغيره : من أنه يفتى بما هو أنفع للوقف فيما اختلف العلماء فيه . التاسع : ما إذا كان أحدهما أوفق لأهل الزمان ؛ فإن ما كان أوفق لعرفهم أو أسهل عليهم ، فهو أولى بالاعتماد عليه ولذا أفتوا بقول الإمامين في مسألة تزكية الشهود وعدم القضاء بظاهر العدالة ؛ لتغير أحوال الزمان ؛ فإن الإمام كان في القرن الذي شهد له رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ،بالخيرية بخلاف عصرهما ؛ فإنه قد فشى فيه الكذب، فلا بد فيه من التزكية . وكذا عدلوا عن قول أئمتنا الثلاثة في عدم جواز الاستئجار على التعليم ونحوه ، لتغير الزمان ووجود الضرورة، إلى القول بجوازه، كما مر بيانه . العاشر : ما إذا كان أحدهما دليله أوضح وأظهر (۳) ، كما تقدم أن (۱) قوله : أن الأرجح الاستحسان أمثلة ترجيح الاستحسان على القياس كثيرة لا يخفى على من طالع الكتب الفقهية. (۲) قوله : أنفع للوقف قال الإمام الحصكفى رحمه الله تعالى : ويفتي بالضمان في غصب عقار الوقف وغصب منافعه ، وكذا يفتى بكل ما هو أنفع للوقف فيما اختلف فيه العلماء حتى نقضوا الإجارة عند الزيادة الفاحشة؛ نظراً للوقف وصيانة لحق الله تعالى حاوى القدسي. (رد المحتار : (٢١/٦) (۳) قوله : دليله أوضح وأظهر كما يجب تكبير التشريق عند الإمـام مـرة عـقب كل فرض أدى بجماعة مستحبة من فجر عرفة إلى عصر العيد وقالا : بوجوبه فور كل فرض مطلقا إلى آخر أيام التشريق . ورجح أهل الترجيح قولهما، وقال في رد المحتار في سبب ترجيح قولهما : هذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف الإمام وصاحباه فالعبرة لقوة الدليل، وهو الأصح . (١٨٠/٢)
Explanation of the Contract of the Mufti. Rules of preference when corrections conflict. His companions; because when there is no preference for one of them, the statement of the Imam is preferred, as was explained, and likewise after it. (2) Fifth: When one of them is from Zahir al-Riwayah, it is given precedence over the other. He said in al-Bahr from the book of al-Rada‘: The fatwa, if it differs, the preference is for Zahir al-Riwayah. And in it from the chapter of al-Masraf: If the correction differs, it is necessary to investigate Zahir al-Riwayah and refer to it. (3) Sixth: When one of the two corrected statements is held by the majority of great scholars. For in Sharh al-Bayri on al-Ashbah: It is established from the scholars that whenever there is a difference in a matter, consideration is given to what the majority said. End. And we have presented something similar from al-Hawi al-Qudsi. (1) His statement: The statement of the Imam is given precedence just as the time of Zuhr is from the declining of the sun until the shadow reaches twice its length according to Imam, and they said until the shadow reaches twice its length. And he said in Rad al-Muhtar: One should not deviate from the statement of Imam to their statement or the statement of one of them except out of necessity. (359/1) (2) His statement: It is given precedence over the other. The author of Bahr mentioned three statements about the amount that necessitates prostration if one recites aloud where one should be silent or vice versa: First, what is in al-Hidayah of estimating it by what makes the prayer valid in both cases. Second, what is in al-Khaniyyah and others of not estimating anything from them. Third, what is in al-Walwaljiyyah of not estimating when one recites aloud where one should be silent, and estimating in the opposite. Then he said: So the preference differed according to three statements, and one should not deviate from Zahir al-Riwayah. Refer to al-Bahr al-Ra‘iq: 171/2. (3) His statement: Held by the majority of great scholars. He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: He does not increase in the obligatory prayer over the tashahhud in the first sitting by consensus. If he increases intentionally, it is disliked and requires repetition; if forgetfully, he must perform sajdah al-sahw if he said 'Allahumma salli ala Muhammad' only. And he said in Rad al-Muhtar: It is said it is not obligatory unless he says 'wa ala ali Muhammad', mentioned by al-Qadi al-Imam, and it is said unless he delays the performance of a pillar... But he mentioned in his small commentary that what al-Qadi al-Imam mentioned is what the majority holds and it is the most correct... And one should give preference to what al-Qadi al-Imam mentioned (Rad al-Muhtar: 1/511,510). Seventh: When one of them is istihsan and the other is qiyas; because we have already presented that istihsan is preferable (1) except in some issues. Eighth: When one of them is more beneficial for the waqf (2); because they stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi and others: He gives fatwa by what is more beneficial for the waqf concerning what the scholars differed on. Ninth: When one of them is more in harmony with the people of the time; because what is more in harmony with their custom or easier for them is more worthy of reliance. Therefore they gave fatwa by the statement of the two Imams in the issue of verifying witnesses and not judging by apparent uprightness due to the change of times. Because the Imam was in the century that the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) testified was the best, unlike their time; for lying had become widespread, so verification is necessary. Likewise they deviated from the statement of our three Imams regarding impermissibility of hiring for teaching and the like due to change of time and existence of necessity, to the statement of permissibility, as was explained. Tenth: When one of them has a clearer and more evident proof (3), as previously stated that (1) His statement: Istihsan is preferable. Examples of preferring istihsan over qiyas are many, not hidden from one who studies the fiqh books. (2) His statement: More beneficial for the waqf. Imam Haskafi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He gives fatwa of liability in usurping waqf real estate and usurping its usufructs, and likewise he gives fatwa by everything that is more beneficial for the waqf in what scholars differed on, even revoking the lease at excessive increase, for the sake of the waqf and preserving the right of Allah. (al-Hawi al-Qudsi). (Rad al-Muhtar: 6/21) (3) His statement: His proof is clearer and more evident. As required: the takbir of tashriq according to Imam is once after every obligatory prayer performed with a recommended congregation from dawn of Arafa to afternoon of Eid, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: obligatory immediately after every obligatory prayer absolutely until the end of the Tashriq days. And the preference experts gave weight to their statement. And he said in Rad al-Muhtar regarding the reason for preferring their statement: This is based on that when the Imam and his two companions differ, consideration is for the strength of the evidence, and that is the most correct. (2/180)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti enumerates ten rules (from the fifth to the tenth) that a mufti should apply when there are contradictory corrections (tashih) for a single issue. The author begins by reaffirming a base principle: when there is no clear preference, the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is preferred over his companions, unless necessity dictates otherwise (as per the footnote citing Rad al-Muhtar). The fifth rule: if one of the rival opinions belongs to Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known transmitted rulings of Imam Muhammad), it is given precedence. The footnote elaborates with an example from al-Bahr al-Ra‘iq regarding the amount of loud/silent recitation that necessitates sajdah; despite three different estimates, the correct approach is to adhere to Zahir al-Riwayah. The sixth rule: if one of the two corrected opinions is held by the majority of great scholars, that opinion is preferred. The footnote gives the example of increasing tashahhud in the first sitting: the majority view (as held by al-Qadi al-Imam) is that one must say 'wa ala ali Muhammad' for sajdah al-sahw to become obligatory, and preference is given to this view. The seventh rule: istihsan (juristic preference) takes precedence over qiyas (analogy), except in certain exceptional cases. The eighth rule: when one opinion is more beneficial for a waqf (endowment), it is to be preferred, as stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. The ninth rule: the opinion more harmonious with the people of the time—their custom or ease—is given weight. The author provides two examples: (a) the requirement of verifying witnesses (tazkiyah) due to increased dishonesty, moving from Imam Abu Hanifa's view of presuming uprightness to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; (b) the permissibility of hiring for teaching and similar activities, deviating from the earlier three Imams' prohibition due to necessity. The tenth rule: the opinion whose proof is clearer and stronger is preferred. The footnote gives the example of the takbir of tashriq: Imam Abu Hanifa said once after each fard prayed with congregation, while the Sahibayn said it is wajib after every fard; the preference authorities gave weight to the Sahibayn's view because of the strength of their evidence. This last example also illustrates that when Imam and his two companions differ, the criterion is the strength of the proof, not mere seniority.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known, authoritative transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in the six core books.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that sets aside strict analogy for a stronger consideration like custom or necessity.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction; deriving a ruling for a new case from a original case due to shared effective cause.
التصحيح (al-tashih): Correction; in this context, a corrected or relied-upon ruling in a fatwa.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preference; the method of giving weight to one evidence or opinion over another.
الوقف (al-waqf): Endowment; a charitable trust in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tenth rule of tarjih, if Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions differ on an issue, how should a mufti decide?
A) Always follow Imam Abu Hanifa.
B) Follow the opinion that is more beneficial for the waqf.
C) Prefer the opinion whose proof is clearer and stronger.
D) Follow the opinion of the majority of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The ten rules of tarjih provide a systematic method for a mufti to choose between conflicting corrections, prioritizing Zahir al-Riwayah, majority opinion, istihsan, benefit for waqf, harmony with time, and ultimately the strength of evidence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Preferring Istihsan Over Qiyas – Rule 7
Rule 7 of tarjih among conflicting sahih positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that istihsan is preferred over qiyas when both conflict, while recognizing the exceptions.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas when two rulings conflict, except in certain issues.

When a mufti finds two equally sahih rulings—one based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the other on qiyas (analogy)—which should he choose? The Hanafi tradition gives priority to istihsan, but not absolutely. This lesson explores the rationale and the exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting proofs
In a case where one ruling is derived via istihsan and the other via qiyas, note the basis of each. The Hanafi school often uses istihsan to relax a strict qiyas for public benefit or custom.
Istihsan is a recognised source of law in the Hanafi madhhab, but not in all schools.
2
Recall the general rule
The text states that istihsan is given preference (al-arjah al-istihsan). This is a default position unless an exception is specified.
Examples of istihsan overriding qiyas are abundant in fiqh works.
3
Check for exceptions
The rule explicitly says 'except in some issues' (illa fi masail). The mufti must know those exceptional cases where qiyas prevails.
These exceptions are documented in detailed fiqh texts.
4
Apply the rule to a new scenario
When confronted with a fatwa request where both a qiyas-based and an istihsan-based ruling exist, the mufti should give fatwa according to the istihsan ruling unless the case falls under a known exception.
If uncertain, consult the tarjih literature or a more senior mufti.

Source Text

السابع : ما إذا كان أحدهما الاستحسان والآخر القياس؛ لما قدمناه من أن الأرجح الاستحسان (۱) إلا فى مسائل . الثامن : ما إذا كان أحدهما أنفع للوقف (۲)؛ لما صرحوا به في الحاوى القدسي وغيره : " من أنه يفتى بما هو أنفع للوقف فيما اختلف العلماء فيه " . التاسع : ما إذا كان أحدهما أوفق لأهل الزمان ؛ فإن ما كان أوفق لعرفهم أو أسهل عليهم ، فهو أولى بالاعتماد عليه ولذا أفتوا بقول الإمامين في مسألة تزكية الشهود وعدم القضاء بظاهر العدالة ؛ لتغير أحوال الزمان ؛ فإن الإمام كان في القرن الذي شهد له رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ،بالخيرية بخلاف عصرهما ؛ فإنه قد فشى فيه الكذب، فلا بد فيه من التزكية . وكذا عدلوا عن قول أئمتنا الثلاثة في عدم جواز الاستئجار على التعليم ونحوه ، لتغير الزمان ووجود الضرورة، إلى القول بجوازه، كما مر بيانه . العاشر : ما إذا كان أحدهما دليله أوضح وأظهر (۳) ، كما تقدم أن (۱) قوله : أن الأرجح الاستحسان " أمثلة ترجيح الاستحسان على القياس كثيرة لا يخفى على من طالع الكتب الفقهية. (۲) قوله : "أنفع للوقف " قال الإمام الحصكفى رحمه الله تعالى : " ويفتي بالضمان في غصب عقار الوقف وغصب منافعه ، وكذا يفتى بكل ما هو أنفع للوقف فيما اختلف فيه العلماء حتى نقضوا الإجارة عند الزيادة الفاحشة؛ نظراً للوقف وصيانة لحق الله تعالى "حاوى القدسي". (رد المحتار : (٢١/٦) (۳) قوله : "دليله أوضح وأظهر " كما يجب تكبير التشريق عند الإمـام مـرة عـقب كل فرض أدى بجماعة مستحبة من فجر عرفة إلى عصر العيد وقالا : بوجوبه فور كل فرض مطلقا إلى آخر أيام التشريق . ورجح أهل الترجيح قولهما، وقال في رد المحتار في سبب ترجيح قولهما : " هذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف الإمام وصاحباه فالعبرة لقوة الدليل، وهو الأصح " . (١٨٠/٢) هذا كله إذا تعارض التصحيح؛ لأن كل واحد من القولين مساو للآخر في الصحة ، فإذا كان فى أحدهما زيادة قوة من جهة أخرى، يكون العمل به أولى من العمل بالآخر . وكذا إذا لم يصرح بتصحيح واحد من القولين، فيقدم ما فيه مرجح من هذه المرجحات، ككونه في المتون، أو قول الإمام، أو ظاهر الرواية . . . إلخ (۱) قوله : "هذا كله " أى جميع ما ذكر من قواعد الترجيح يعمل بها في صورتين : عند تعارض التصحيح، وعند عدم تصحيح واحد من القولين . وهذا إشارة إلى أن هذه القواعد عامة تفيد الترجيح بين الأقوال المختلفة، وكذا بين التصحيحات المختلفة والقواعد المارة من قبل خاصة تفيد الترجيح بين الأقوال المتعارضة فقط . ثم اعلم أن بعض هذه القواعد مشتركة بين هذين النوعين، وهي خمسة : كونه قول الإمام أو ظاهر الرولمية أو فى المتون، أو أقوى دليلا أو استحسانًا، كما مر .
Seventh: When one of them is istihsan and the other is qiyas; because we have stated previously that istihsan is given preference (1) except in some issues. Eighth: When one of them is more beneficial for the waqf (2); because they have explicitly stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi and others: 'One gives fatwa based on what is more beneficial for the waqf in matters where scholars differ.' Ninth: When one of them is more suitable for the people of the time; for that which is more in accordance with their custom or easier upon them is more deserving of reliance. For this reason they gave fatwa according to the statement of the two Imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the issue of tazkiyah of witnesses and not judging based on apparent probity, due to the change of the times; for Imam Abu Hanifa was in the century which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified to be the best, unlike his two companions' time, where lying had become widespread, so tazkiyah is necessary. Similarly, they deviated from the statement of our three Imams regarding the impermissibility of hiring for teaching and the like, due to the change of times and existence of necessity, to the statement of permissibility, as explained earlier. Tenth: When one of them has a clearer and more apparent proof (3), as previously mentioned that (1) He said: 'Istihsan is given preference' — examples of preferring istihsan over qiyas are many, not hidden from one who studies the fiqh books. (2) He said: 'More beneficial for the waqf' — Imam al-Haskafi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'One gives fatwa with liability in usurping the property of the waqf and usurping its benefits, and likewise one gives fatwa with everything that is more beneficial for the waqf in matters where scholars differ, even to the extent of annulling the lease when the increase is excessive; out of consideration for the waqf and preservation of the right of Allah Almighty.' (al-Hawi al-Qudsi) (Radd al-Muhtar 6/21) (3) He said: 'His proof is clearer and more apparent' — as in the takbir of tashriq: according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is one time after each obligatory prayer performed in congregation, as a sunnah, from Fajr of Arafa until Asr of the day of Eid; while the two companions say it is obligatory immediately after every obligatory prayer absolutely until the last of the days of tashriq. The people of tarjih gave preference to their statement, and it is said in Radd al-Muhtar regarding the reason for preferring their statement: 'This is based on the principle that when Imam and his two companions differ, consideration is given to the strength of the evidence, and this is the most correct.' (2/180) All this applies when there is conflicting tashih (correction); because each of the two statements is equal in correctness, so if there is in one of them an additional strength from another aspect, acting upon it is more appropriate than acting upon the other. Likewise, if no tashih is explicitly stated for either of the two statements, then precedence is given to what contains a tarjih factor among these factors, such as its being in the matn (text), or the statement of the Imam, or the zahir al-riwayah, etc. (1) He said: 'All this' i.e., all that has been mentioned of the rules of tarjih are applied in two scenarios: when there is conflicting tashih, and when there is no tashih for either statement. This indicates that these rules are general, giving preference between different statements, and also between different tashihs, while the previous rules were specific to giving preference between conflicting statements only. Then know that some of these rules are common to both types, and they are five: being the statement of the Imam, or of zahir al-riwayah, or in the matn, or stronger in evidence, or istihsan, as has passed.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage presents rules 7 to 10 of the rules for tarjīḥ (preference) when conflicting taṣḥīḥ (authoritative rulings) are found. Rule 7: If one ruling is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference) and the other on qiyās (analogy), the one based on istiḥsān is given preference, except in certain issues. The commentator notes that examples of preferring istiḥsān over qiyās are abundant in fiqh literature. Rule 8: When one ruling is more beneficial for a waqf (endowment), it is preferred. The commentator quotes al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī citing Imam al-Ḥaskafī: a muftī should give fatwa based on what is more beneficial for the waqf when scholars disagree, even to the extent of annulling a lease if the rent increases excessively, to protect the waqf as a divine trust. Rule 9: The ruling more suitable for the people of the time is preferred, especially if it conforms to their custom or is easier. The text gives two examples: (a) requiring tazkiyah (witness accreditation) instead of relying on apparent probity, because lying became common after the best generation; (b) permitting hiring for teaching, which was initially prohibited by the three founders (Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad), due to changed circumstances and necessity. Rule 10: The ruling whose evidence is clearer and stronger is preferred. The commentator illustrates with the ruling on takbīr al-tashrīq: Imam Abū Ḥanīfa held it as a sunna once after each fard prayed in congregation, while his two companions held it wajib after every fard. The experts in tarjīḥ preferred the companions' view due to stronger evidence, as stated in Radd al-Muḥtār. The author then explains that these rules apply when two rulings are equally ṣaḥīḥ (correct) or when no taṣḥīḥ is specified. They are general rules applicable to both conflicting rulings and conflicting corrections. Additionally, five of the rules mentioned previously (being the Imam's statement, being in the ẓāhir al-riwāyah, being in the matn, having stronger evidence, or being istiḥsān) apply to both types of conflict.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference: preferring one ruling over another based on what is more suitable or equitable, often overriding a clear analogy (qiyās).
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (aṣl) to a new case (farʿ) due to a shared effective cause (ʿilla).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Rule 7, when a ruling based on istihsan conflicts with a ruling based on qiyas, what is the default preference?
A) Qiyas is preferred
B) Istihsan is preferred
C) Both are given equal weight
D) The ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa is always taken

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is preferred over qiyas when two sahih rulings conflict, but always check for exceptions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Preferring the More Beneficial for Waqf – Rule 8
Rule 8 of tarjih among conflicting sahih positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that when scholars differ on a waqf matter, the mufti should adopt the ruling most beneficial for the waqf.

Core Idea
When choosing among differing fatwas for a waqf, pick the one that best preserves and benefits the endowment.

Waqf properties are sacred trusts dedicated to Allah. When scholars disagree over a waqf-related ruling, the mufti is not free to pick any view. The Hanafi tradition instructs him to choose the ruling that is most beneficial for the waqf, even if it means overriding a default rule. This lesson unpacks that principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqf-related conflict
Recognise that the issue at hand involves a waqf (endowment) and that there are differing sahih opinions among scholars on how to rule.
The conflict may be about leasing, sale, compensation, or management.
2
Evaluate the impact on the waqf
For each possible ruling, consider its effect on the waqf's preservation, income, and purpose. The ruling that best serves the waqf's long-term benefit is to be chosen.
Benefit includes financial gain, protection of assets, and fulfilment of the founder's intent.
3
Apply the rule of preference
Select the ruling that is 'anfa' li al-waqf' (more beneficial for the waqf). This may involve overriding standard rules, like annulling a lease with excessive rent increase.
The text quotes al-Haskafi: 'One gives fatwa with everything that is more beneficial for the waqf... even annulling the lease when the increase is excessive.'
4
Confirm that the ruling is from a reliable source
The chosen opinion must still be a valid sahih position within the madhhab. The rule only applies when there is genuine ikhtilaf among authoritative scholars.
If there is no ikhtilaf, the unanimous view applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع : ما إذا كان أحدهما الاستحسان والآخر القياس؛ لما قدمناه من أن الأرجح الاستحسان (۱) إلا فى مسائل . الثامن : ما إذا كان أحدهما أنفع للوقف (۲)؛ لما صرحوا به في الحاوى القدسي وغيره : " من أنه يفتى بما هو أنفع للوقف فيما اختلف العلماء فيه " . التاسع : ما إذا كان أحدهما أوفق لأهل الزمان ؛ فإن ما كان أوفق لعرفهم أو أسهل عليهم ، فهو أولى بالاعتماد عليه ولذا أفتوا بقول الإمامين في مسألة تزكية الشهود وعدم القضاء بظاهر العدالة ؛ لتغير أحوال الزمان ؛ فإن الإمام كان في القرن الذي شهد له رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ،بالخيرية بخلاف عصرهما ؛ فإنه قد فشى فيه الكذب، فلا بد فيه من التزكية . وكذا عدلوا عن قول أئمتنا الثلاثة في عدم جواز الاستئجار على التعليم ونحوه ، لتغير الزمان ووجود الضرورة، إلى القول بجوازه، كما مر بيانه . العاشر : ما إذا كان أحدهما دليله أوضح وأظهر (۳) ، كما تقدم أن (۱) قوله : أن الأرجح الاستحسان " أمثلة ترجيح الاستحسان على القياس كثيرة لا يخفى على من طالع الكتب الفقهية. (۲) قوله : "أنفع للوقف " قال الإمام الحصكفى رحمه الله تعالى : " ويفتي بالضمان في غصب عقار الوقف وغصب منافعه ، وكذا يفتى بكل ما هو أنفع للوقف فيما اختلف فيه العلماء حتى نقضوا الإجارة عند الزيادة الفاحشة؛ نظراً للوقف وصيانة لحق الله تعالى "حاوى القدسي". (رد المحتار : (٢١/٦) (۳) قوله : "دليله أوضح وأظهر " كما يجب تكبير التشريق عند الإمـام مـرة عـقب كل فرض أدى بجماعة مستحبة من فجر عرفة إلى عصر العيد وقالا : بوجوبه فور كل فرض مطلقا إلى آخر أيام التشريق . ورجح أهل الترجيح قولهما، وقال في رد المحتار في سبب ترجيح قولهما : " هذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف الإمام وصاحباه فالعبرة لقوة الدليل، وهو الأصح " . (١٨٠/٢) هذا كله إذا تعارض التصحيح؛ لأن كل واحد من القولين مساو للآخر في الصحة ، فإذا كان فى أحدهما زيادة قوة من جهة أخرى، يكون العمل به أولى من العمل بالآخر . وكذا إذا لم يصرح بتصحيح واحد من القولين، فيقدم ما فيه مرجح من هذه المرجحات، ككونه في المتون، أو قول الإمام، أو ظاهر الرواية . . . إلخ (۱) قوله : "هذا كله " أى جميع ما ذكر من قواعد الترجيح يعمل بها في صورتين : عند تعارض التصحيح، وعند عدم تصحيح واحد من القولين . وهذا إشارة إلى أن هذه القواعد عامة تفيد الترجيح بين الأقوال المختلفة، وكذا بين التصحيحات المختلفة والقواعد المارة من قبل خاصة تفيد الترجيح بين الأقوال المتعارضة فقط . ثم اعلم أن بعض هذه القواعد مشتركة بين هذين النوعين، وهي خمسة : كونه قول الإمام أو ظاهر الرولمية أو فى المتون، أو أقوى دليلا أو استحسانًا، كما مر .
Seventh: When one of them is istihsan and the other is qiyas; because we have stated previously that istihsan is given preference (1) except in some issues. Eighth: When one of them is more beneficial for the waqf (2); because they have explicitly stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi and others: 'One gives fatwa based on what is more beneficial for the waqf in matters where scholars differ.' Ninth: When one of them is more suitable for the people of the time; for that which is more in accordance with their custom or easier upon them is more deserving of reliance. For this reason they gave fatwa according to the statement of the two Imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the issue of tazkiyah of witnesses and not judging based on apparent probity, due to the change of the times; for Imam Abu Hanifa was in the century which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified to be the best, unlike his two companions' time, where lying had become widespread, so tazkiyah is necessary. Similarly, they deviated from the statement of our three Imams regarding the impermissibility of hiring for teaching and the like, due to the change of times and existence of necessity, to the statement of permissibility, as explained earlier. Tenth: When one of them has a clearer and more apparent proof (3), as previously mentioned that (1) He said: 'Istihsan is given preference' — examples of preferring istihsan over qiyas are many, not hidden from one who studies the fiqh books. (2) He said: 'More beneficial for the waqf' — Imam al-Haskafi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'One gives fatwa with liability in usurping the property of the waqf and usurping its benefits, and likewise one gives fatwa with everything that is more beneficial for the waqf in matters where scholars differ, even to the extent of annulling the lease when the increase is excessive; out of consideration for the waqf and preservation of the right of Allah Almighty.' (al-Hawi al-Qudsi) (Radd al-Muhtar 6/21) (3) He said: 'His proof is clearer and more apparent' — as in the takbir of tashriq: according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is one time after each obligatory prayer performed in congregation, as a sunnah, from Fajr of Arafa until Asr of the day of Eid; while the two companions say it is obligatory immediately after every obligatory prayer absolutely until the last of the days of tashriq. The people of tarjih gave preference to their statement, and it is said in Radd al-Muhtar regarding the reason for preferring their statement: 'This is based on the principle that when Imam and his two companions differ, consideration is given to the strength of the evidence, and this is the most correct.' (2/180) All this applies when there is conflicting tashih (correction); because each of the two statements is equal in correctness, so if there is in one of them an additional strength from another aspect, acting upon it is more appropriate than acting upon the other. Likewise, if no tashih is explicitly stated for either of the two statements, then precedence is given to what contains a tarjih factor among these factors, such as its being in the matn (text), or the statement of the Imam, or the zahir al-riwayah, etc. (1) He said: 'All this' i.e., all that has been mentioned of the rules of tarjih are applied in two scenarios: when there is conflicting tashih, and when there is no tashih for either statement. This indicates that these rules are general, giving preference between different statements, and also between different tashihs, while the previous rules were specific to giving preference between conflicting statements only. Then know that some of these rules are common to both types, and they are five: being the statement of the Imam, or of zahir al-riwayah, or in the matn, or stronger in evidence, or istihsan, as has passed.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage presents rules 7 to 10 of the rules for tarjīḥ (preference) when conflicting taṣḥīḥ (authoritative rulings) are found. Rule 7: If one ruling is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference) and the other on qiyās (analogy), the one based on istiḥsān is given preference, except in certain issues. The commentator notes that examples of preferring istiḥsān over qiyās are abundant in fiqh literature. Rule 8: When one ruling is more beneficial for a waqf (endowment), it is preferred. The commentator quotes al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī citing Imam al-Ḥaskafī: a muftī should give fatwa based on what is more beneficial for the waqf when scholars disagree, even to the extent of annulling a lease if the rent increases excessively, to protect the waqf as a divine trust. Rule 9: The ruling more suitable for the people of the time is preferred, especially if it conforms to their custom or is easier. The text gives two examples: (a) requiring tazkiyah (witness accreditation) instead of relying on apparent probity, because lying became common after the best generation; (b) permitting hiring for teaching, which was initially prohibited by the three founders (Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad), due to changed circumstances and necessity. Rule 10: The ruling whose evidence is clearer and stronger is preferred. The commentator illustrates with the ruling on takbīr al-tashrīq: Imam Abū Ḥanīfa held it as a sunna once after each fard prayed in congregation, while his two companions held it wajib after every fard. The experts in tarjīḥ preferred the companions' view due to stronger evidence, as stated in Radd al-Muḥtār. The author then explains that these rules apply when two rulings are equally ṣaḥīḥ (correct) or when no taṣḥīḥ is specified. They are general rules applicable to both conflicting rulings and conflicting corrections. Additionally, five of the rules mentioned previously (being the Imam's statement, being in the ẓāhir al-riwāyah, being in the matn, having stronger evidence, or being istiḥsān) apply to both types of conflict.

Key Terms
الوقف (al-waqf): An Islamic endowment, where assets are dedicated for charitable or religious purposes in perpetuity.
أنفع للوقف (anfa' li al-waqf): More beneficial for the endowment; the criterion for choosing among differing opinions in waqf matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Rule 8, when scholars differ on a waqf matter, which ruling should the mufti prefer?
A) The ruling that is easiest for the people
B) The ruling that is most beneficial for the waqf
C) The ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa
D) The ruling that is most common among later scholars

Key Takeaway
In waqf disputes, the mufti must choose the ruling that best serves the endowment, even if it overrides default rules.

Preferring What Suits the People of the Time – Rule 9
Rule 9 of tarjih among conflicting sahih positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a ruling more suitable to contemporary custom and ease should be preferred, using classical examples.

Core Idea
What was suitable for the best generation may not suit later times; the mufti follows what is easier and more fitting for the era.

Times change, and so do customs and needs. A ruling that was appropriate in the 2nd century may become burdensome later. The Hanafi tradition acknowledges this by allowing muftis to prefer opinions that are 'more suitable for the people of the time' (awfaq li ahl al-zaman). This lesson examines two classical illustrations: witness accreditation (tazkiyah) and hiring for teaching.

Guided Path
1
Identify the changing custom or circumstance
Determine the relevant 'urf (custom) or change in social conditions that renders one ruling less suitable. For example, spread of dishonesty may require stricter witness verification.
The change must be genuine and widely recognised.
2
Compare the available sahih opinions
There must be differing sahih rulings among the Hanafi authorities. The rule applies when one opinion is more in line with the new reality.
If all opinions are equally suitable, this rule does not apply.
3
Prefer the ruling that is easier or more fitting
Choose the opinion that conforms to the current custom or eases hardship, as long as it is a valid position.
The text gives examples: requiring tazkiyah due to widespread lying, and permitting hiring for teaching due to necessity.
4
Verify the ruling's basis in the madhhab
Ensure that the preferred opinion is from a recognised Hanafi source. The rule does not permit inventing new rulings, only selecting among existing ones.
The mufti should also consider whether the change is temporary or permanent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Which of the following is an example given in the text of applying Rule 9?
A) Preferring istihsan over qiyas

Preferring the Clearer Evidence – Rule 10
Rule 10 of tarjih among conflicting sahih positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that when two rulings are equally sahih, the one with clearer and stronger evidence is preferred, using the example of takbir al-tashriq.

Core Idea
When two sahih rulings conflict, the one with stronger evidence (orazhar dalil) is to be followed, even if it comes from the companions rather than Imam Abu Hanifa.

Sometimes two rulings are both considered sahih within the madhhab, but one is supported by clearer evidence. Rule 10 instructs the mufti to prefer the one with the stronger proof, regardless of whether it is the Imam's own view. This lesson examines the classical dispute on takbir al-tashriq to illustrate the principle.

Guided Path
1
Establish the conflict of equally sahih rulings
Identify two rulings that are both considered sahih (correct) in the madhhab. They may come from different authorities (Imam vs companions) or different transmissions.
The text says 'each of the two statements is equal in correctness'.
2
Assess the strength of evidence for each
Examine the dalil (proof) of each ruling. Which is clearer (azhar) and more apparent (azhar)? Consider the source, chain, clarity, and weight of evidence.
In the example, the companions' evidence is considered stronger.
3
Apply the tarjih based on evidence strength
Prefer the ruling with the stronger evidence, even if it contradicts the Imam's opinion. The text states: 'when Imam and his two companions differ, consideration is given to the strength of the evidence.'
This overrides the default of following the Imam's view, because evidence takes precedence.
4
Understand the thamarah (practical result)
The mufti will adopt the ruling with stronger evidence. In the example, takbir al-tashriq becomes wajib (companions' view) rather than sunna (Imam's view).
The ruling affects the obligation of the community.

(۲) قوله : "أنفع للوقف " قال الإمام الحصكفى رحمه الله تعالى : " ويفتي بالضمان في غصب عقار الوقف وغصب منافعه ، وكذا يفتى بكل ما هو أنفع للوقف فيما اختلف فيه العلماء حتى نقضوا الإجارة عند الزيادة الفاحشة؛ نظراً للوقف وصيانة لحق الله تعالى "حاوى القدسي". (رد المحتار : (٢١/٦) (۳) قوله : "دليله أوضح وأظهر " كما يجب تكبير التشريق عند الإمـام مـرة عـقب كل فرض أدى بجماعة مستحبة من فجر عرفة إلى عصر العيد وقالا : بوجوبه فور كل فرض مطلقا إلى آخر أيام التشريق . ورجح أهل الترجيح قولهما، وقال في رد المحتار في سبب ترجيح قولهما : " هذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف الإمام وصاحباه فالعبرة لقوة الدليل، وهو الأصح " . (١٨٠/٢) هذا كله إذا تعارض التصحيح؛ لأن كل واحد من القولين مساو للآخر في الصحة ، فإذا كان فى أحدهما زيادة قوة من جهة أخرى، يكون العمل به أولى من العمل بالآخر . وكذا إذا لم يصرح بتصحيح واحد من القولين، فيقدم ما فيه مرجح من هذه المرجحات، ككونه في المتون، أو قول الإمام، أو ظاهر الرواية . . . إلخ (۱) قوله : "هذا كله " أى جميع ما ذكر من قواعد الترجيح يعمل بها في صورتين : عند تعارض التصحيح، وعند عدم تصحيح واحد من القولين . وهذا إشارة إلى أن هذه القواعد عامة تفيد الترجيح بين الأقوال المختلفة، وكذا بين التصحيحات المختلفة والقواعد المارة من قبل خاصة تفيد الترجيح بين الأقوال المتعارضة فقط . ثم اعلم أن بعض هذه القواعد مشتركة بين هذين النوعين، وهي خمسة : كونه قول الإمام أو ظاهر الرولمية أو فى المتون، أو أقوى دليلا أو استحسانًا، كما مر .
Seventh: When one of them is istihsan and the other is qiyas; because we have stated previously that istihsan is given preference (1) except in some issues. Eighth: When one of them is more beneficial for the waqf (2); because they have explicitly stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi and others: 'One gives fatwa based on what is more beneficial for the waqf in matters where scholars differ.' Ninth: When one of them is more suitable for the people of the time; for that which is more in accordance with their custom or easier upon them is more deserving of reliance. For this reason they gave fatwa according to the statement of the two Imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the issue of tazkiyah of witnesses and not judging based on apparent probity, due to the change of the times; for Imam Abu Hanifa was in the century which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified to be the best, unlike his two companions' time, where lying had become widespread, so tazkiyah is necessary. Similarly, they deviated from the statement of our three Imams regarding the impermissibility of hiring for teaching and the like, due to the change of times and existence of necessity, to the statement of permissibility, as explained earlier. Tenth: When one of them has a clearer and more apparent proof (3), as previously mentioned that (1) He said: 'Istihsan is given preference' — examples of preferring istihsan over qiyas are many, not hidden from one who studies the fiqh books. (2) He said: 'More beneficial for the waqf' — Imam al-Haskafi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'One gives fatwa with liability in usurping the property of the waqf and usurping its benefits, and likewise one gives fatwa with everything that is more beneficial for the waqf in matters where scholars differ, even to the extent of annulling the lease when the increase is excessive; out of consideration for the waqf and preservation of the right of Allah Almighty.' (al-Hawi al-Qudsi) (Radd al-Muhtar 6/21) (3) He said: 'His proof is clearer and more apparent' — as in the takbir of tashriq: according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is one time after each obligatory prayer performed in congregation, as a sunnah, from Fajr of Arafa until Asr of the day of Eid; while the two companions say it is obligatory immediately after every obligatory prayer absolutely until the last of the days of tashriq. The people of tarjih gave preference to their statement, and it is said in Radd al-Muhtar regarding the reason for preferring their statement: 'This is based on the principle that when Imam and his two companions differ, consideration is given to the strength of the evidence, and this is the most correct.' (2/180) All this applies when there is conflicting tashih (correction); because each of the two statements is equal in correctness, so if there is in one of them an additional strength from another aspect, acting upon it is more appropriate than acting upon the other. Likewise, if no tashih is explicitly stated for either of the two statements, then precedence is given to what contains a tarjih factor among these factors, such as its being in the matn (text), or the statement of the Imam, or the zahir al-riwayah, etc. (1) He said: 'All this' i.e., all that has been mentioned of the rules of tarjih are applied in two scenarios: when there is conflicting tashih, and when there is no tashih for either statement. This indicates that these rules are general, giving preference between different statements, and also between different tashihs, while the previous rules were specific to giving preference between conflicting statements only. Then know that some of these rules are common to both types, and they are five: being the statement of the Imam, or of zahir al-riwayah, or in the matn, or stronger in evidence, or istihsan, as has passed.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage presents rules 7 to 10 of the rules for tarjīḥ (preference) when conflicting taṣḥīḥ (authoritative rulings) are found. Rule 7: If one ruling is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference) and the other on qiyās (analogy), the one based on istiḥsān is given preference, except in certain issues. The commentator notes that examples of preferring istiḥsān over qiyās are abundant in fiqh literature. Rule 8: When one ruling is more beneficial for a waqf (endowment), it is preferred. The commentator quotes al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī citing Imam al-Ḥaskafī: a muftī should give fatwa based on what is more beneficial for the waqf when scholars disagree, even to the extent of annulling a lease if the rent increases excessively, to protect the waqf as a divine trust. Rule 9: The ruling more suitable for the people of the time is preferred, especially if it conforms to their custom or is easier. The text gives two examples: (a) requiring tazkiyah (witness accreditation) instead of relying on apparent probity, because lying became common after the best generation; (b) permitting hiring for teaching, which was initially prohibited by the three founders (Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad), due to changed circumstances and necessity. Rule 10: The ruling whose evidence is clearer and stronger is preferred. The commentator illustrates with the ruling on takbīr al-tashrīq: Imam Abū Ḥanīfa held it as a sunna once after each fard prayed in congregation, while his two companions held it wajib after every fard. The experts in tarjīḥ preferred the companions' view due to stronger evidence, as stated in Radd al-Muḥtār. The author then explains that these rules apply when two rulings are equally ṣaḥīḥ (correct) or when no taṣḥīḥ is specified. They are general rules applicable to both conflicting rulings and conflicting corrections. Additionally, five of the rules mentioned previously (being the Imam's statement, being in the ẓāhir al-riwāyah, being in the matn, having stronger evidence, or being istiḥsān) apply to both types of conflict.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) recited after obligatory prayers during the days of tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) and for some from Fajr of 9th to Asr of 13th.
العبرة لقوة الدليل (al-‘ibra li qawwat al-dalīl): Consideration is given to the strength of the evidence; the principle that when authorities differ, the stronger proof determines the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Rule 10, what is the decisive factor when two sahih rulings conflict?
A) The authority of the scholar (Imam vs companion)
B) The strength of the evidence
C) The popularity of the ruling among later scholars
D) The ease of the ruling for the people

Key Takeaway
When two sahih rulings conflict, the one with stronger evidence is to be preferred, even if it comes from the companions rather than the Imam.

Mafhum (Implicature): Definition, Types, and Its Role in Fatwa
Defining mafhum and its types with the condition for its use.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mantuq and mafhum, identify mafhum muwafaqa, and state the condition for acting upon mafhum in fatwa.

Core Idea
Mafhum is valid only if it does not contradict an explicit established text.

This lesson introduces the concept of mafhum (implied meaning) as a tool for deriving rulings from transmitted reports. It distinguishes mantuq (explicit meaning) from mafhum (implicit meaning), focusing on mafhum muwafaqa (harmony). The matn instructs the mufti to act upon mafhum provided it does not oppose a clear nass.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mantuq from mafhum
Mantuq is what the wording indicates about the explicitly mentioned item; mafhum is what it implies about something unmentioned. Identify which part of a statement gives a direct ruling and which gives an implied one.
Mantuq is the foundation; mafhum derives from it.
2
Identify the two types of mafhum
Mafhum divides into mafhum muwafaqa (harmony) and mafhum mukhālafa (opposition). This lesson focuses on muwafaqa, where the implied ruling agrees with the explicit in reasoning.
Mafhum muwafaqa is often considered stronger than mukhālafa.
3
Apply the condition from the matn
The matn says: 'Act upon mafhum as long as it does not contradict an explicit established text.' Test any mafhum derivation against this condition before using it in fatwa.
If a mafhum opposes a clear nass, it is invalid.
4
Work through the 'uff' example
From 'Do not say 'uff' to your parents' (explicit), the mafhum muwafaqa prohibits hitting them, since hitting is worse. This mafhum does not contradict any explicit text, so it is valid.
The mafhum is derived from the intensity of the act.
5
Understand the hierarchy
Mantuq takes priority over mafhum. If a mafhum conflicts with a mantuq from another text, the mantuq prevails unless it is weak in transmission.
This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that explicit evidence overrides implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
68 - وَاعْمَلْ بِمَفْهُوْمِ رِوَايَاتِ أَتَى مَا لَمْ يُخَالِفُ لِصَرِيحٍ ثَبَنَا مطلب في المفهوم وأقسامه وحكمه (٢) اعلم أن المفهوم قسمان (۲) : مفهوم موافقة (۳): وهو دلالة اللفظ على (۲) قوله : أن المفهوم قسمان : اعلم أن المفهوم مقابل للمنطوق، والمنطوق أصل للمفهوم، فلا بد من تحقيق معناهما ، فنقول : المنطوق ما دل عليه اللفظ في محل النطق ، أى يكون حكمًا للمذكور وحالا من أحواله . ودلالة المنطوق هي : دلالة اللفظ على حكم شيء مذكور في الكلام والمفهوم ما دل عليه اللفظ لا في محل النطق ، أى يكون حكماً لغير المذكور وحالا من أحواله، وبعبارة أخرى هو : دلالة اللفظ على حكم شيء لم يذكر في الكلام .
68 - And act upon the mafhum (implied meaning) of transmitted reports that come, as long as it does not contradict an explicit text that has been established. A request concerning mafhum, its divisions and its ruling. (2) Know that mafhum is of two types (2): mafhum muwafaqa (implied meaning of harmony) (3): which is the indication of the wording upon (2) He said: 'That mafhum is of two types': Know that mafhum is the opposite of mantuq (explicit statement), and mantuq is the foundation for mafhum, so it is necessary to realize their meanings. We say: Mantuq is what the wording indicates at the place of utterance, i.e., it is a ruling for the mentioned thing and a state of its states. And the indication of mantuq is: the indication of the wording upon the ruling of something mentioned in the speech. And mafhum is what the wording indicates not at the place of utterance, i.e., it is a ruling for something other than the mentioned and a state of its states; in other words, it is the indication of the wording upon the ruling of something not mentioned in the speech.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of mafhum (implied meaning) as a tool for understanding transmitted reports (riwāyāt) and deriving rulings. It begins with a line from the matn (verse): 'And act upon the mafhum of transmitted reports that come, as long as it does not contradict an explicit text that has been established.' This sets the principle that mafhum is a valid source of guidance in fatwa unless it clashes with a clear and established nass. The commentary then defines mafhum and its counterpart mantuq. Mantuq is the explicit meaning: what the wording directly indicates about the mentioned thing. Mafhum is the implicit meaning: what the wording indicates about something not explicitly mentioned. For example, if a text says 'Do not say 'uff' to your parents,' the mantuq is the prohibition of saying 'uff,' while the mafhum (muwāfaqa) is the prohibition of hitting them, since preventing something implies preventing worse actions. The passage states that mafhum is divided into two types: mafhum muwāfaqa (harmony) and presumably mafhum mukhālafa (opposition), though the latter is not detailed here due to truncation. The commentator emphasizes that mantuq is the foundation (aṣl) for mafhum, meaning that mafhum cannot exist without an explicit statement. This principle is crucial for a muftī to ensure rulings derived from connotative meanings are valid and do not contradict explicit texts.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhūm): The implied meaning of a text: the indication of the wording to a ruling for something not mentioned in the speech.
المنطوق (al-manṭūq): The explicit meaning of a text: the indication of the wording to a ruling for something mentioned in the speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, when is it permissible to act upon the mafhum of transmitted reports?
A) Always
B) Only when it supports the madhhab
C) As long as it does not contradict an explicit text
D) Only in matters of worship

Key Takeaway
Mafhum is a valid source of rulings in the Hanafi school, but it can only be used when it does not contradict an explicit established text.

Tarjīḥ bi-Quwwat al-Dalīl: Preferring the Stronger Evidence
A rule for mufti when two correct rulings conflict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tarjīḥ bi-quwwat al-dalīl to resolve conflicting correct rulings within the Hanafi school by identifying preponderating factors such as being in the mutun, the Imam's statement, or ẓāhir al-riwāyah.

Core Idea
When two correct rulings conflict, the stronger evidence prevails — a rational preponderance, not mere preference.

As a mufti, you will often encounter cases where two opinions within the Hanafi school have both been verified as correct (tasḥīḥ). How do you decide which to give in a fatwa? The rule of tarjīḥ bi-quwwat al-dalīl provides the answer: you must examine the strength of the evidence behind each opinion. This lesson unpacks the rule and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Find two rulings that have both been explicitly declared correct (muṣaḥḥaḥ) by authoritative Hanafi scholars. If no explicit tasḥīḥ exists, look for preponderating factors directly.
The rule only applies when both are considered equally authentic in transmission.
2
List potential preponderating factors
From the text, key murajjiḥāt include: being in the core texts (al-mutun), being the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa himself, and being from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. Other factors like the later preferred view (al-mukhtār) also apply.
These are not exhaustive; later scholars added more factors.
3
Compare the evidence
Assess which opinion has a stronger evidentiary basis. For example, an opinion from the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is generally stronger than one from the Nawādir.
The evidence may include textual strength, narratorial reliability, or consistency with uṣūl.
4
Apply tarjīḥ
Prefer the opinion with the stronger evidence. If no clear preponderance is found, the mufti should seek further guidance from the school's hierarchical rules (e.g., preferring the later muftā bihi).
"Acting upon it is better" (al-ʿamal bihi awlā) indicates preference, not compulsion, but in practice it becomes the operative position.
5
Issue the fatwa
State the preferred opinion as the muftā bihi, citing the murajjiḥ if needed. If a weaker opinion is followed in case of dire need, it may be allowed but the stronger is primary.
The mufti should have the competence (ahlīyat al-naẓar) to assess evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترجيح بقوة الدليل فحيث وجد تصحيحان، ورأى من كان له أهلية النظر فى الدليل أن دليل أحدهما أقوى، فالعمل به أولى
(1)
هذا كله إذا تعارض التصحيح؛ لأن كل واحد من القولين مساو للآخر في الصحة ، فإذا كان فى أحدهما زيادة قوة من جهة أخرى، يكون العمل به أولى من العمل بالآخر . وكذا إذا لم يصرح بتصحيح واحد من القولين، فيقدم ما فيه مرجح من هذه المرجحات، ككونه في المتون، أو قول الإمام، أو ظاهر الرواية . . . إلخ
Preponderance by strength of evidence: whenever there are two verified rulings, and the person with competence to examine evidence sees that the evidence of one of them is stronger, then acting upon it is better. (1) This entire [discussion] applies when verification conflicts, because each of the two statements is equal to the other in authenticity. If one of them has additional strength from another direction, then acting upon it is better than acting upon the other. Similarly, if no verification of either statement is explicitly made, whichever has a preponderant factor among these preponderating factors is given precedence, such as being in the authoritative texts (al-mutun), or the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), or that which is apparent in transmission (zahir al-riwayah), etc.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage provides a rasm rule for the mufti: when two rulings have both been deemed correct (tasḥīḥ) but conflict, the stronger one should be followed. The commentary explains that this applies only when both are equal in authenticity; if one has greater evidentiary force (e.g., it is from Imam Abu Hanifa, or from the authoritative texts, or is apparent in transmission), it takes precedence. The rule also applies when no explicit verification is given—the mufti must then look for preponderating factors. The text lists key factors: being in the core texts, being the Imam's own view, or being from the widely transmitted reports (zahir al-riwayah). This is a rational principle of juristic preference.

Key Terms
التصحيح (al-tasḥīḥ): The act of declaring a legal opinion (qawl) as correct and authoritative for fatwa.
المرجح (al-murajjiḥ): A factor that gives preponderance (tarjīḥ) to one opinion over another.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The transmitted rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani in the six authoritative works (the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the rule of preferring the stronger evidence (tarjīḥ bi-quwwat al-dalīl) be applied?
A) Whenever two rulings conflict in a case.
B) Only when both rulings are equally authentic and conflict.
C) Only when one ruling is from the mutun and the other is not.
D) Only when the mufti personally suspects one ruling is stronger.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must prefer the opinion with stronger evidence when two verified opinions conflict, using recognized murajjiḥāt such as being in the mutun or ẓāhir al-riwāyah.

Acting upon the Implied Meaning (Mafhum) of Narrations
Rule on acting upon implied meanings (mafhum)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on mafhum to distinguish between valid mafhum al-muwafaqah (dalalat al-nass) and invalid mafhum al-mukhalafah in the speech of the Lawgiver, and justify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-muwafaqah is valid by consensus; mafhum al-mukhalafah is fasad al-istidlal in shari'ah.

A mufti frequently encounters narrations whose explicit wording addresses a specific case, but the context implies a broader or different ruling. This lesson clarifies when such implied meanings may be used for fatwa. The Hanafi school distinguishes between two types of mafhum: one that agrees with the explicit ruling (mafhum al-muwafaqah) and one that contradicts it (mafhum al-mukhalafah). Understanding this distinction is essential for sound ijtihad and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic rule
The rule states: 'Act upon the implied meaning of narrations that come, as long as it does not contradict an explicit text firmly established.' This is a general principle for the mufti.
The rule is from the matn (verse 68).
2
Differentiate mafhum al-muwafaqah and mafhum al-mukhalafah
Identify the two types: mafhum al-muwafaqah (the unspoken agrees with the spoken in ruling, called dalalat al-nass) and mafhum al-mukhalafah (the unspoken has the opposite ruling, called takhsis al-shay' bi al-dhikr).
Mafhum al-muwafaqah includes fahwa al-khitab (more deserving) and lahn al-khitab (equal).
3
Recognize the Hanafi position on mafhum al-mukhalafah
According to Hanafis, mafhum al-mukhalafah is corrupt deduction (fasad al-istidlal) in the speech of the Lawgiver (shari'ah). It may be valid in non-shari'ah contexts (e.g., contracts).
Shafi'is accept it with conditions.
4
Analyze the example of 'do not say 'uff''
The verse 'do not say to them 'uff'' (Q 17:23) implies prohibition of striking through mafhum al-muwafaqah (striking is worse, so the ruling is stronger). This is dalalat al-nass, not qiyas, because it is understood directly from language.
This shows how mafhum al-muwafaqah works without ijtihad.

(۱) قوله : " بلا توقف على رأى واجتهاد" إشارة إلى الفرق بين مفهوم الموافقة - أى دلالة النص والقياس، وهذا ؛ لأن مفهوم الموافقة يسمّى "دلالة النص" عندنا ، وهى لا تتوقف على نظر واستنباط بل يعرفها كل من كان من أهل اللسان بغير احتياج إلى ترتيب المقدمات والنظر ، فلو احتاج إليه كان قياسا لا يقف عليه إلا المجتهد، لا مفهوماً .
(۲) قوله : دلالة لا تَقُل لَّهُمَا أف على تحريم الضرب " فإن المعنى العادى له تحريم
68. Act upon the implied meaning (mafhum) of narrations that come, as long as it does not contradict an explicit [text] that is firmly established.

Section on mafhum, its divisions and its ruling.
(2) Know that mafhum is of two types: Mafhum al-Muwafaqah (consonant meaning) – it is the indication of the wording to ... (1) His saying: 'This entire [discussion]' means all that was mentioned of the rules of preponderance that are applied in two situations: when verification conflicts, and when there is no verification of either statement. This indicates that these rules are general, providing preponderance between differing statements and also between differing verifications, while the previous rules specifically provide preponderance only between conflicting statements.
Then know that some of these rules are common between these two types; there are five: [the opinion] being the statement of the Imam, or apparent in transmission, or in the authoritative texts, or stronger in evidence, or istihsan, as previously mentioned.
(2) His saying: 'Mafhum is two types': Know that mafhum is the opposite of mantuq, and mantuq is the foundation of mafhum, so it is necessary to ascertain their meanings. We say: mantuq is what the wording indicates in the place of utterance (i.e., it is a ruling for the mentioned [subject] and a state from its states). The indication of mantuq is: the indication of the wording to the ruling of a mentioned thing in the speech. Mafhum is what the wording indicates not in the place of utterance (i.e., it is a ruling for something other than the mentioned subject and a state of its states). In other words, it is the indication of the wording to the ruling of something not mentioned in the speech. The establishment of the ruling of mantuq for the unmentioned [subject] by mere understanding of the language, i.e., without pausing for opinion and ijtihad, like the indication of 'do not say to them 'uff'' upon the prohibition of striking.
(2) The summary: Words are molds for meanings derived from them. Sometimes they are derived from the aspect of utterance explicitly, and sometimes from the aspect of insinuation. The first is mantuq, the second is mafhum. Mantuq is the indication of the wording to a mentioned thing, and it includes the explicit expression of the text and its indication. Mafhum is the indication of the wording to something unspoken. Mafhum al-Muwafaqah is that the unspoken agrees with the spoken in ruling; Mafhum al-Mukhalafah is the opposite. The first is called by us 'dalalat al-nass' (textual implication), and it is valid by consensus. The other is called 'takhsis al-shay' bi al-dhikr' (specification by mention), and it is disputed: according to us, in the speech of the Lawgiver it is from corrupt deductions, and is only considered valid in other [speech]; according to the Shafi'is, it is valid in the speech of the Lawgiver and other speech with certain conditions. The full discussion will come later. Then know that both mantuq and mafhum are, in terminology, subdivisions of meaning; but in language, mantuq is the uttered expression, which is the actual wording, not the meaning, and mafhum is what is understood from the wording, which is the meaning. Hence, the application of mantuq to meaning is a terminological reality, not linguistic, because meaning is not uttered; rather the wording that indicates it is uttered. (360/1, 361)
(3) His saying: 'Mafhum al-Muwafaqah' – it is also called 'tanbih al-khitab' (prompting of discourse). (Mazahir) It is what the Hanafis express by 'dalalat al-nass', and it is called mafhum al-muwafaqah because the unspoken agrees with the spoken in ruling. So mafhum al-muwafaqah is: what the unspoken agrees with the spoken in ruling. If it is more deserving of the ruling than the spoken expression, it is called 'fahwa al-khitab' (purport of discourse), i.e., its mafhum. If it is equal, it is called 'lahn al-khitab' (tone of discourse). Lahn al-khitab in language means conveying something without explicit mention; from it is His statement: 'And you will surely recognize them in the tone (lahn) of speech' – i.e., in the slips of speech without explicit mention of hypocrisy.
(1) His saying: 'without pausing for opinion and ijtihad' – an indication of the difference between mafhum al-muwafaqah – i.e., dalalat al-nass – and qiyas. This is because mafhum al-muwafaqah – called 'dalalat al-nass' according to us – does not require reflection and deduction; rather everyone who is a native speaker knows it without needing to set up premises and reflection. If it required that, it would be qiyas, which only the mujtahid can grasp, not a mafhum.
(2) His saying: 'The indication of 'do not say to them 'uff'' upon the prohibition of striking' – for its ordinary meaning is the prohibition of...
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule (verse 68) that instructs the mufti to act upon the mafhum (implied meaning) of narrations unless it contradicts an explicit and firmly established text. The commentary then provides a comprehensive definition of mafhum and its two divisions: mafhum al-muwafaqah (consonant meaning) and mafhum al-mukhalafah (dissonant meaning). The first, which the Hanafis call dalalat al-nass (textual implication), is valid by consensus and includes fahwa al-khitab (where the unspoken is more deserving) and lahn al-khitab (where the unspoken is equal). The second, mafhum al-mukhalafah, is disputed: the Hanafis consider it invalid in the speech of the Lawgiver (i.e., it is not used for deduction in the Qur'an and Sunna) but valid in other contexts, while the Shafi'is accept it with conditions. The passage also clarifies the distinction between mantuq (explicitly uttered meaning) and mafhum (implied meaning), noting that in terminology mantuq refers to the meaning expressed, while in language it refers to the actual words. A key example is given: the verse 'do not say to them 'uff'' implies the prohibition of striking through mafhum al-muwafaqah (since striking is worse than 'uff', it is more deserving of prohibition). This is a clear case of dalalat al-nass, which does not require ijtihad but is understood by any native speaker.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhūm): The implied meaning indicated by the wording, not in the place of utterance; a ruling for something not explicitly mentioned.
المنطوق (al-manṭūq): The explicit meaning indicated by the wording in the place of utterance; the ruling for the mentioned subject.
دلالة النص (dalālat al-naṣṣ): The Hanafi term for mafhum al-muwafaqah: the textual implication where the unspoken subject agrees with the spoken one in ruling, without need for ijtihad.
فحوى الخطاب (faḥwā al-khiṭāb): The purport of discourse: when the unspoken subject is more deserving of the ruling than the spoken one (e.g., prohibition of striking from 'do not say 'uff'').
لحن الخطاب (laḥn al-khiṭāb): The tone of discourse: when the unspoken subject is equal in ruling to the spoken one (e.g., both are prohibited at the same level).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using mafhum al-mukhalafah in the speech of the Lawgiver (shari'ah)?
A) It is valid like mafhum al-muwafaqah.
B) It is invalid and considered corrupt deduction (fasad al-istidlal).
C) It is valid only if it does not contradict explicit text.
D) It is valid but requires ijtihad to apply.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, always use mafhum al-muwafaqah (dalalat al-nass) as a valid proof, and never rely on mafhum al-mukhalafah in the Qur'an and Sunna.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Hanafi Stance on Mafhum al-Mukhalafah in Shari' Speech
Explains Hanafi rejection of opposite implication in divine texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects mafhum al-mukhalafah in Shari' speech and identify where it is considered valid.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafah is valid in human speech and transactions, but not in the words of the Lawgiver.

The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between human speech and divine speech when it comes to deriving rulings from implications. While a qualification in everyday language often implies a restriction, the same cannot be assumed for the Quran and Sunnah because Allah's purposes are beyond full human comprehension. This lesson unpacks the three Hanafi proofs for rejecting mafhum al-mukhalafah in Shari' texts and explains its limited acceptance in human transactions and intellectual matters.

Guided Path
1
Define mafhum al-mukhalafah
Understand the concept and its disputed status across madhahib.
2
Analyze the three Hanafi proofs
Work through each proof: (1) divine purposes are inscrutable, (2) application would lead to corrupt meanings, (3) explicit Quranic statements make implication unnecessary.
3
Distinguish between Shari' speech and human speech
Note that mafhum is valid in human transactions and intellectual matters because human purposes are knowable.
4
Apply the ruling to a fatwa scenario
Given the example of 'Jumu'a is upon free men', explain why a Hanafi mufti cannot rely on mafhum to exclude women.
