تعريف العرف وبيان حجيته

قوله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم : «ما رآه المسلمون (۱) حسنا فهو عند الله حسن .
واعلم أن اعتبار العادة والعرف يرجع إليه في مسائل كثيرة، حتى قديستانس به في تأييد المعنى الاصطلاحي .
واستدل بعضهم بقوله تعالى : وعاشروهن بالمعروف وقوله تعالى : وعلى المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف وقوله تعالى : ولهن مثل الذي عليهن بالمعروف وقوله تعالى : فأمسكوهن بمعروف أو سرحوهن بمعروف وقوله تعالى : وللمطلقات متاع بالمعروف وقوله تعالى : فمن عفى له من أخيه شيء فاتباع بالمعروف وقوله تعالى : ومن كان فقيراً فليأكل بالمعروف فقد أمر الله سبحانه في مثل هذه الآيات التي تبلغ إلى تسع عشرة آية بالأخذ بما هو متعارف عند الناس فى باب الطلاق والمهر، والنفقة والمتعة، وأجرة المرضعة والإمساك والتسريح والمعاشرة، والوصية ومطالبة بدل الصلح والدين، وأكل الولى من مال اليتيم ونحوه، وكذلك قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لهند زوجة أبي سفيان : خذى ما يكفيك وولدك بالمعروف فلم يضع رسول الله صلي الله عليه وسلم حدا معينا لنفقتها بل ترك ذلك إلى العرف .

(۱) قوله : " ما رآه المسلمون " قال السخاوي في "المقاصد الحسنة" : حديث : «ما رأه المسلمون ... إلخ رواه أحمد في كتاب السنة " ، ووهم من عزاه للمسند [ أى مسند ابن حنبل ] من حديث أبي وائل عن ابن مسعود (مظ) قال الزيلعي عن هذا الحديث : غريب مرفوعًا ولم أجده إلا موقوفا على ابن مسعود (راجع نصب الراية : ١٣٣/٤ ) .
قال الهيثمي : ورواه أحمد والبزار والطبراني في الكبير عن ابن مسعود، ورجاله موثقون. (مجمع الزوائد ۱۷۸/۱)
(۲) قوله : " في مسائل كثيرة " لو تأملت في هذه المسائل وجدتها ترجع إلى أصول أربعة: الأول : تعيين معنى اللفظ، فإن كل متكلم إنما يتكلم على عرفه، واستعمال الناس حجة يجب العمل بها الثاني : اعتبار العادة في العقود، فتجرى العقود المطلقة عن البيان على ما يتعارفه الناس . الثالث : تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان فإن المسائل المبنية على العرف والزمان تتغير بتبدل العرف وتختلف باختلاف الزمان .

جعلوا ذلك أصلا، فقالوا : "تترك الحقيقة بدلالة الاستعمال والعادة ) . ثم ذكر في "الأشباه " : "أما العادة إنما تعتبر إذا اردت أو غلبت (۲)، ولذا قالوا في البيع : لو باع بدراهم أو دنانير في بلد اختلف فيها النقود مع الاختلاف في المالية والرواج انصرف البيع إلى الأغلب . قال في "الهداية" : "لأنه هو المتعارف، فينصرف المطلق إليه " . وفي شرح البيرى عن المبسوط " : الثابت بالعرف كالثابت بالنص . اهـ .
(۳)
الرابع : تعارف أهل البلد بما فيه ضرورة شديدة وحاجة عامة، فإنه يفتى بما هو أرفق للناس إذا ظهر عليه التعامل ولزم الحرج بنزع الناس عن عادتهم .

(۱) قوله : "بدلالة الاستعمال والعادة " [أى إذا كانت الحقيقة مهجورة ] اختلف في عطف العادة على الاستعمال ، فقيل : هما مترادفان . وقيل : المراد من الاستعمال : نقل اللفظ عن موضوعه الأصلى إلى معناه المجازى شرعًا، وغلبة استعماله فيه ومن العادة : نقله إلى معناه المجازى عرفا. (مظ) وقيل : الاستعمال يرجع إلى اللفظ والعادة إلى الفعل .
(۲) قوله : "إذا اطردت أو غلبت " أى إذا عمّت وشاعت بحيث يعرفها كل أحد ممن هو من أهلها، وإن لم تكن شائعة مستفيضة فلا أقل من أن تكون غالبة . قال الشارح في نشر العرف" : اعلم أن كلا من العرف العام والخاص إنما يعتبر إذا كان شائعا مستفيضا بين أهله يعرفه جميعهم، أما لو كان مشتركاً لا يصح الرجوع إليه ؛ للتردّد ، ولا يبنى الحكم عليه ؛ لأنه لما كان مشتركًا صار متعارضاً فلا يصلح مقيداً . انتهى ملخصاً. (١٣٤/٢)
(۳) قوله : " بالنص" الألف واللام عوض عن المضاف إليه، أي بنص المتكلم، كأنه اشترطه صريحًا، وهذا معنى قولهم : المعروف عرفًا كالمشروط شرطاً ، وقولهم : التعيين بالعرف كالتعيين بالنص".
Definition of custom and explanation of its authority. He (may Allah exalt him) said: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah.' Know that consideration of habit and custom is referred to in many issues, so much so that it is used to support the technical meaning. Some have adduced evidence from His statement: 'And consort with them in kindness' [4:19], and His statement: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing in the customary manner' [2:233], and His statement: 'And they have rights similar to those against them in kindness' [2:228], and His statement: 'Then retain them in kindness or release them in kindness' [65:2], and His statement: 'For divorced women is provision in kindness' [2:241], and His statement: 'But if anyone remits something to his brother, then follow-up should be in kindness' [2:178], and His statement: 'And if he is poor, let him eat in kindness' [4:6]. For Allah commanded in these verses—which number nineteen—to follow what is customarily accepted among people concerning divorce, dower, maintenance, mut'ah, nursing fee, retention, release, companionship, will, demand for compensation in compromise, debt, the guardian's taking from the orphan's wealth, and the like. Likewise his saying (peace be upon him) to Hind, wife of Abu Sufyan: 'Take what suffices you and your child in kindness.' The Messenger of Allah did not set a specific limit for her maintenance but left it to custom. (1) His saying: 'What the Muslims see as good'—al-Sakhawi said in al-Maqasid al-Hasana: The hadith 'What the Muslims see as good...' was narrated by Ahmad in Kitab al-Sunna, and he who attributed it to the Musnad [i.e., Musnad of Ibn Hanbal] is mistaken, from the hadith of Abi Wa'il from Ibn Mas'ud (?) al-Zayla'i said about this hadith: it is gharib marfu' and I did not find it except as mawquf from Ibn Mas'ud (see Nasb al-Raya 4/133). al-Haythami said: Ahmad, al-Bazzar, and al-Tabarani in al-Kabir narrated it from Ibn Mas'ud, and its narrators are trustworthy (Majma' al-Zawa'id 1/178). (2) His saying: 'in many issues'—if you ponder these issues, you find they reduce to four principles: First: determining the meaning of a word, for every speaker speaks according to his custom, and people's usage is a proof that must be acted upon. Second: considering custom in contracts, so absolute contracts are interpreted according to people's custom. Third: change of rulings with change of time, for issues based on custom and time change with change of custom and differ with difference of time. They made that a principle, saying: 'The literal meaning is abandoned due to usage and custom.' Then he mentioned in al-Ashbah: 'Custom is only considered if it is continuous or predominant.' Hence they said concerning sale: If one sells for dirhams or dinars in a country where currencies differ in value and circulation, the sale is referred to the predominant. al-Hidayah said: 'Because it is the customary, so the absolute is referred to it.' In Sharh al-Bayri from al-Mabsut: 'What is established by custom is like what is established by text.' End. (3) Fourth: The custom of the people of a town when it involves severe necessity and general need, then fatwa is given according to what is easier for the people when dealing has appeared based on it, and hardship would follow from removing people from their custom. (1) His saying: 'by indication of usage and custom' [i.e., when the literal meaning is abandoned]—there is disagreement on the conjunction of custom to usage. Some say they are synonymous. Some say what is meant by usage is the transfer of a word from its original meaning to its metaphorical meaning by shari'ah and its predominant use, and by custom is its transfer to its metaphorical meaning by 'urf. (?) And some say usage pertains to words and custom to actions. (2) His saying: 'if it is continuous or predominant'—i.e., if it is general and widespread such that everyone from its people knows it, and if it is not widespread at least it is predominant. The commentator said in Nashr al-'Urf: Know that both general and specific custom are only considered if it is widespread among its people such that all of them know it. As for if it is shared (i.e., not predominant), it is not valid to refer to it due to hesitation, and the ruling is not built upon it, because being shared makes it conflicting, so it is not suitable as a restrictor. End, summarized. (3) His saying: 'by text'—the alif and lam substitute for the mudaf ilayh, meaning by the explicit text of the speaker, as if he explicitly stipulated it. This is the meaning of their saying: 'What is known by custom is like what is stipulated by condition,' and their saying: 'Specification by custom is like specification by text.'
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the definition and authority (hujjiyyah) of custom ('urf) in Hanafi jurisprudence. The author begins by citing a hadith (though noted as mawquf by some) that whatever Muslims deem good is good with Allah, establishing a foundational principle that communal consensus on goodness is authoritative. He then clarifies that custom is relied upon in many legal issues, even used to support technical terminology. The proof is drawn from numerous Quranic verses (nineteen in total) that command acting 'with ma'ruf' (good custom) in matters like divorce, maintenance, dower, and others, indicating that Shari'ah delegates details to customary practice. The hadith of Hind is also cited, where the Prophet did not fix a specific amount for maintenance but left it to custom. Footnotes provide scholarly verification of the hadith's authenticity (narrated by Ahmad, al-Bazzar, etc., though some consider it mawquf). The author then enumerates four principles (usul arba'ah) underlying the use of custom: (1) determining word meanings by custom, as speakers follow their customs; (2) interpreting contracts according to custom; (3) recognizing that rulings change with time when based on custom; (4) allowing fatwa according to people's custom when there is necessity and hardship would arise from forcing them to abandon it. The text then presents a key legal maxim: 'The literal meaning is abandoned due to usage and custom' (tutraku al-haqiqah bi dalalat al-istimal wa al-'adah). This is a methodological rule in ifta'. It is conditioned on custom being continuous (mutaridah) or predominant (ghalibah). Application: in a sale where currency is ambiguous, the contract is referred to the prevalent currency. Another principle: 'What is established by custom is like what is established by text' (al-thabit bi al-'urf ka al-thabit bi al-nass). Footnotes clarify that usage (istimal) often refers to transferring a word from literal to metaphorical by shari'ah, while custom ('adah) does so by 'urf. Some equate them. The condition for considering custom is that it be widespread, known to all concerned. If it is shared (not predominant), it lacks clarity and cannot restrict. The final footnote explains that 'by text' (bi al-nass) means the explicit stipulation of the speaker, thus 'known by custom is like stipulated by condition.'

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): ما تعارف عليه الناس واستقر في عاداتهم من قول أو فعل
العادة (al-'adah): مرادف للعرف أو ما يتكرر من الأفعال
الاستعمال (al-istimal): نقل اللفظ عن معناه الأصلي إلى معناه مجازي شرعاً أو غالباً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for custom ('urf) to be considered legally valid?
A) It must be recorded in writing by scholars.
B) It must be continuous (mutarid) or predominant (ghalib).
C) It must be approved by a living mujtahid.
D) It must be explicitly mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Custom (‘urf) is a legally valid source in Hanafi fiqh when it is predominant or continuous, and it can specify general texts and determine the interpretation of absolute expressions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Authority of Custom ('Urf) in Hanafi Iftaa
Defining custom and its legal authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that custom is equivalent to text by identifying when a custom is valid (continuous or predominant) and using it to derive rulings.

Core Idea
Custom is equivalent to explicit textual stipulation—if widespread, it governs absolute expressions.

Custom ('urf) is a fundamental source in Hanafi fiqh, especially in transactions. This lesson unpacks its definition, conditions, and authority, showing how the mufti uses customary practice to interpret ambiguous terms and issue rulings that align with people's needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Recognize the rule that literal meaning is abandoned for customary usage: 'tutrak al-haqiqah bi dalalat al-isti'mal wa al-'adah'.
This is the starting point for invoking custom.
2
State the condition
Custom must be 'continuous or predominant' (مطردة أو غالبة); widespread enough that everyone knows it or at least it is the prevailing practice.
A custom that is disputed or rare cannot override the literal meaning.
3
Apply the maxim
Recall the maxim: 'al-thabit bil 'urf kathabit bil nass' (what is established by custom is like what is established by text). This gives custom binding force in interpretation and ruling.
The maxim is equivalent to saying custom acts as a tacit condition.
4
Recognize exceptions
Custom cannot override a clear textual ruling (nass). It only operates in areas where the text is silent or ambiguous.
This is a critical limit on the authority of custom.
5
Practice with an example
Apply the principle to the dirham/dinar case: when a sale mentions currency without specifying, refer to the predominant local currency.
This shows how custom resolves ambiguity in contracts.

(۳)
الرابع : تعارف أهل البلد بما فيه ضرورة شديدة وحاجة عامة، فإنه يفتى بما هو أرفق للناس إذا ظهر عليه التعامل ولزم الحرج بنزع الناس عن عادتهم .
(۱) قوله : "بدلالة الاستعمال والعادة " [أى إذا كانت الحقيقة مهجورة ] اختلف في عطف العادة على الاستعمال ، فقيل : هما مترادفان . وقيل : المراد من الاستعمال : نقل اللفظ عن موضوعه الأصلى إلى معناه المجازى شرعًا، وغلبة استعماله فيه ومن العادة : نقله إلى معناه المجازى عرفا. (مظ) وقيل : الاستعمال يرجع إلى اللفظ والعادة إلى الفعل .
(۲) قوله : "إذا اطردت أو غلبت " أى إذا عمّت وشاعت بحيث يعرفها كل أحد ممن هو من أهلها، وإن لم تكن شائعة مستفيضة فلا أقل من أن تكون غالبة . قال الشارح في نشر العرف" : اعلم أن كلا من العرف العام والخاص إنما يعتبر إذا كان شائعا مستفيضا بين أهله يعرفه جميعهم، أما لو كان مشتركاً لا يصح الرجوع إليه ؛ للتردّد ، ولا يبنى الحكم عليه ؛ لأنه لما كان مشتركًا صار متعارضاً فلا يصلح مقيداً . انتهى ملخصاً. (١٣٤/٢)
(۳) قوله : " بالنص" الألف واللام عوض عن المضاف إليه، أي بنص المتكلم، كأنه اشترطه صريحًا، وهذا معنى قولهم : المعروف عرفًا كالمشروط شرطاً ، وقولهم : التعيين بالعرف كالتعيين بالنص".
Definition of custom and statement of its authority. --(1). Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: They made that a principle and said: 'The literal meaning is abandoned due to indication of usage and custom.' Then in al-Ashbah: 'Custom is only considered if it is continuous or predominant (2). Hence they said in sale: if one sells for dirhams or dinars in a country where coins differ in value and circulation, the sale is referred to the predominant (coin).' He said in al-Hidayah: 'Because it is the customary, so the absolute is directed to it.' And in Sharh al-Bayri from al-Mabsut: 'What is established by custom is like what is established by text.' End. (3) Fourth: The custom of the people of a town that involves severe necessity and general need, then one gives fatwa with what is more convenient for the people if dealing appears upon it and hardship would follow from removing them from their custom. (1) His saying: 'by indication of usage and custom' [i.e., when the literal meaning is abandoned]. There is disagreement about the conjunction of custom to usage. Some say they are synonymous. Some say by 'usage' is meant the transfer of the word from its original meaning to its metaphorical meaning legally and its prevalent usage in that, and by 'custom' is meant its transfer to its metaphorical meaning conventionally. (Mazhari) And some say usage relates to words and custom to actions. (2) His saying: 'if it is continuous or predominant' i.e., if it is general and widespread such that everyone among its people knows it; if it is not widespread and prevalent, then at least it should be predominant. The commentator said in Nashr al-Urf: 'Know that both general and specific custom are only considered if they are widespread and prevalent among its people, known by all of them. But if it is disputed (mushtarak), it is not valid to refer to it due to hesitation, and the ruling is not built upon it because since it is disputed, it becomes conflicting and thus not suitable as a restrictor.' End, summarized. (2/134) (3) His saying: 'by text' – the alif and lam substitute for the added (mudaf ilayh), i.e., by the text of the speaker, as if he explicitly stipulated it. This is the meaning of their saying: 'What is known by custom is like what is stipulated by condition' and their saying: 'Specification by custom is like specification by text.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning the authority of custom ('urf) in Hanafi fiqh. It opens with the principle that the literal meaning of a word is abandoned when there is a customary usage that indicates a different meaning, as established by the school. The text then clarifies that custom is only considered if it is continuous or at least predominant. An example illustrates this: if a sale mentions dirhams without specifying the type, it is interpreted according to the predominant currency in that locality. The passage further states that what is established by custom is equivalent to what is established by an explicit textual stipulation—a major Hanafi maxim. Finally, it adds a fourth point: in cases of severe necessity or general need, a mufti may issue a fatwa that is more convenient for the people if the custom has become prevalent and abandoning it would cause hardship. The footnotes expand on these points: the relationship between 'usage' and 'custom', the condition that custom must be widespread or at least predominant, and the explanation that 'bin-nass' means as if the speaker had explicitly said it. This passage is foundational for understanding how custom operates as a source of law in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): A practice or usage that is prevalent among people, either in speech or action, and is a recognized source of law under conditions.
العادة (al-'adah): Custom, often used synonymously with 'urf in this text; refers to repeated practice.
الحقيقة (al-haqiqah): The original literal meaning of a word, which is abandoned when custom indicates a different meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must custom satisfy to be considered a valid basis for a ruling?
A) It must be explicitly mentioned in the contract.
B) It must be widespread (continuous) or at least predominant.
C) It must be approved by all contemporary scholars.
D) It must be based on a prophetic hadith.

Key Takeaway
Custom is a binding source in Hanafi fiqh, but only when it is widespread or predominant and does not contradict explicit legal texts.
